TERMINOLOGIES Niyyah: Niyyah is the intention in oneʼs heart to knowingly do an action for the sole sake of Allāh .

 Farḍ (pl. Farāʼiḍ): A duty commanded by Allāh and definitively established in the Qurʼān and/or Sunnah. Within an action, Farḍ refers to something which must be done, and leaving it out renders the act void.

Wājib (pl. Wājibāt): A duty commanded by Allāh and established in the Qurʼān and/or Sunnah. Within an action, Wājib refers to something which must be done, and leaving it out renders the act incomplete.

Sunnah (pl. Sunan)ﷺﷺ: The way of the Prophet , and it includes anything that the Messenger did, said, or approved.

Mustaḥab (pl. Mustaḥabbāt): An act that is good to do and is beloved in Islām. A person receives reward for carrying out a Mustaḥab act.

Nafl (pl. Nawāfil): An optional good act. It brings reward if done, but there is no punishment for leaving it out.

Mubāḥ: An act which has no legal ruling and is therefore permitted. A person will not receive punishment or reward for doing it.

Makrūh (pl. Makrūhāt): Something that is disliked.

Makrūh Tanzīhī: An act which is disliked, but not sinful.

Makrūh Taḥrīmī: An act which is impermissible and sinful.

Ḥarām: An act that is forbidden. It is clearly proven from the Qurʼān and/or Ḥadīth.

Nāqiḍ (pl. Nawāqiḍ): Nullifier. THE FIVE PILLARS OF ISLĀM SHAHĀDAHṢALĀHZAKĀHṢAWMḤAJJ

Ṭahārah

HYGIENE Hygiene is an essential part of a Muslimʼs life. As Muslims, we are encouraged to be spiritually and physically pure at all times, and required to be ritually pure for many of our obligatory acts. Therefore, it is for this reason that a Muslim keeps good personal hygiene habits, and is mindful of coming into contact with any impurity.

NAJĀSAH (IMPURITY)

Najāsah is of two types:

Najāsah Ḥaqīqī: physical impurity. This is of two types:1. a.Najāsah Ghalīẓah (heavy impurity): the greater impurities such as blood, urine, semen, stool, etc. b.Najāsah Khafīfah (light impurity): the lighter impurity such as the urine of ḥalāl animals It is preferable to remove any impurity from the body or clothes, and a requirement to remove it before performing Ṣalāh. However, in the case of Najāsah Ghalīẓah, an amount the size of a dirham (2.75cm in diameter or roughly the diameter of a large coin denomination) is excused. For Najāsah Khafīfah on the other hand, an amount covering less than one-fourth of a limb or corresponding piece of clothing will be excused.

Najāsah Ḥukmī: state of impurity. This also is divided into two types:2. a.Ḥadath al-Akbar: when a person requires Ghusl (ritual bathing) b.Ḥadath al-Aṣghar: when a person requires Wuḍūʼ (ablution)

ISTINJĀʼ When a person uses the toilet, they should recite the Duʻāʼ prior to entering the bathroom with their • left foot.

One should not urinate standing or at a urinal in view of others, nor should their front or back face the • direction of the Qiblah. The left hand should be used for Istinjāʼ (cleaning oneself) and Istibrāʼ (removing excess urine drops). • Both water and tissue should be used to clean oneself, though in the absence or unavailability of one, • the other may suffice. A Muslim should endeavour to remain clean, and therefore ought to ensure that no urine or faeces • remain on themselves, their clothes, the toilet bowl, or seat after they relieve themselves. If there is, one should clean it. Thereafter, one should wash their hands and recite the Duʻāʼ after leaving the bathroom with the right foot.

ISTIBRĀʼ Istibrāʼ refers to removing excess urine drops after urinating. The Prophet ﷺ warned of being negligent in cleaning urine drops, and Istibrāʼ is a crucial process in making sure one’s body and clothes are clean so that Salāh and other acts of worship are valid.

Istibrāʼ may be performed using one or more of the following methods:

Whilst holding tissue at the head of the male organ, apply pressure from the bottom to the top and • squeeze the head to remove excess urine onto the tissue.

Cough to apply pressure that might force excess urine out.• Whilst holding tissue at the head of the male organ, one may move around a little to force the urine • out. If it takes longer, one may wrap tissue around the male organ and leave the toilet, walk around, • and return a few minutes later to remove the tissue and wash oneself. After applying methods of Istibrāʼ, one should sprinkle some water on their male organ and the • area surrounding it to remove doubts which may occur from feeling wetness later.

FARḌ ACTS OF WUḌŪʼ Washing of the face from the forehead to the chin, and from one earlobe to the other.1.

Washing of both arms including the elbows.2.

Performing Masaḥ (wiping of wet hands) on a quarter of the head.3.

Washing of both feet including the ankles.4.

SOME SUNAN OF WUḌŪʼ Niyyah.1.

Reciting the Duʻās taught by the Messenger Muḥammad ﷺ.2.

Washing both hands including the wrist.3.

Brush the teeth using the Miswāk.4.

Rinsing the mouth.5.

Rinsing the nose.6.

Performing Khilāl (running wet fingers through) of the beard.7.

Performing Khilāl of the fingers and toes.8.

Doing Masaḥ of the whole head once.9.

Doing Masaḥ of both ears once.10.

Performing each step three times except Masaḥ.11.

Performing the Wuḍūʼ in the correct order.12.

Washing each part before the previous part dries.13.

TAYAMMUM Tayammum refers to dry ablution that is performed in place of Wuḍūʼ. It can be done in the following situations: If there is no water for an approximate one-mile radius.• If one has an illness which will intensify from using water.• If warm water is unavailable, and extreme cold weather prevents one from performing Ghusl.• If water is nearby but one cannot reach it due to fear.• If water is available but only enough for drinking.• Tayammum can be done with soil, stone, brick, sand, limestone and dust. The method for performing Tayammum:

One must make intention to purify oneself.1.

Strike both hands on the medium (thing you are doing Tayammum on) once, before rubbing the 2. entire face.

Strike both hands on the medium once more, and rub both arms fully including the elbows.3.

MASAḤ ʻALA AL-KHUFFAYN Khuffayn are a certain type of socks upon which one can do Masaḥ (wipe wet hands over) on rather than wash the feet during Wuḍūʼ. Khuffayn are made of leather, but one may perform Masaḥ over any other socks with durable thick material that meets certain conditions. It is Farḍ to make Masaḥ equal to the area of three fingers on each sock. In order to do Masaḥ on the socks, the following conditions must be met: The socks must be worn after washing the feet in Wuḍūʼ before Wuḍūʼ is broken again.1. The socks must cover the feet including the ankles.2. If the socks are not made of leather, they should be durable enough to withstand three miles of 3. walking without tearing.

Each sock must be free from tears that equal the size of three of the smallest toe.4. The sock should be thick enough that water does not easily seep through when Masaḥ is 5. performed. The socks should remain in position (covering the foreleg) without being tied.6. The Masaḥ on socks will remain valid for 24 hours for a Muqīm, and 72 hours for a Musāfir. This will begin from the first breaking of Wuḍūʼ following the wearing of the socks. Masaḥ will be invalidated following the expiry time, and if the person is in the state of Wuḍūʼ, they will be required to remove their socks and wash their feet if they wish for their Wuḍūʼ to remain valid. The same applies for one who removes their socks after having done Masaḥ on them; the Masaḥ is invalidated but the Wuḍūʼ will remain by washing the feet (See Ṣalāh al-Musāfir).

NAWĀQIḌ (BREAKERS) OF WUḌŪʼ Sleeping in a manner that relaxes the gluteal muscles.Laughing aloud whilst in Ṣalāh.1.5.

Any discharge of Najāsah (impurity) from the private Vomiting a mouthful.2.6. parts (e.g. urine, stool, blood).Loss of consciousness; fainting.7.

Passing wind.Becoming insane.3.8.

Flowing blood or pus (if one bleeds from the mouth, Being intoxicated (including 4.9. then the amount must be more than the saliva it is consuming drugs which intoxicate). mixed with).

IMPORTANT POINTS If a person who has made Tayammum sees water, their Wuḍūʼ is invalidated. Likewise, if a person 1. performs Tayammum due to an illness that prevents using water, their Tayammum is invalidated upon their recovery and ability to use water once more.

ʻWhen the time for prayer ends, the Wuḍūʼ of an excused person (Madhūr) is invalidated.

BULŪGH (PUBERTY) When a person grows from childhood to adolescence, certain changes begin to appear on the body for both males and females. Puberty brings about hair growth around the private parts as well as under the armpits and the development of certain body parts. To ensure good hygiene practice, one is expected to remove such hair after a certain period of growth. It is sinful to let the hair grow unattended for more than 40 days. When a person becomes Bāligh, they are considered accountable for obligatory commandments.

PUBERTY FOR MALES A boy is considered to have reached puberty upon having his first wet dream or ejaculation, or upon reaching 15 lunar years (14 years and 7 months). For a man, there are certain types of liquids that are released by the male private organ. They are:

Urine.1.

Manī (semen): a thick white liquid released from the male organ at climax; a yellow liquid for 2. women released at climax.

Madhī (prostatic fluid): a thin white sticky fluid released as a result of sexual arousal, but its 3. release does not cause a listlessness of the private part.

Wadī: a thick white fluid that comes out after or before urination.4. Of the above, all will break Wuḍūʼ but only the release of Manī necessitates Ghusl.

PUBERTY FOR FEMALES For a woman, maturity begins at the release of blood from the vagina or upon reaching 15 lunar years (14 years and 7 months).

Women have three types of bleeding:

Ḥayḍ (period or menstruation).1.

Istiḥāḍah (dysfunctional uterine bleeding or bleeding due to an illness).2.

Nifās (lochia or post-natal bleeding).3.

WHAT NECESSITATES GHUSLPROHIBITIONS DURING MAJOR IMPURITY There are five actions which are impermissible Sexual Intercourse (insertion of 1. when in the state of Ḥadath al-Akbar (where one is the head of the male organ into the required to perform Ghusl):female organ necessitates Ghusl for both spouses) To perform Ṣalāh.1.

Release of Manī (semen) for males 2. To enter or remain in the Masjid.2. and females To recite the Qurʼān.3.

Wet dream3. To touch the Qurʼān.4.

End of Ḥayḍ4. To perform Ṭawāf of the Kaʻbah.End of Nifās5.5.

FARḌ ACTS OF GHUSL (RITUAL BATHING)

Rinsing the mouth fully (gargling).1.

Rinsing the nose.2.

Pouring water over the whole body, ensuring nothing remains dry.3.

SOME SUNAN OF GHUSL Making intention to clean oneself.1.

Washing both hands first up to the wrist.2.

Washing off any dirt and cleaning the private parts.3.

Performing Wuḍūʼ except for washing the feet if water has gathered around the feet.4.

Pouring water over the head, then the right shoulder, and then the left shoulder three times, 5. ensuring no part of the body is left dry.

Washing the feet three times at the end if water had gathered.6.

Using as little water as possible.7.

ḤAYḌ Ḥayḍ can only begin after a girl turns nine in lunar years (8 years and 9 months). Any blood prior to this is considered Istiḥāḍah. The onset of Ḥayḍ marks maturity for a woman, and she will be classed as an adult thereafter. If a woman has not experienced Ḥayḍ at 15 (lunar) years, she will still be considered mature.

Minimum period of Ḥayḍ: three days and three nights (72 hours).

Maximum period of Ḥayḍ: ten days and ten nights (240 hours). The blood of Ḥayḍ may flow in different colours, such as red, yellow, green or brown.

All will be considered as Ḥayḍ.

NIFĀS Nifās is the release of blood after childbirth. Nifās may continue for 40 days, and there is no minimum amount.

ISTIḤĀḌAH Istiḥāḍah is abnormal vaginal bleeding occurring beside the times of Ḥayḍ or Nifās. A woman who experiences Istiḥāḍah is not exempt from Ṣalāh or fasting, nor prohibited from what a woman in Ḥayḍ is prohibited from.

Any bleeding which is:

Less than three days (72 hours)• More than 10 days (240 hours)• Within the 15 days of purity following a Ḥayḍ• is considered to be Istiḥāḍah. If the flow of Istiḥāḍah is constant over a full Ṣalāh time, and occurs even once over subsequent Ṣalāh times, the woman will be classed as Maʻdhūr. The woman with Istiḥāḍah will clean herself, wear a clean pad and perform Wuḍūʼ for every Ṣalāh time, which will then last until that Ṣalāh time ends. During this time, she may perform any act of worship usually requiring Wuḍūʼ. Her Wuḍūʼ will break automatically at the end of the Ṣalāh time. She will continue like this until she ceases to be Maʻdhūr. If a woman however does not experience a constant flow of Istiḥāḍah, but rather experiences irregular blood flow, her Wuḍūʼ will break whenever her blood flows. PROHIBITIONS DURING ḤAYḌ AND NIFĀS Performing Ṣalāh. There will not be Qaḍāʼ of Ṣalāh missed in Ḥayḍ.1.

Fasting. One will be required to make up missed fasts.2.

Touching the Qurʼān.3.

Reading the Qurʼān (Duʻāʼs from the Qurʼān are allowed if recited with the intention of Duʻāʼ).4.

Entering the Masjid.5.

Ṭawāf of the Kaʻbah.6.

Intercourse.7.

ACTS OF WORSHIP PERMISSIBLE DURING ḤAYḌ AND NIFĀS While certain acts of worship are impermissible during Ḥayḍ, one should not see Ḥayḍ as a ‘break’ from spirituality, but rather as an opportunity to engage in alternate forms of worship. One may develop and further build their relationship with Allāh  through the following:

Listen to, and reflect on the meaning of the Qurʼān.• Performing Duʻāʼ and various types of Adhkār.• Seek knowledge through reading and listening.• Helping others who are engaged in worship.• Reflect on the Names of Allāh , His Attributes, and His signs within His creation.• Planning and starting new habits of good deeds.• ṬUHR (PURITY)

Following Ḥayḍ, there is a period of time before the next Ḥayḍ begins which is called a Ṭuhr (period of purity). The minimum number of days between two Ḥayḍ is 15 days (360 hours). Any bleeding before the completion of 15 days following Ḥayḍ will be considered Istiḥāḍah. There is no maximum number of days for Ṭuhr, and it may extend by days, months or even years. A woman must keep a track of her Ṭuhr by noting the time and date her Ḥayḍ ends. Likewise, a record should be kept of the start time and date of Ḥayḍ, so that one may calculate their menstrual cycle effectively. This is useful in the case of Istiḥāḍah, or any changes in the menstrual cycle. One may use a smartphone application to effectively track their menstrual cycle. THE CYCLE LENGTH OF ḤAYḌ A cycle length (ʻĀdah), sometimes referred to as a womanʼs habit, is the usual number of days a womanʼs menstruation and Ṭuhr lasts. Any time the number of days for Ḥayḍ and Ṭuhr change, it will be the new cycle length. For example, a woman has consistently had six days of Ḥayḍ. If in the following month she has Ḥayḍ for eight days, this will now be her new cycle length, and will be considered as such for the coming month. The same will apply if the days of Ḥayḍ reduce. If a woman has an irregular cycle length and her period days fluctuate every month, then her cycle length will be based on her most recent Ḥayḍ.

WHY IS THE CYCLE LENGTH IMPORTANT?

Keeping a track of oneʼs Ḥayḍ and Ṭuhr is useful in determining between Ḥayḍ and Istiḥāḍah if it occurs. For example, a woman has a cycle length of six days, which changes the following month. The change will be either: A change in her cycle length but under ten days: For example, she bleeds for eight days the 1. following month, in which case all eight days will be considered Ḥayḍ and the following month her cycle length will be eight days. If they however exceed 10 days, then the normal cycle length will be considered Ḥayḍ and the remaining days Istiḥāḍah. For the days of Istiḥāḍah, Qaḍāʼ must be performed of missed Ṣalāh and fasts.

ḤAYḌ TIPS Whilst one is unable to perform certain acts of worship, an effort should be made to perform other acts • instead. Dhikr (remembrance of Allāh ), Duʻāʼ, and other optional acts of worship are allowed, and one should utilise their time to still strengthen their connection with Allāh .

During and prior the period, one may experience pain. Period cramps may differ from person to person • and should be managed accordingly. Pain-relief medication may be used, as well as heat therapy through hot compresses, warm baths, or heating pads to provide relief.

Good hygiene is crucially important for a woman during Ḥayḍ, not only from the Islamic perspective, • but also for her health. Using correct sanitary pads to manage menstrual flow, changing out sanitary products, and washing oneself at timely intervals prevents the growth of bacteria which may lead to discomfort and infection.

One may wear comfortable clothing that ensure correct hygiene whilst bearing Islamic principles in • mind.

Maintaining a healthy diet is important for wellbeing during Ḥayḍ and recovery after. One should include • foods rich in iron to replenish blood loss during a period. Likewise, keeping oneself hydrated with water and water-rich foods is also beneficial.

DISCHARGE Discharge is of three types:

Fluid from the Farj al-Khārij (vulva - external region of the vagina).1.

Fluid from the Farj ad-Dākhil (vagina).2.

Fluid from anywhere beyond the Farj ad-Dākhil (beyond the vagina).3. The first two do not nullify Wuḍūʼ, and the fluids are pure. The third is impure and nullifies Wuḍūʼ. If a woman is certain that fluidal discharge is from the vagina, then her Wuḍūʼ will remain, provided the discharge is clear and white, and has not mixed with blood or arousal discharge.

If, however, a woman is unsure or unaware of the origin of her discharge, which is often the case, then she must renew her Wuḍūʼ and purify her body or clothes from any such discharge. Wearing pads or something similar may prove helpful in maintaining hygiene and purity.

SUNAN AL-FIṬRAH There are ten practices which form a part of the Sunnah of all the Prophets. They are:

Shaving the pubic hair7.Using the Miswāk (brushing oneʼs teeth)

Using water to clean oneʼs private parts after 8.Rinsing the mouth 2. relieving oneselfRinsing the nose 3.

Clipping the moustache (for males)9.Washing the joints 4.

Lengthening the beard (for males)10.Clipping the nails 5.

Plucking the hair under the armpit6.

MUSLIM

Ṣalāh

TIMINGS OF ṢALĀH Fajr begins at Ṣubḥ Ṣādiq (true dawn). It ends • when the sun begins to rise.

Ẓuhr begins when the sun moves from the highest • position at noon, which is also called Zawāl. It ends when the shadow of an object becomes twice its length. This is called Mithlayn.

ʻAṣr starts at Mithlayn and ends at sunset.• Maghrib begins at sunset following the complete • setting of the sun. It ends at the total darkening of the sky, after the red and white twilight disappear.

ʻIshāʼ begins after twilight has disappeared. It • ends at Ṣubḥ Ṣādiq.

IMPERMISSIBLE PRAYER TIMES There are three times during the day when it is impermissible to perform any Ṣalāh:

Whilst the sun is rising.1.

Whilst the sun is at its highest point during the day. This is a few minutes before Ẓuhr time.2.

Whilst the sun is setting. One may only perform the ʻAṣr prayer of that day during that time if they 3. have not yet done so.

DISLIKED PRAYER TIMES There are three times during the day when it is Makrūh to perform Nafl prayers:

Following the commencement of Fajr time, one should only perform the Sunnah of Fajr.1. After the Farḍ of Fajr, one should not perform any Nafl until after the sun has fully risen.2. After one has performed their ʻAṣr prayer, no Nafl prayer should be performed. 3.

Qaḍāʼ, Janāzah Ṣalāh and Sajdah Tilāwah may be performed in these Makrūh times of Ṣalāh.

SUNNAH TOTAL SUNNAH SUNNAH GHAYR FARḌNAFLWITRNAFL MUʼAKKADAHRAKʻĀTMUʼAKKADAH MUʼAKKADAH FAJR2----2- ẒUHR2--442- ʻAṢR--4-4-- MAGHRIB-322--- ʻISHĀʼ-422324 JUMUʻAH24 + 22---4 TARĀWĪḤ-20---20-- CONDITIONS BEFORE ṢALĀH Ensuring the body and clothes are clean.1.

Covering the ʻAwrah.2.

Performing Wuḍūʼ and Ghusl if necessary.3. Being in a clean place for Ṣalāh.4.

Facing the Qiblah.5.

Praying in the correct time.6.

Making the correct Niyyah (intention).7.

CONDITIONS OF ṢALĀH The conditions of Ṣalāh are the pillars of the Ṣalāh. If any of these are missed out, the Ṣalāh will be invalid.

Takbīr Taḥrīmah: The first Takbir (saying Allāhu Akbar) when starting Ṣalāh.1.

Qiyām: The standing position in Ṣalāh.2.

Qirāʼah: Reciting the Qurʼān.3.

Rukūʻ: Bowing down.4.

Sajdah: Prostration on the ground.5.

Qaʻdah Akhīrah: The last sitting before Salām. This must be at least for the duration of reciting 6.

Tashahhud.

WĀJIBĀT OF ṢALĀH Wājib actions of Ṣalāh are actions which if omitted intentionally will render the Ṣalāh invalid. If however, they are omitted accidentally and one remembers during Ṣalāh, they must perform Sajdah as-Sahw to make up for what they omitted, and their Ṣalāh will be complete. To perform every action in order.1. To perform every action calmly.2. To recite Sūrah al-Fātiḥah.3. To recite Sūrah al-Fātiḥah before any Sūrah.4. To recite a Sūrah or at least one long Āyah or three short Āyāt in the first two Rak‘āt of Farḍ Ṣalāh.5. To recite a Sūrah or at least one long Āyah or three short Āyāt in all Rakʻāt of Wājib, Sunnah and 6.

Nafl Ṣalāh. For the Imām: to recite aloud in Fajr, Jumuʻah, Tarāwīḥ, Witr in Ramaḍān, ʻĪd Ṣalāh, and the first 7. two Rakʻāt of Maghrib and ʻIshāʼ; to recite quietly in Ẓuhr, ʻAṣr, the last Rakʻah of Maghrib and the last two Rakʻāt of ʻIshāʼ Ṣalāh. To stand in Qawmah (the position after Rukūʻ).8. To sit in Jalsah (the position between two Sajdahs).9. To recite Tashahhud in the two Qaʻdahs (sittings).10. To sit in Qaʻdah Ūlā (the first sitting, after two Rakʻāt in a three or four Rakʻāt Ṣalāh).11. To end the Ṣalāh with Salām.12.

SAJDAH AS-SAHW If one accidentally misses a Wājib action, or delays a Rukn (position), then they will be required to perform Sajdah as-Sahw to make up for the mistake before the end of the Ṣalāh. Sajdah as-Sahw is extra Sajdahs performed in the last Qaʻdah. The method to perform it follows below: In the last Qaʻdah (sitting), after reciting Tashahhud, make one Salām to the right.1.

Thereafter, perform two Sajdahs reciting the Tasbīh of Sajdah.2. After the two Sajdahs, complete the Ṣalāh as usual (by reciting Tashahhud, Durūd and Du’ā’, and 3. ending with Salām).

NAWĀQIḌ OF ṢALĀH To eat or drink.1. To make any type of unnecessary noise.2. To do ʻAmal Kathīr: an action which if people were to see would think that the person is not in Ṣalāh; 3. or excessive movement. To talk or laugh aloud in Ṣalāh.4. To not let the feet touch the ground even once, throughout the entire Sajdah.5.

Opening of a quarter of any limb of the ʻAwrah for the duration of one Rukn (the length of time it 6. takes to recite Subḥānallāh three times). To turn the chest away from the Qiblah.7.

Making an error in the recitation of the Qurʼān which produces a grave change in meaning.8. To step ahead of the Imām in Ṣalāh as a Muqtadī (follower in a congregational prayer).9.

Anything that invalidates Wuḍūʼ.10.

MASBŪQ One who arrives to a congregational prayer late (after the Rukūʻ of the first Rakʻah) is called a Masbūq. The following table details how they should complete the missed Rakʻah/Rakʻāt of their Ṣalāh.

RAKʻAH RAKʻAH WITH HOW MISSEDIMĀM Stand up after the Imām has made Salām.

Recite:

  • Duʻāʼ al-Istiftāḥ, Taʻawwudh & Tasmiyah
  • Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and a Sūrah

Complete the rest of the Rakʻah. After the Sajdah, sit & recite Tashahhud, Durūd & Duʻāʼ.

Stand up after the Imām has made Salām.

Recite:

  • Duʻāʼ al-Istiftāḥ, Taʻawwudh & Tasmiyah
  • Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and a Sūrah

Stand up for the last Rakʻah after Sajdah.

Recite:

  • Tasmiyah, Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and a Sūrah

Sit after Sajdah & complete Ṣalāh as normal.

Stand up after the Imām has made Salām.

Recite:

  • Duʻāʼ al-Istiftāḥ, Taʻawwudh & Tasmiyah
  • Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and a Sūrah

Sit down after Sajdah & recite Tashahhud only, then stand up for the next Rakʻah Recite:

  • Tasmiyah, Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and a Sūrah

Do not sit down after the Sajdah but stand straight up for the last Rakʻah Recite:

  • Tasmiyah and Sūrah al-Fātiḥah

After the Sajdah sit and complete Ṣalāh as normal.

Stand up after the Imām has made Salām and pray as you are praying a normal four Rakʻah Ṣalāh.

WHAT TO DO IF YOU ARE MASBŪQ FOR MAGHRIB ṢALĀH?

RAKʻAH RAKʻAH WITH HOW MISSEDIMĀM Stand up after the Imām has made Salām.

Recite:

  • Duʻāʼ al-Istiftāḥ, Taʻawwudh & Tasmiyah
  • Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and a Sūrah

Complete the rest of the Rakʻah. After the Sajdah, sit & recite Tashahhud, Durūd & Duʻāʼ.

Stand up after the Imām has made Salām.

Recite:

  • Duʻāʼ al-Istiftāḥ, Taʻawwudh & Tasmiyah
  • Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and a Sūrah

Sit down after Sajdah & recite Tashahhud only, then stand up for the next Rakʻah

  • Tasmiyah, Sūrah al-Fātiḥah and a Sūrah

Sit after Sajdah & complete Ṣalāh as normal.

Stand up after the Imām has made Salām and pray as you are praying a normal three Rakʻah Ṣalāh. IN PROGRESS QAḌĀʼ ṢALĀH Completing a Ṣalāh which has been missed is called Qaḍāʼ. One should make every effort to never miss a Ṣalāh, but if it is missed, then one should make it up as soon as possible. Qaḍāʼ is done for Farḍ and Witr Ṣalāh. It should also be done for the Sunnah of Fajr until Zawāl of the same day. One may complete Qaḍāʼ

SAJDAH AT-TILĀWAH If a verse of Sajdah is recited either in or out of Ṣalāh, then one must perform Sajdah. If one is in Ṣalāh, they may simply go straight into Sajdah after the verse has been recited saying the Takbīr, recite the Tasbīh of Sajdah as usual, and then stand and continue with their recitation. If the verse is recited outside of Ṣalāh however, the procedure is as follows:

One should have the intention of performing Sajdah at-Tilāwah.1. From a standing or sitting position, recite the Takbīr and go into Sajdah without raising the hands.2.

Perform a single Sajdah with Tasbīh as usual.3.

Recite the Takbīr and raise the head from Sajdah. There is no Salām.4.

AL-MARĪḌ If a person cannot stand for Ṣalāh, they should sit on the ground and perform Ṣalāh with Rukūʻ and • Sujūd. However, if they can stand for a short while, they should do so, even if they have to use a support to lean. If the person cannot perform Rukūʻ and Sujūd too, then they will perform them using gestures with • the head. If a person cannot sit and perform Ṣalāh, they may perform it lying on their back with gestures.• If a person cannot perform Sajdah but can stand, they should stand for Qiyām and perform Rukūʻ as • normal, and perform Sajdah with gestures whilst sitting on the ground. If a person cannot gesture with their head due to extreme illness or unconsciousness for six prayers or • more, they will not have to make up the Ṣalāh missed.

Standing in Ṣalāh is obligatory in Farḍ and Wājib Salāh, and a person may not offer it seated without a valid excuse. If one however is unable to stand and perform Salāh, then they should sit on the ground and perform Ṣalāh without using a chair. Sitting on a chair should only be a last resort when sitting on the ground is too difficult.

AL-MAʻDHŪR If a person suffers an illness whereby from the entry time of a Farḍ Ṣalāh until its expiry they cannot • keep their Wuḍūʼ for long enough to perform Wuḍūʼ and Ṣalāh without breaking their Wuḍūʼ, they are considered Maʻdhūr.

Once a person is considered Maʻdhūr, the occurrence of their illness (e.g. flowing of blood) will not • break their Wuḍūʼ within a Ṣalāh time. They may perform any act of worship within that time. Their Wuḍūʼ will break with the ending of the Ṣalāh time. The occurrence of the illness (the reason the person is Maʻdhūr) will not break Wuḍūʼ, though any • other Nawāqiḍ will do so. For example, the Wuḍūʼ of one suffering from continuous bleeding will be broken by passing wind, even though the bleeding does not. For a person to continue being Maʻdhūr, the illness must occur at least once in every Ṣalāh time. •

ʻĪD ṢALĀH ʻĪd Ṣalāh is performed on the two days of celebration: ʻĪd al-Fiṭr and ʻĪd al-Aḍḥā. The ʻĪd Ṣalāh have six extra Takbīrāt (three in each Rakʻah) which are Wājib.

First Rakʻah After Takbīr Taḥrīmah and the Duʻāʼ al-Istiftāḥ, raise your hands with the Imām saying Takbīr and drop them to the side. Do this again, and finally raise your hands saying Takbīr, and fold them. The Ṣalāh will continue as normal with recitation of the Qurʼān.

Second Rakʻah After the Qirāʼah (recitation), raise your hands with the Imām saying Takbīr. Do this two more times, each time raising the hands saying Takbīr, and dropping the hands to the side. Finally, go into Rukūʻ saying Takbīr. The remainder of the Ṣalāh is as normal.

Khuṭbah In ʻĪd Ṣalāh, the Khuṭbah will follow the Ṣalāh.

TARĀWĪḤ ṢALĀH The Tarāwīḥ Ṣalāh is a Sunnah Muʼakkadah which has been established from the time of the Ṣaḥābah until now, and has the consensus of the scholars backing it. Tarāwīḥ Ṣalāh is 20 Rakʻāt performed in units of two after ʻIshāʼ Ṣalāh in Ramaḍān, before Witr.

IʻTIKĀF Iʻtikāf is the Sunnah of the Messenger ﷺ, and for men it involves voluntarily restricting oneself to the Masjid for worship. Women may perform Iʻtikāf in a designated portion of their home. The intention of Iʻtikāf can be Sunnah, and it will be performed in the final ten days of Ramaḍān. One may also make intention of Nafl Iʻtikāf every time they enter a Masjid. A man performing Sunnah Iʻtikāf must stay within the Masjid for the full duration of the ten days. A woman performing Sunnah Iʻtikāf must stay within a designated room of her home or a portion of a large room for the full duration of the ten days.

One cannot leave Iʻtikāf without a valid reason. If one does do so, their Sunnah Iʻtikāf will be broken and they will have to perform Qaḍāʼ of that day.

There are three types of valid excuses to leave during Iʻtikāf:

Sharʻī reason: For example, to perform Farḍ Ghusl, Ḥayḍ.1.

Natural reason: For example: to relieve oneself.2.

Necessity: For example, evacuating the Masjid due to a fire, preparing food.3.

Du'ā'

Duʻāʼ is our conversation with our Lord. It is an opportunity for us to express our Du āʼ innermost selves to our Creator, with full assurance that we will be heard. We ask Allāh  because He is the only one who can give. Allāh  is our Lord, and we are His obedient slaves. Duʻāʼ is an exhibition of our helplessness and humility in front of Allāh , and it illustrates our complete servitude to our Creator and Provider. We can make Duʻāʼ anywhere and at any time. We share a profound bond and connection with our Creator, and therefore we are not required to visit a special place, be in a certain condition, or forward our prayers through particular people to Allāh . Duʻāʼ is the ultimate blessing for a believer, an enduring association between the believer and the Lord of the Worlds.

When making Duʻāʼ, we should display our utter helplessness before Allāh .

Much like one drowning at sea will call out for help, our Duʻāʼ in the comfort of our homes should be similar in desperation. Our Duʻāʼ should show our dire need and our humility before the Creator of the Heavens and Earth, and we should make an effort to express our helplessness before Him.

ETIQUETTE OF MAKING DUʻĀʼ There are certain etiquettes to keep in mind before and whilst making Duʻāʼ:

1.Humbling oneself. This is done not only in the physical sense by raising oneʼs hands and expressing need, but also in the spiritual sense by considering the One we are asking from and appreciating His Grandeur.

2.Have firm belief that Allāh  will answer your Duʻāʼ.

3.Be persistent in your Duʻāʼ.

4.Do not lose hope or become impatient.

5.Use Duʻās from the Qurʼān and Sunnah.

6.Avoid sinning and consuming Ḥarām.

7.Make Duʻāʼ in times of ease as well as times of hardship.

8.Donʼt be shy to ask for something.

HOW TO MAKE DUʻĀʼ SUPPLICATIONS AND ADHKĀR 1.Start by praising Allāh .

Try to memorise all the Duʻāʼs with their 2.Send salutations on the Messenger Muḥammad ﷺ. meanings in this section.

3.Ask Allāh using His Beautiful Names.

4.Sincerely repent for your sins and ask Allāh  for Some Duʻāʼs will be for certain times, forgiveness.but many can be used in oneʼs daily 5.supplications too. Be completely humble in your Duʻāʼ.

I ask you for the good consequences of Your Decree. ūAḥmad, Ibn Mājah

The Islamic Calendar

Ṣaḥābah, various opinions on when the calendar should begin were offered, and eventually the decision was made to base the beginning of the Islamic calendar on the year of the Hijrah (migration). This was because the Hijrah was significant as a defining point for Islām: it marked the beginning of the rise of Islām, and marked the clear distinction between truth and falsehood. As for the first month of the year, since Hijrah occurred in Rabī‘ al-Awwal, it was considered for the first month. However, the Messenger of Allāh ﷺ made intention for migration in Muḥarram, and gave permission

to others to migrate from this month. ‘Umarرضي الله عنه therefore, with the Ṣaḥābah, decided that the first month

should be Muḥarram.

ﷺOn this date, the Messenger left Makkah for Madīnah, signalling the beginning of the Hijrah and a hugely important milestone for the Muslims.The Islamic months begin 01 - The Beginning of the Hijrahwith the sighting of the new moon, and each month ﷺThe Messenger arrived in Madīnah on this date. The religion of will be either 29 or 30 days Islām would firmly lay its roots in Madīnah, and the laws of Allāh long.

 would be established.

Allāh blessed humanity with the sending of His fast of this day with a fast on the final prophet, who brought His final message and book, day prior or after (9th or 11th of for all times, and all people.

Muḥarram). The most excellent fast after Ramaḍān is Allāh's month: al- Muḥarram

MUSLIM

Surely, the number of months according to Allāh is 12 (as written) in the Book of Allāh on the day He created the Heavens and the Earth, of which there are Four Sacred Months.

QUR’ĀN 9:36 Time has come back to its original state ūas it had been on the day when Allāh created the Heavens and the Earth. The year is 12 months, four of which are sacred. Three of them are in succession: Dhul Qa‘dah, Dhul Ḥijjah and Muḥarram; and (the fourth being) Rajab.

Attributes of Allāh

 The objective and purpose of every person is to recognise their Lord, the Creator of the Heavens and the Earth. This is the ultimate goal for every person. Furthermore, recognition of their Lord should bring about humility and subservience which commit a person to action. For this purpose, Allāh has left signs in His creation which indicate His existence, through which we can better appreciate His majesty and grandeur.

BUKHĀRĪ

It is through appreciating and comprehending who Allāh is through His Names that a person can elevate their worship and it is only through truly understanding who Allāh is that a person can develop Taqwā (God-conciousness) that stops him from evil, in its many forms and guises.

Allāh ʼs Beautiful Names are for our benefit: to delight our hearts and minds, moisten our tongues and beautify our prayers and supplications. As Allāh says in the Qurʼān, Allāh has the Most Beautiful Names. So call upon Him by them.

QURʼĀN 7:180

BRINGING THE NAMES OF ALLĀH  INTO OUR LIVES A person should strive to incorporate the Names of Allāh into their life. If Allāh is the embodiment of perfection, and His attributes are descriptors of perfection, then it is only natural that in our effort to attain Iḥsān (perfection) we turn to the One who is already perfect. Every name of Allāh is worthy of thought and contemplation, followed by action and practice in bringing it into our lives. We should spend some time reading and contemplating on them, so that we can bring these qualities, however imperfectly, into our own lives.

A-r A-r rAḥmānAndrAḥīm THE ALL-MERCIFUL, THE VERY MERCIFUL Allāh is the source of mercy. His mercy extends the breadth of His dominion and encompasses the extent of His creation. Nothing is beyond the realm of His mercy, and it is only by way of His grace that any being enjoys existence. Where it is mostly empathy that drives a person to compassion, a person may oftentimes be merciful for selfish aims or personal reasons, and if not, then least of all to relieve the guilt they feel of seeing another in distress. This, however, is not the case with Allāh . Allāh is not merciful for any selfish goals or gratitude, but rather His mercy is perfect, untainted by hidden intents. We can bring the quality of mercy into our lives through being kind and thoughtful: showing empathy and humanity in the spirit of wanting to be closer to Allāh through embodying His attributes. Mercy then should be a defining characteristic of the one who loves Allāh , for it is an attribute Allāh most often describes Himself with. Mercy ﷺdisqualifies injustice, it halts contempt, diffuses anger, and fosters calmness. The Messenger said, The merciful ones are shown mercy by The Merciful One. Be merciful to those on the Earth, ūand the One in the Heavens shall shower mercy upon you.

A-G A-G lhAfūrAndlhAffār THE ALL-FORGIVING AND THE ONE FULL OF FORGIVENESS Forgiveness in Arabic comes from the word for concealing because Allāh conceals our faults, giving us ample opportunity to ask for forgiveness and turn back to Him. He conceals the most depraved of our thoughts and intentions and does not take us to task for those things that we intend but do not carry out.

Moreover, He allows us dignity and honour, which none would have afforded us had our thoughts and actions been unconcealed. Then, when we turn back to Allāh , Allāh forgives unconditionally. His forgiveness encompasses all sins, for anyone of sincere repentance. Allāh says in a Ḥadīth Qudsī, O son of Ādam! Verily so long as you call upon Me and hope in Me, I shall forgive you, despite whatever may have occurred from you, and I do not mind. O son of Ādam! Were your sins to reach the clouds of the sky, then you sought forgiveness from Me, I would forgive you, and I would not mind.

TIRMIDHĪ

Our practising upon the qualities of Al-Ghafūr and Al-Ghaffār is two-fold:

Firstly, we need to make the most of the blessing of being able to turn to Allāh by turning to Him at every instance and juncture, especially following sin.  Allāh is the All-Forgiving, and we should never lose hope in His forgiveness.

ﷺThe Messenger of Allāh said, Every son of Ādam sins, but the best of the sinners is the repentant.

IBN MĀJAH

Secondly, we should also act as people of forgiveness and concealment by forgiving those who wrong us, concealing the shortcomings of others, thinking good of them, and only making public what is good within others.

ʻA-m luizz THE HONOURER Allāh is the only being from whom respect and authority is attained, and likewise, it is only Allāh who can bring about a fall from grace for even the most esteemed in society. He grants honour to whom He wills, and He removes it from whom He wills. No person can claim respect and admiration by virtue of themselves, rather it is Allāh who has blessed them with what may be considered praiseworthy. Allāh raises some people in this life, and lowers others, and just as quickly as Allāh can raise a person in rank, Allāh can bring them disgrace.

True respect and honour, both in this life and the hereafter, lies firmly in following the commandments of Allāh that He has sent down. Through them, a person will be eternally saved from despair, and the worst that may happen to them in this life will be that they undergo brief and temporary tests of their faith. On the other hand, true disgrace and dishonour is in disregarding the commandments of Allāh and the ﷺway of His Messenger , and though a person doing so may be highly regarded in this life by people, this respect is a temporary and fleeting pleasure which will be nothing in comparison to the eternal humiliation. Our goal is for eternal salvation, dignity, and honour, and for that we need to follow what Allāh and ﷺHis Messenger have set out for us. We should not seek the temporary admiration which may be gained from disregarding the commandments of Allāh , but aim for the eternal honour which Allāh has promised for those who strive in His way, no matter how difficult it may be.

A-W lAkīl THE TRUSTEE Trust is invaluable to anyone, and the best trust is that which is placed with one who can overlook all affairs, and who is perfectly capable of fulfilling anything given to them. For this, there is no one better than Allāh as the recipient of our trust. We value our families, friends, and close associates for how much we trust in them, but they cannot provide the same degree of trust that Allāh can. Allāh sees all our affairs: the ones we may tell others about, and the ones we keep secret. Allāh can take care of all our affairs, whereas others we entrust may not be able to do anything to help us besides giving reassurance.

Al-Wakīl as the name of Allāh should bring us to a state of total and absolute reliance on Allāh in all matters. Whilst there will be others in life in whom we place a fair degree of trust, it should ultimately be Allāh in whom we have the greatest faith and confidence. A person is truly fortunate who turns to Allāh rather than any of the creation when they require something and have full conviction that Allāh will answer them. Allāh  is the one deserving of our trust, and we should place it in His care.

A-m lutAkAbbir THE MAJESTIC Pride can only be for one who is permanently greater, and no person, being or thing is permanently greater except Allāh . Every person has the potential to improve or become worse, and when that is the case, one cannot consider themselves greater than another because there is always the possibility of the other being greater, either presently or potentially. It is for this reason that pride in a person has negative connotations, since no one is truly deserving of it. Allāh , however, is forever great, without the possibility of His greatness increasing or decreasing. Therefore, only Allāh is worthy of any pride, and for Him there are no negative connotations attached to His pride since He is forever worthy.

Reflecting on the Blessed Name of Allāh 'Al-Mutakabbir' should bring a realisation within a person that pride does not befit them. A-Q lādir THE ALL POWERFUL Power is determined by the ability of a person to perform an act as they intend. Humans are deficient in their power as they are limited in their ability to do as they wish, and no being has complete authority to do as they will. Only Allāh has complete power that He may do exactly as He wishes and when He wishes. Furthermore, the creationʼs power comes directly from Allāh Himself, which further illustrates the magnitude of Allāh ʼs power. The creation must come to the understanding that nothing happens except through Allāh ʼs will, and that there is no power besides the power of Allāh . If He so wishes, He may remove it from anyone, and thus it is only proper to not abuse the power given to us by Allāh . Al-Qādir further demonstrates how weak we really are, and that there is no reason for any person to be proud of their temporary power, since ultimately it is Allāh who has given it to them. In the Qurʼān, where  Allāh ʼs oneness is mentioned or relevant, the pronoun 'Iʼ is used.

However, when the Qurʼān speaks of  Allāh ʼs Majesty, Power or Grandeur, the pronoun 'Weʼ is used to reflect His Greatness.

A-s shhAkūr THE MOST APPRECIATIVE To show genuine appreciation to someone for something they gave or did is to show gratitude, and gratitude may be expressed by giving something in return, verbally or as a gift. In doing so, we of standards to will cement our Īmān (faith). determine right and wrong; the extent to which an action is right or wrong 'real' facts and not influenced by personal beliefs or feelings personal feelings or opinions HOW DOES A PHILOSOPHICAL ARGUMENT WORK?based on their end purpose In philosophy, there is a distinction between statements and arguments. A statement is simply a sentence which has a truth value; it may be considered either true or false. For example, the sentence: 'it is raining today' can be proven true or false by looking observingoutside and . However, there is nothing within a statement which indicates to its accuracy, and singular statements cannot generally provide truth. On the other hand, arguments are based on two or more statements called premises to provide a third statement, otherwise known as a conclusion. In this case, the conclusion will be true so long as the previous statements are accurate.

This allows us to understand something as true even though we do not necessarily have to observe it. For example:

Premise 1Premise 2Conclusion All men =+Zayd Zayd is are is a a man mortalmortal The example shows that we do not need to prove that Zayd is mortal (by fatally injuring him) to show that he is! We can understand it to be true using other observations and statements derived from those observations.

Whilst there are further details to philosophical arguments, for the following proofs of the existence of Allāh you will premiseargumentconclusionneed to remember the terms , , and , as well as how they work in this regard. THE UNIVERSE: CREATED OR UNCREATED?

There are two claims put forward about the origin of the Universe by those who do not believe that it was created. They assert that either it created itself, or that it came into existence by chance. For reasons which you will read, both are rebutted easily with other arguments which apply to them, as seen below.

12It came into It created itself being by chance can be answered by the can be answered by the 'Kalām' cosmological argument 'Design' argument

THE DESIGN (TELEOLOGICAL) ARGUMENT Imagine you are walking along a unique trail in a forest, through an area which shows no sign of human presence.

There is also no indication that anyone had ever been through this area before. Suddenly, as you look down, you see a mobile phone and as you pick it up, you realise that it had been there for some time. It is muddy, dirty, and not working. In this example, would you think that such a mobile phone was there because someone had dropped it, or would you assume that it had randomly come into being by chance? If you assumed that it had come about there because someone dropped it, then you believe that objects of complexity require an intelligent designer and premisepurpose, and that they do not randomly come into existence. This is the behind the 'Designʼ argument. We know a mobile phone needs a designer and purpose because we see the intricate design and detail of it, and we appreciate the complexity of its conception and build. In a similar manner, the 'Designʼ argument claims that the particular compatibilityUniverse, in its even greater complexity and the way that it shows for life, is far more likely to have - and require - an intelligent designer, and that it must have been created for a purpose. Whilst this argument does not necessarily prove the existence of Allāh , it does show the need for a creator that is supremely powerful. We then use this argument in conjunction with others to prove Allāh ʼs existence.

PARTICULAR COMPATIBILITY fine-tuningThis is referred to as the of the Universe.

Reflect on the perfect Scientists today and in times past have marvelled over just order of Allāh ʼs creation how precisely engineered the Universe is to support life. around you. For example, the Earth sits directly within the habitable that relates to the Design zone of the solar system, and had it been a little closer or argument. further away from the sun, life on this planet would not have been possible. Another example is the law of gravity, which is crucial because through it, galaxies and stars form; without gravity there would be no planets and no life. The strength of gravity is finely-tuned, and had it been stronger or weaker by even the tiniest degree, it would have been impossible for the Universe to be as it is. Thus, the fine- tuning of the Universe points to a creator having made it in such a way that it is uniquely designed to sustain life. THE REASONING OF THE TELEOLOGICAL ARGUMENT IS:

THE KALĀM (COSMOLOGICAL) ARGUMENT Imagine you want to open a shop, but to do so you need permission from your local authority. After applying at your local authority, you are told you need to get permission from even higher up the chain, and so you make an application to the government. You then find out that your shop will not be granted a license unless you ask, in person, from the highest authority in your country. You might assume that this is the final step, and getting permission from the Prime Minister or President would allow you to finally open your business. You would think that the hierarchical chain would end somewhere, otherwise no one would ever get permission to do anything. This is the premise of the Kalām argument. The Kalām (cosmological) argument is remarkably simple to follow. The Universe has a beginning, and everything that has a beginning has a cause. Like how your chair came from a shop, and the shop bought it from a carpenter, who shaped it from wood he bought from a lumberjack, who cut down a tree that was grown, and so on: the Universe had a beginning. This beginning must have been initiated by someone or something, and that is Allāh . Allāh is eternal, and does not need a beginning, and that can be proven by the fact that if He did, the Universe would never have come into existence. Remember the earlier example of the shop? If you cannot get a resolution from anyone as you climb the chain of authority, the shop will never get started. Similarly, Allāh ends the chain of beginnings, and He is the Eternal One, without beginning or end.

Abū Hāmid Muḥammad al-Ghazālī رحمه الله تعالىThe Kalām (cosmological) argument was developed by a great scholar in Islām: .

The premises are all true on their own and therefore the conclusion is irrefutable. THE ARGUMENT GOES AS FOLLOWS:

Premise 1ConclusionPremise 2 Therefore, Whatever The Universe += begins to exist the Universe began to has a causehas a causeexist soundBecause all of the above premises are individually , the conclusion therefore naturally follows and is undeniable.

THE ARGUMENT FROM MORALITY moralityThe argument from states that because all people have some sense of what is right and wrong, and there is no way for nature, chance, or evolution to create such morality, then it must have come from something or someone beyond ourselves. We will then say that it is Allāh who has given us the ability to recognise what is good and bad.

Allāh has provided the faculty of reason through which people can determine what is right and what is wrong. Through this, there are certain actions which everyone (from every society and across time) considers evil and other actions which everyone considers good. Think of giving charity, or forgiveness, or self-sacrifice, from an evolutionary perspective, they would be disadvantageous and thus counterproductive for survival. On the other hand, stealing from others to claim their food and resources, killing for the sake of survival and preying on the weak would be advantageous for survival, and they should be passed down. Yet we universally consider such shouldbeactions abhorrent. The fact that the opposite of what apparently '', is the case in reality, and that we consider justice (even when against ourselves), charity (at our expense), self-sacrifice and other similar values to be good, shows that we share an objective sense of morality which could only have come from Allāh , as there is no other explanation for its existence. THE ARGUMENT FROM MORALITY GOES AS FOLLOWS:

ConclusionPremise 1Premise 2 If God does not exist, then Objective Therefore, += objective moral moral values God values cannot do existexists exist

THE ARGUMENT FROM CONSCIOUSNESS What is consciousness? What makes you… you? Your awareness of yourself, your thoughts and feelings, and your existence is called consciousness. Humans are conscious beings, and they will have inclinations, desires, thoughts, and emotions which extend beyond simple animalistic instinct. Our consciousness allows us to differentiate from one another through our varying attitudes and thoughts to different events and experiences in our lives, which pile up to make a proclaimed 'self'. This self then experiences and feels things differently, where for one a certain experience may induce a particular reaction, but for another it would spur something completely different. For example, one personʼs smelling of coffee might provide them with a very different conscious sensation than for another person. The materialistic explanation for consciousness is that it is merely a brain state. This says that our consciousness can simply be explained by referencing our brains as computer-like, receiving inputs and calculating reactions. Taking the example above, when smelling coffee, our brain is merely receiving the input from the nose, and our brain is interpreting that to create a sensation within ourselves. The problem with this assumption is that it does not account for individual differences between people in how they might experience the smell of coffee, nor explain how even we ourselves might have different sensations at separate times. Most importantly, knowing the chemical structure of coffee and a personʼs brain state will give no indication to the feeling of that person. Their experience will be from their consciousness. The only remaining explanation for consciousness, considering it does not have materialistic explanation, is that it must come from Allāh . Allāh has created consciousness within every person to provide them with the ability to examine themselves in relation to the world around them, to ponder their purpose in this life, and to set themselves on the path Iḥsānto master their own consciousness, so that it becomes one devoted to its Creator, striving towards .

WHAT DOES THE QURʼĀN SAY?

As Muslims, the evidence for Allāh ʼs existence comes first and foremost in His book, the Qurʼān. The Qurʼān is, by virtue of its composition and content, a miracle which could only have been divinely inspired. The Qurʼān instructs us to look into the creation of Allāh for His signs, and calls upon those of intelligence to see the undeniable proofs of Allāh in the world around them. In many verses of the Qurʼān, we are instructed to do Tafakkur (contemplation) and Tadabbur () over the signs of Allāh ʼs creation. Thus, knowing of Allāh ʼs signs, and having a firm grounding in our belief is following a commandment of Allāh , and fulfilling an obligation to which we are bound. As Muslims today, we should make an active effort to develop our understanding and contemplate over the the arguments from this topic. generations to come. Evil & Suffering

the will cover problem of evil Many people throughout history have questioned the existence of Allāh . The and suffering, solutions offered arguments against His existence have ranged from the simple to the seemingly sound, to answer the and those arguments have been regurgitated time and again in different packaging over many centuries. One of the oldest contentions is the argument of the problem of evil problem of evil,

عليه السلامthe Islamic and suffering. This had been proposed since the classical age before ʻĪsā and has and

perspective to been argued since. Over the course of the years, various responses and rebuttals have suffering in the been offered, and naturally, Islām gives a solution to the matter to resolve the burning question.world.

Theodicy: A theodicy is an attempt to justify or defend God from the problem of evil and suffering Inconsistent Triad: where three prepositions exist but only two can be true Logical: clear and sound reasoning inconsistent triadThe problem of evil and suffering may be considered an ''. This is where three prepositions exist but only two may be true, because all three being true creates a logical inconsistency. In this case, the contention is that if:

Allāh is all-Merciful All-MercifulAllāh is all-Powerful THE then how can it be that evil and suffering exists? If He is all-Merciful, INCONSISTENT then He should not desire evil to exist, and since He is all- TRIAD Powerful, He should easily be able to remove all evil. If evil then Evil and All-exists, that would seemingly mean that one of the two other Suffering Powerfulprepositions are untrue.

Exists

SOLUTIONS TO THE PROBLEM OF EVIL AND SUFFERING It is important to note that the problem of evil and suffering contains two layers: THE EMOTIONAL this relates to the idea of Allāh being all- Merciful and all-Powerful yet seemingly allowing ONE people to suffer, which some find difficult to understand. THE LOGICAL this relates to the inconsistent triad mentioned previously, where it would seem illogical to ONE believe that all three can simultaneously exist. The logical aspect of the problem of evil and suffering, whilst seemingly making sense, suffers from hidden assumptions which when disclosed undermine the argument at the core. Firstly, it assumes that Allāh is only all-Merciful and all-Powerful, which is not true. Whilst we certainly do affirm Allāh ʼs Infinite Mercy and Power, we also acknowledge His Infinite Wisdom and Knowledge.

Thus, one response to the problem of evil and suffering is that Allāh , in His Wisdom and Knowledge, has moral and good reason for the existence of evil and suffering. We may be unaware of such reasons as we do not have the scope of understanding or knowledge, in that we are unable to 'zoom' out and 'see the whole picture'.

Another issue with the problem of evil and suffering is the assumption that Allāh , who is all-Merciful and all-Powerful, would 'want' to see a world in which there is no suffering or evil. This assumption fails to recognise that whilst Allāh certainly can create a world in which there is no evil or suffering, such a world would not have any free will. For life to be a test, free will must exist and therefore humans must be given the choice of choosing one of two paths: towards good, or towards the committing of evil.

A further rebuttal against the contention within the problem of evil and suffering, namely that Allāh would be unjust in allowing suffering and evil when he can stop it, is that it does not accommodate the idea of a hereafter. As Allāh mentions, And We shall place the scales of justice on the Day of Judgment, so no soul will be wronged in the least. And ūeven if a deed is the weight of a mustard seed, We shall bring it forth.

QURʼĀN 21:47

The Day of Qiyāmah is not just a day of reckoning, but also a day of restoring justice. Those who were unjustly oppressed or suffered, will be proportionately compensated, and those who oppressed or caused suffering, will have to face reckoning.

Try to make a habit of saying the following whenever something seemingly bad happens to you:َ

لِاحِلِّكُ لعَ هِللدمََحلاِِ�

Praise be to Allāh in all situations

The problem of evil and suffering does not account for the fact that suffering in this world may actually be a cause for much good. As believers, we are distinctly aware of how it is often difficult times that bring us closer to Allāh , and so suffering allows us to forge a deep connection with Him. Moreover, Allāh , in His mercy, even rewards us for the patience and forbearance we show upon the calamities which may befall us, and where others are suffering, we may be rewarded through our charity and kindness to them and they will be rewarded on their patience. This demonstrates the idea that much good cannot come into being without the necessary existence of some suffering or evil first.

Amazing is the affair of the believer, indeed all of his affairs are good, and this is for none but the believer. If something good meets him, he is grateful and that is good for him. And if some harm befalls him, he is patient and that is good for him.

MUSLIM

No calamity afflicts a Muslim except that Allāh expiates some sin of his for it, even if ūthe calamity were the prick he endures from a thorn.

BUKHĀRĪ

Ultimately, the reason behind suffering and evil in this world is understood fully only by Allāh , and none beside Him. It is Allāh ʼs Qadr, good and bad, which comes from Him and only He knows where the twists of fate lead. As humans with limited capacity to understand the grand tapestry of all existence, we cannot even begin to understand, let alone fully comprehend the wisdom in Allāh ʼs decisions, or the intricacies of Qadr. It is as though we are trying to form a picture from viewing one piece of the puzzle, when only Allāh can see the full picture. We should content ourselves with the belief that Allāh , whilst being the Most Powerful, Merciful and Wise, is also the Most Just. Whatever evil may be, Allāh  will never allow injustice to prevail. None will suffer more than they can bear, and none shall be rewarded for what they have not earnt. Allāh Himself says, And I am not unjust with my slaves.

QURʼĀN 50:29

SOLUTIONS TO THE 'PROBLEM OF EVIL AND SUFFERING'

GOOD COMES FROM IT There is much good that cannot come into 01being except through the existence of suffering and evil. Kindness we show to others when something afflicts them can only come through affliction; huge amounts of charity is given during times of hardship; people come together when crisis strikes. Thus, the presence of evil is often the cause of a far greater amount of good.

BEYOND HUMAN COMPREHENSION

عليهما السلامAs the story of Mūsā and Khaḍir shows us, even the

height of human intelligence and knowledge cannot fully grasp the intricacies of Qadr. Allāh  has reasons for what He does and allows to happen, and the moving parts of the universe all work in conjunction to bring about a result Allāh  wants. Since we have a very limited view, and can only see one angle, we cannot form the full picture. This does not mean however that there is no overarching plan devised by Allāh  in His Wisdom and Knowledge.

A TEST FROM ALLĀH As Muslims, we believe we have been placed in this world to be tested, and our test will come through various difficulties we face in life and how we react to them. A believer will see difficulties as ways to get closer to Allāh  and understand that the ultimate prize of paradise can only be attained through bearing any hardship in this world.

DETACHMENT FROM THE WORLD The suffering of this world gives us indication to the fact that it is a temporary abode and allows us to detach ourselves from it. We see the passing of people every day, and the transitory reality of everything in existence is forever staring at us. Though we may sometimes forget this due to our worldly occupations, its ever-present and inescapable truth reminds us to give timely thought and effort for the hereafter.

FREE WILL It is logically impossible to create a world to test humanity, where they have the free choice to do good and evil, whilst also making it such that no evil exists in that world. Allāh  certainly can create beings which can only do good, as he did with angels, however, in our specific case, doing so would mean there would be no test.

SPIRITUAL PERSPECTIVE Suffering in this world provides fertile ground for the spiritual growth of both the one afflicted, and those who may be present to assist them. As Muslims, we believe every difficulty to be an opportunity to get closer to Allāh , and every personʼs need is similarly an opportunity for us to be charitable and helpful in every way possible. The rewards of our attitude and efforts to combat suffering, hardship, and afflictions of any and every kind are far greater than their pain in this world, and we believe Allāh to fulfil His promise to reward us for our patience and generosity.

رحمه الله تعالىIMĀM GHAZĀLI ʼS EXAMPLE رحمه الله تعالىImām Ghazālī was also asked about the problem of

evil and suffering, to which he answered with the following example: A young child may be doted upon by his mother who prevents him receiving treatment (which may temporarily pain him), whilst the determined father may take him for treatment forcefully, and to this an ignorant person may consider the mother merciful rather than the father. However, an intelligent person will understand that the fatherʼs placing of his son in pain through treatment is due to the utmost mercy, love, and affection for him.

Imām continues, رحمه الله تعالىGhazālī

And there is no evil in existence except that within it is good, and by the removal of that evil the good is also removed. Furthermore, by the removal of that good, an evil transpires that is greater than the evil it replaced.

AL-MAQSAD AL-ASNĀ

In this case, the pain of the treatment may be avoided but the child will suffer from the illness far more than what he might have during the treatment. THE STORY OF MŪSĀ AND KHAḌIR

عليه السلامعليه السلامعليه السلامعليه السلامAnother example is in the story of Mūsā and Khaḍir . Mūsā set out on a journey to learn from Khaḍir , as عليه السلامعليه السلامAllāh had informed him that he is more knowledgeable than Mūsā . When they met, Mūsā asked to accompany عليه السلامعليه السلامhim to learn from him. Khaḍir eventually accepted, though he warned Mūsā that he would not be able to bear

with his actions, and that he should not question him.

عليه السلامعليه السلامOn their travels together, they boarded a ship, which Khaḍir intentionally damaged causing Mūsā to protest, عليه السلامespecially considering they had been granted free passage. Later, they encountered a boy whom Khaḍir killed, and عليه السلامعليه السلامعليه السلامagain Mūsā protested the killing of an innocent child. Khaḍir reminded Mūsā that he had agreed not to عليه السلامquestion him, and Mūsā relented.

Then, later in their travels, they entered a town where they asked for lodging and food from the townspeople. The townspeople, against respected custom, refused to host the travellers, leaving them to fend for themselves.

عليه السلامعليه السلامعليه السلامKhaḍir , whilst in the town, saw a broken wall and repaired it. Mūsā then protested again, asking Khaḍir why عليه السلامhe did not ask for payment from the townspeople, at least in food and lodging. Seeing this as the final straw, Khaḍir عليه السلامexcused himself from Mūsā ʼs companionship.

Before they left each other however,

عليه السلامعليه السلامKhaḍir offered Mūsā the

explanation for his actions, and it is in this explanation where we get a glance at the hidden wisdom behind Allāh allowing matters to occur

عليه السلامas they do. Khaḍir explained

that he had damaged the ship in the first incident to save it from being repossessed by an oppressive ruler, who had been taking ships in good condition. He then explained the second incident, that the child had pious parents, and that he knew from knowledge he had been given by Allāh , that this child would one day grow to corrupt them.

Thus, he took the childʼs life and Allāh gave the parents another child.

Lastly, he repaired the wall in the town of misers without payment as he knew of their nature, and that the wall belonged to a pair of orphans under which their parents had buried wealth. He knew that if the wall disintegrated any further, the townspeople would discover and deprive the orphans of their wealth.

This entire story shows us the hidden reasons behind why Allāh may allow the existence of what we consider evil.

It is only a glimpse at the wisdom of Allāh , and we would not be able to comprehend more than what Allāh has allowed us. This story was mentioned for us to take hope from, and to provide an answer to the problem of evil.

Proofs of Prophethood

Human beings are hard-wired to believe in a God or a higher power. Throughout recorded history, and in every civilization known to man, the people of each society felt the innate need to worship and attribute their existence to something greater than themselves. We as Muslims believe this to be Allāh ʼs doing; that He has placed within each of us a kernel will cover the need prophets, so that once we recognise His existence, we are provided with a link to Him for Prophethood, through them and through His books. different proofs for our ﷺMessenger ʼs prophethood, and why the Qurʼān Risālah:the sending is the greatest of messengers and miracle sent as their messagean evidence of Islāmʼs truth.Throughout Islamic history, Muslim scholars have Subjective: pondered, written, and elaborated on a genre of influenced by or literature called Dalāʼil an-Nubuwwah (Proofs of based on personal Prophethood). beliefs or feelings

Thus, Allāh ʼs sending of prophets and books is so that humanity not only understands that there is a Creator, but what the Creator wants of them. Prophets and books teach people what is right and wrong, and what they need to objectivedo to achieve goodness. They provide what is called an morality, which means a collection of ethics and moral values that exist outside of human interpretation. This provides purpose to a person and offers a reason for every personʼs existence.

Another benefit of prophethood is that through it we can recognise Allāh . Without prophethood, humanity would not know Allāh ʼs attributes or how to worship Him, nor would we know about the hereafter, the Day of Judgement, and the rewards or consequences of our actions. Thus, Risālah is vital in giving purpose to a believer, and allows them to recognise their Lord as He wants His creation to do so.

WHY IS THE PROPHET MUḤAMMAD ﷺ A TRUE PROPHET?

ﷺThe Prophet was the final appointment within a long line of prophets who were sent by Allāh . The truth of his prophethood is proved through the Qurʼān, the miracles he was blessed with, and his flawless character. We believe ﷺthe Messenger to be Allāh ʼs final messenger for various reasons, some of which will be detailed below.

MIRACLES ﷺThe Messenger was blessed with many miracles, some minor and some major. Miracles are events that occur outside the scope and explanation of science, and are granted to certain people whom Allāh favours so that He may display a sign through them (to His creation).

Interestingly, the word in Arabic for a miracle is 'Muʻjizah', which translates as 'something which renders incapable', as ﷺa miracle leaves its witnesses incapable of producing anything similar. Allāh blessed our Messenger Muḥammad with many great miracles, for example: The Night Journey (al-Isrāʼ and al-Miʻrāj)

Allāh  blessed Rasūlullāh ﷺ with the incredible ascent to the Heavens called the Miʻrāj. This journey, which was completed in merely one night, began with al-Isrāʼ, the Prophet ﷺʼs visit to Masjid al-Aqṣā. When he later recounted this journey in the presence of the Makkans, the disbelievers scoffed and ridiculed him. He was, however, able to validate his account by relating to them exact details of the Al-Aqṣā precinct that only one who had travelled there would be able Why do we believe these narrations?ﷺto recognise. Furthermore, Rasūlullāh These narrations have been recorded by foretold the arrival of trade caravans he had so many people that they reach the level passed which none knew were to return. of Tawātur (see The Search for Truth).

The Splitting of the Moon Allāh  refers to this miracle in the Qurʼān: The Hour has drawn near, and the moon has split asunder.

QURʼĀN 54:1

The Makkan disbelievers asked the Prophet ﷺ for a miracle to be shown to them, and Allāh  allowed the ﷺProphet to split the moon in half. The disbelievers and believers alike bore witness to a miracle unlike any other. The Miracle of Water There are many narrations of Rasūlullāh ﷺ being given a small amount of water in a vessel when water supplies were dwindling, and him multiplying it by Allāh ʼs permission, much to the amazement of onlookers. The Miracle of Provision Numerous reports from various ﷺCompanions of the Prophet mention how Rasūlullāh ﷺ vastly increased a tiny portion of food, dates, or a meal to feed or supply a vast group of people. Some narrations record how even after everyone had finished eating, the original amount remained as it was to be stored for later.

THE GREATEST MIRACLE The Qurʼān is without doubt the greatest of all of Allāh ʼs miracles. As mentioned earlier, a miracle is something which renders others incapable of reproducing, and the Qurʼān is unique in that Allāh challenges others to reproduce its likeness or better, and yet none have been able to. The people of Makkah during the time of the Prophet ﷺ were renowned masters of the Arabic language, and yet they conceded to not being able to produce even one verse which might match any in the Qurʼān for its eloquence, meaning and beauty. Therefore, the Qurʼān is a miracle in the fullest sense and, moreover, it is unique as a miracle as it is an enduring one, lasting until the final days. The Qurʼān is miraculous in its eloquence but not limited to it: it contains numerical and scientific miracles, prophecies, and it is linguistically flawless. It is further miraculous in that Allāh promises its perfect preservation and that it has indeed been perfectly preserved. The Qurʼān is the most read and studied book in human history, and its status amongst other books stands clear in every regard. It is Allāh ʼs gift to humanity.

QURANIC MIRACLES THE MIRACLE OF ITS PRESERVATION Very few books that are popular survive centuries in the exact form in which they are written, as people that come later distort the books to suit their own narratives, beliefs and ideas. Even modern books undergo revisions as peopleʼs attitudes and feelings change, and the books are amended to reflect those newer beliefs. However, an enduring miracle of the Qurʼān is that Allāh promises within it, that He is to preserve it. Allāh says, It is certainly We who have revealed the Reminder (Qurʼān), and it is certainly We who will preserve it.

QURʼĀN 15:9

The fact that the Qurʼān prophesises its preservation, and after a millennia and a half later, has remained exactly as it was ﷺrevealed to the Messenger , is one of its greatest miracles.

SCIENTIFIC MIRACLES Modern science has shown how life requires water to sustain itself, and for the very basis of life itself, water is a necessary component. The Qurʼān, over 1,400 years ago, mentioned the same idea, that every living thing begins with water. Allāh says, And we created every living thing from water…

QURʼĀN 24:45

This simple statement encompasses a scientific truth of great importance, and in the time of the ﷺProphet , it could only have been known by someone informed by the Divine. The universe is in constant expansion, as science has discovered through observations of galaxies and stars over years of study and with highly advanced instruments. The Qurʼān however told us over 14 centuries ago, where Allāh says, And the Heavens We created with Our hands, and indeed We are expanding it.

QURʼĀN 51:47

This verse points to one of the miracles of the Qurʼān as ﷺRasūlullāh could only have known this through revelation, and no other person alive could have known this.

A SHORT PROPHECY  One famous prophecy is within Sūrah ar-Rūm, where Allāh prophesises the 'comeback' victory of the Romans against the Persians. The previous wars had seen such deep Persian advances into Byzantine Roman territory that many predicted the end of the great empire.

Within nine years however, against all odds, the Romans had managed to regain their territory in full and forced a treaty with the Persians. This would have been considered impossible a decade earlier, yet the Qurʼān predicted it with incredible accuracy.

RING COMPOSITION - CHIASMUS The ring structure is a linguistic method of composition - also called 'chiasmus' - wherein themes of within a text flow in a circular pattern, mirroring each other and bringing natural closure to themes opened for . In this structure, the first topic mirrors the last, the second with the second last, and so on. The ring composition is found in Sūrah al-Baqarah, the longest chapter in the Qurʼān and one which was revealed in parts, at different times, and often corresponding to events. It would have been impossible to organise the chapter ﷺaccording to the ring structure unless one had prior knowledge of questions which were to be asked of the Prophet and of events which were to occur. Furthermore, considering the Qurʼān was not written, this structure would have had to be organised in the mind, which is an impossible feat for any of the creation.

The Final Revelation

The Qurʼān is the unchanged Word of Allāh , sent down via the Angel Jibrīl and etched ﷺonto the heart of the Prophet Muḥammad . It is the book revered by Muslims around the world: recited, read and pondered over, steering mankind for over 1,400 years. The Qurʼān was sent as a miracle to inspire, a guide to be followed, and an everlasting vestige of Allāh what will cover ﷺthe proof of prophethood for the final and greatest of Allāh ʼs messengers: Muḥammad .
