WAḤY - REVELATION The Qurʼān was initially revealed on Laylatul Qadr to the First Heaven, to be ﷺﷺrevealed in parts to the Messenger Muḥammad . Rasūlullāh received his first revelation in the Cave of Hirā, where he had been secluding himself for many days and nights at a time. The first revelation came as a shock, as ﷺthe Angel Jibrīl gripped the Prophet Muḥammad and proclaimed to him “Read!”

ﷺThe revelation would come to the Prophet via the Angel Jibrīl, either in actual form or in the form of a person. It

ﷺرضي الله عنهwas an arduous process for the Prophet and would take a certain physiological toll on him. Zayd narrates

ﷺthat the Prophet ʼs thigh was on his thigh when revelation came down, and it became so heavy that he feared his ﷺWaḥythigh would break. Rasūlullāh himself, when asked how would be revealed, gave the explanation that, Sometimes it is ūrevealed like the ringing of a bell (the sound coming from all directions) – and this form of revelation is the hardest of all.

BUKHĀRĪ

رضي الله عنهاʻĀʼishah further mentions,

ﷺI saw the Messenger receiving revelation on an extremely cold day, and I noticed sweat dripping from his forehead.

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺWaḥy would come at intervals, often due to an incident or occasion in the life of the Prophet or one of his companions (see example). Sometimes, it was because revelation was asked for or demanded, and on such occasions large portions of revelation were revealed in one go rather than singular verses or small portions. For example, one opinion on why Sūrah Yūsuf was revealed is that the Makkans

ﷺعليه السلامasked the Prophet about the story of Yūsuf to test his truthfulness, and thus it was revealed in

one revelation.

رضي الله عنهاEXAMPLE: KHAWLAH BINT THAʻLABAH Khawlah bint Thaʻlabah was a Madanī woman who was married to the Companion of رضي الله عنها ﷺرضي الله عنهthe Prophet Aws ibn Ṣāmit . She and her husband fell out over an argument, and

he swore to stay away from her. When he eventually calmed down, he tried to return to his wife, but she removed herself from his company claiming that he had sworn an oath. She ﷺthen informed her husband that until Allāh and His Messenger have not decided ﷺbetween them, she would not return to him. After she complained to the Prophet , Allāh  revealed verses which vindicated her, and certain injunctions were passed based on her case. Allāh mentions her plea in the Qurʼān:

Indeed, Allāh has heard the argument of the woman who pleaded with you ūO Prophet concerning her husband, and complained to Allāh.

QURʼĀN 58:1

Incredibly, the Qurʼān was not revealed in the order we see today. It was revealed over 23 years correlating with events in ﷺthe life of the Prophet , and different parts were revealed at separate times. Amazingly, however, despite the Messenger ﷺ not being able to write the Qurʼān as he was unlettered, the Qurʼān still does not show any signs of contradiction or irregularity, neither in content, clarity nor composition. Allāh alludes to this in the Qurʼān saying... A TAPESTRY OF REVELATION REVELATION 13 YEARS BEFORE HIJRAH (610 CE)

Revelation began in the Cave of Hira in 610 CE.

ﷺRasūlullāh was approached by the Angel Jibrīl and commanded to read, though he was unable to. The first five verses of Sūrah al-ʻAlaq (96:1-5) were revealed during this revelation.

MAKKAN PERIOD 13 YEARS (610 – 622 CE) This is the time the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions spent in Makkah. The Sūrahs revealed during this period are considered 'Makkī' Sūrahs. These chapters focused mainly on establishing Tawḥīd (belief in the oneness of Allāh ) and belief in the Ākhirah (Hereafter). Stories of previous prophets, messengers and people were also revealed to serve as both inspiration and warning to the Makkan believers and non-believers.

...Do they not then ponder over the Qurʼān? Had it been from someone other than Allāh, they would have found in it a great deal of discrepancy.

QURʼĀN 4:82

MADANĪ PERIOD 11 YEARS (622 – 632 CE) The Muslims migrated to Yathrib (Madīnah) after enduring pain and suffering in Makkah. The Messenger of Allāh ﷺ continued to receive revelation, but the themes changed with the change in environment. The chapters which were revealed after Hijrah are called 'Madanī' Sūrahs, and focus more on laws, commandments, and societal instruction. This is because the belief of the companions had been firmly established during the Makkan years to now wholeheartedly accept any command issued to them. The Hijrah marked the turning point for the Muslims who now had their own communal setting to practice their religion freely.

Find out the virtues of and challenge yourself to memorise the following: Sūrah Yāsīn, Sūrah al-Mulk, Sūrah as-Sajdah, Sūrah ad-Dukhān and the first and last 10 verses of Sūrah al-Kahf.

WRITING The Qurʼān was written down and preserved during ﷺthe time of the Prophet by several official scribes and certain others who could also write. They would write on slate, bones, parchment, and other similar material. However, it was not one uniform collection in the form of one book.

TEACHING AND LEARNING At the same time, the Qurʼān was preserved through the , teaching and learning of the ﷺCompanions. Rasūlullāh encouraged memorising the Qurʼān, and mentioned the virtues for the one who memorises and devotes himself to it. One famous Ḥadīth quotes him as saying, The companion of the Qurʼān will be told (on the Day of Qiyamah): Recite! And ascend (the stages of paradise)! Recite carefully as you recited in the world, for you will reach your abode when you come to the last verse you recite.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

ﷺThe Companions were also told to constantly revise what they had learnt, with Rasūlullāh advising:

Keep refreshing your knowledge of the Qurʼān, for I swear by Him in Whose Hand the life of Muḥammad rests, it flees the memory faster than a camel does from its tying ropes.

MUSLIM

Furthermore, many Companions were sent out to teach the Qurʼān to

رضي الله عنهothers. For example, Mus‘ab ibn ʻUmayr was sent to Madīnah before the رضي الله عنهHijrah, and consequently Barāʼ ibn ʻĀzib relates that he knew all of the

MADĪNAH Mufaṣṣalāt (Sūrah Qāf till Sūrah an-Nās) even prior to the coming of the Prophet

ﷺرضي الله عنه to Madīnah. Amongst others, Mu‘ādh ibn Jabl was sent to Yemen, and رضي الله عنهAbū ʻUbaydah was sent to Najrān. A group of Qurrāʼ (proficient reciters of the

MAKKAH Qurʼān) were sent to a place called Biʼr Ma‘ūnah, but they were tragically ambushed and martyred enroute. This all illustrates that not only is there no doubt regarding the preservation of the Qurʼān, NAJRĀN but that there was a living tradition of learning and propagating the blessed book as it had ﷺbeen revealed. During the lifetime of the Messenger , both written records and memory were YEMEN used in the preservation of the Qurʼān, with the memory of the Companions being aided by written records, and the written records being verified by the collective memory of the Companions. This divinely contrived two-factor process meant that the Qurʼān we read today is exactly the same as was ﷺrevealed to Rasūlullāh .

ﷺTHE DEMISE OF RASŪLULLĀH 11 AH (632 CE)

ﷺRasūlullāh passed away in 11 AH (632 CE), after receiving the entire Qurʼān and having taught it fully to others. In his

رضي الله عنهاﷺfinal Ramaḍān, the order of the verses and chapters was finalised. Fāṭimah narrates that the Prophet informed

her that:

Jibrīl would present (recite) the Qurʼān to myself every year, and this year ﷺ(the Ramaḍān before the Prophet 's demise) he presented it twice, and I believe my time has drawn close.

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺDuring Rasūlullāh ʼs life, he completed receiving the Qurʼān and delivered it to his people and all of humanity. The verses were ordered, the chapters sequenced and the revelation complete before he left this world. There were many Ṣaḥābah remaining, a great number of whom were Ḥuffāẓ (those who had memorised the Qurʼān entirely) and even more had written verses and chapters of the Qurʼān. THE KHILĀFAH OF ABŪ BAKR 11 – 13 AH (632 – 634 CE)

رضي الله عنهThe Khilāfah of Abū Bakr saw several false prophets emerge. The most prominent

amongst them was Musaylamah al-Kadhdhāb (The Liar). The Muslims eventually defeated him at the battle of Yamāmah where he was killed, but the battle unfortunately saw the loss of many Ṣaḥābah who were Ḥuffāẓ. This prompted concerns for the Qurʼānʼs preservation amongst the Companions.

رضي الله عنهرضي الله عنهOut of this concern, ʻUmar approached Abū Bakr and suggested the compilation of رضي الله عنهthe Qurʼān in a written form. Though Abū Bakr was initially hesitant, saying:

ﷺHow can you do that which the Prophet himself did not do?

BUKHĀRĪ

THE KHILĀFAH OF ʻUTHMĀN 23 – 35 AH (644 – 656 CE)

رضي الله عنهThe Khilāfah of ʻUthmān saw further expansion of the Muslim Empire, and

an influx of reverts to the growing faith. As many of those who became Muslim spoke different dialects of Arabic (and even different languages) to the Quraysh, certain groups began to have disagreements as to the correct pronunciation of the Qurʼān.

Ḥudhayfah ibn al-Yamān came to ʻUthmān in 25 AH from the رضي الله عنهرضي الله عنه

Azerbaijan and Armenian border, where he reported the issues the Muslims were facing over the correct Qurʼānic pronunciation. He advised ʻUthmān

to take definitive steps in redressing the issue, or face the Ummah رضي الله عنه

having the same issues regarding the Qurʼān which had plagued the Jews and the Christians before them.

رضي الله عنهʻUthmān resolved رضي الله عنهاto end these disputes. He sent for Ḥafṣah ʼs copy رضي الله عنهof the Qurʼān, and ordered Zayd ibn Thābit , ʻAbdullāh رضي الله عنهرضي الله عنهibn az-Zubayr , Sa‘īd ibn al-ʻĀṣ and ʻAbdur رضي الله عنهRaḥmān ibn al-Ḥārith to make perfect copies of

it. He also instructed them to write in the dialect of the Quraysh, yet in a way that the script is complimentary to other dialects. Once they completed the task,

رضي الله عنهʻUthmān had the Qurʼān recited to the Companions

for their approval. He then ordered all other manuscripts or fragments on which the Qurʼān had been written to be destroyed.

Eight copies of the newly completed Muṣḥaf were sent to THE MANUSCRIPT OF THE QURʼĀN IN BIRMINGHAM, UKdifferent parts of the Muslim empire. People of each area were told to make copies from the Muṣḥaf sent to them if they required them for personal use. Thus, the ʻUthmāni Muṣḥaf became prevalent throughout the Muslim world, and the differences in dialect, pronunciation and certain words were resolved.

RIGHTS OF THE QUR’ĀN 01FIRM BELIEF The Qur’ān is Allāh ’s word that holds true for all time and people, and it deserves our belief and conviction in it. We believe in all that the Qur’ān says, and we reject nothing of it.

02RESPECT AND HONOUR The Qur’ān has the right to be honoured; this is through respect of it, its written and recited form, and respect of those people and places blessed by a relation to it.

RECITATION We have been commanded to recite the Qur’ān, and we have been promised great rewards for its recitation. The Qur’ān has a right that a believer spends time daily reciting portions of it.

UNDERSTANDING AND 04 Allāh  sent down the Qur’ān as a message of guidance for all humanity. We are responsible to make an effort in understanding and reflecting over Allāh ’s message, and allowing it to create a change in our lives.

05IMPLEMENTATION The Qur’ān should have an effect in our lives, and the instructions within Allāh ’s book are to be implemented and brought into action within one’s life.

06PROPAGATION Allāh ’s final revelation was for all time, and for all people. It is our responsibility as those blessed with the Qur’ān that we share it with others.

Allāh ’s gift of the Qur’ān is not to be enjoyed alone, but to be shared with all so that each may be presented with the offer of eternal success.

READING WITH TAJWĪD AND A PLEASANT TONE ﷺThe Qurʼān is to be read, reflected upon, and enjoyed. The Messenger said, Beautify the Qurʼān with your voices.

NASĀʼĪ

Through paying close attention to the rules of Tajwīd and the Makhārij (pronunciation) of letters and words, as well as attempting to read the Qurʼān melodiously, we can beautify our recitation of the Qurʼān. We should endeavour to perfect our Tajwīd and pronunciation and take steps to constantly improve. Allāh promises great reward to those who try to ﷺimprove their recitation of the Qurʼān. Rasūlullāh mentioned that, One who is proficient in the Qurʼān is associated with the noble, upright, recording angels; and he who falters in it, and finds it difficult, will have two rewards.

MUSLIM

Similarly, though everyone has different voices and some are born with sweeter-sounding voices than others, we should still try and recite the Qurʼān in a manner whereby we are attempting to beautify it. This not only adds to the enjoyment of reading it, but undoubtedly also serves to soothe our hearts during such recitation. Have a class traditional and to speak about. The Search for Truth

As human beings, we are constantly faced with the question of truth. This matter is everywhere, from the classroom to the courtroom, and we are perpetually being placed in positions Fiqh: laws taken out In this you by Muslim jurists and where we must determine what the truth is. what is will cover legal scholars from the Sometimes truth (or true knowledge) can be knowledgehow we , sources of Islamic law easily established, as in determining whether know things, and someone has a father for example, as their what are sources of Ijmāʻ: consensus of existence proves that. In Islām, we have our own framework for determining what is true and false, which helps us understand the laws which shape our lives, and the way we live as well.

HOW DO WE KNOW THINGS?

REASON AND LOGIC: We may use our intellect and reason to come to a fair number of conclusions based on evidence or facts, such as mathematical principles or that all triangles must have three sides.

BELIEF: We may believe something to be true, such as our family loving us. This may be evidenced by the actions of our family towards us.

OBSERVATION: We may see things and come to conclusions on certain matters through observation. For example, planting a seed, watering it, and then observing it grow, gives us knowledge of how things grow.

AUTHORITY: We trust those who we believe have greater knowledge or expertise, such as experts or reliable sources. We believe the information we receive from such people because we trust their ability to provide truthful knowledge.

TESTIMONY: We may acquire knowledge and information from someone else through their testimony or account of an event. Depending on their reliability, we may choose to trust them or consider them dishonest. Of the above, whilst we get knowledge from them, it may not necessarily be true knowledge. We may believe something to be true, or observe something, only to find out the opposite or realise we have observed it incorrectly. It is important for us to consider our sources of knowledge because they shape our beliefs and assumptions, and from there, our actions and habits.

In Islām, we consider two routes for us to ascertain knowledge. Of these, we believe that one gives us absolute truth, as it has divine origin. The other however, may give us knowledge that is true or untrue, and we will have to use various tools and methods to determine its accuracy. The two branches are:

ʻUlūm Naqliyyah ʻUlūm ʻAqliyyah Transmitted KnowledgeRational Knowledge This is the branch of knowledge that is from This refers to knowledge which may come to us Allāh through the Qurʼān and the Sunnah of through the senses or through rational thought ﷺthe Messenger , and so it includes our beliefs, and inference. The knowledge acquired through theology, laws, rituals, and worship. observation and experimentation would fall within this category, and so this branch includes Ruling: Knowing of ʻUlūm ʻNaqliyyah that applies to each person is Farḍ ʻAyn.the formal (logic, mathematics) and empirical (natural, social, applied) sciences.

Ruling: Engaging with ʻUlūm ʻAqliyyah is considered Farḍ Kifāyah.

ʻUlūm Naqliyyah is the nobler of the two branches of knowledge as it has divine origin and involves the study of Allāh ʼs book, the sayings of our beloved ﷺMessenger , and the Sharīʻah. We study these so that we understand what Allāh wants of us, and so that we may derive laws and rulings on how to live our lives.

ʻULŪM AD-DĪN - THE RELIGIOUS SCIENCES ﷺThe Prophet of Allāh said, If Allāh wills good for a person, He grants them comprehension of the Dīn (religion).

BUKHĀRĪ

Being competent and knowledgeable of the religious sciences is a sign of a personʼs acceptance in the court of Allāh , and that is because these sciences are such which relate to the greatest of books and lives: the Qurʼān and the life of our Beloved ﷺMessenger Muḥammad .

Whilst the entirety of the religious sciences is a complex, living body of work built upon for over a thousand years, we will cover some of the largest branches here.

QURʼĀN The Qurʼān is not only to be read, but to be understood, and its deeper meanings to be brought forth. In this endeavour, Muslim scholars have over centuries written volumes upon volumes of Tafsīr (Qurʼānic exegesis or explanation) shining a light upon the meaning of the Qurʼān from different angles. Some may view it to explain laws, others for the moral s, whilst others may highlight individual meanings of words and go in depth within the eloquence of Allāh ʼs word. The in-depth study of Qurʼān cannot be done by any layperson. Understanding itʼs deeper meaning, or attempting to explain the Qurʼān can only be done by one proficient in a number of fields relating to Qurʼānic study. For example, having an expertise in Arabic grammar and syntax, coupled with an understanding of Arabic rhetoric, is the bare necessity in language. Following that, one should be aware of Ḥadīth, Fiqh, Uṣūl al-Fiqh (principles of Fiqh), and Uṣūl at-Tafsīr (principles of Tafsīr) before attempting to derive meanings from the Qurʼān.

Nevertheless, one may read the Qurʼān and its translation to their hearts content.

ḤADĪTH The Ḥadīth are a collection of narrations detailing the sayings, actions ﷺand approval of our beloved Messenger Muḥammad . The Ḥadīth are important for our religion not only for the information they give us on his blessed life and character, but they form a foundation for many of our laws and they explain the Qurʼān comprehensively.

Allāh says in the Qurʼān, Whatever the Messenger gives you, take it, and whatever he forbids you from, abstain (from it).

QURʼĀN 59:7

This verse highlights the importance of Ḥadīth, and from this importance came the field of Ḥadīth studies.

Since a large part of our Sharīʻah comes from the field of Ḥadīth, scholars of the past spent truly extraordinary efforts to preserve and maintain the authenticity of Aḥādīth. They classified the Aḥādīth according to authenticity, checked every narrator for their piety and reliability, and then wrote books documenting their ﷺwork for others. This was done to attribute only the most reliable of narrations to the Prophet and use them ﷺfor law, and to stop people from incorrectly ascribing to our Messenger what he had not said.

ﷺFrom the time of Rasūlullāh , the Ṣaḥābah would memorise his sayings, and they passed them to those who came to learn from them, and the cycle continued. Certain places were held in high regard for their Ḥadīth scholars, and students flocked from all over the Muslim world to attend the s of renowned Muḥaddithūn (Ḥadīth narrators). Over time however, many Aḥādith began to be narrated, with many fabricated. The Muḥaddithūn realised this and developed criteria to regulate the authenticity of every Ḥadīth. These criteria evaluated the piety and integrity of the narrator, as well as their strength of memory. Only those narrators who were deemed to be honest and pious, and have extremely strong retention were considered for Aḥādīth. The scholars also judged the content of the Ḥadīth itself, applying concepts such as Tawātur. The criteria written down by the scholars, though different from Muḥaddith to Muḥaddith, had largely overlapping principles. These principles formed the Uṣūl al-Ḥadīth.

A CLOSER LOOK AT A ḤADĪTH SANAD (CHAIN)

Ḥadīth would do extensive on the people they learnt their Ḥadīth from, disregarding

رحمه الله تعالىanyone about whom they had doubts. ʻAbdullāh ibn al-Mubārak , a famous Ḥadīth scholar, says,

TAWĀTUR Tawātur is a concept within Islamic law wherein a testimony is accepted if there are so many independent narrators of the same report that they could not have conspired to fabricate the report without the fabrication being exposed. The diagram below illustrates how this may happen.

FIQH AND UṢŪL AL-FIQH FiqhUṣūl al-FiqhThe study of law is called , and within it, are the principles for law called . Uṣūl al-Fiqh are principles which determine how rulings are understood from the Qurʼān and Sunnah, or made through other means. This science is a very intricate and detailed field of study, and it exists so that the Sharīʻah is understood as intended in the Qurʼān and Sunnah, and not misinterpreted, deliberately or mistakenly, by anyone. Adhering to the Uṣūl (principles) is of the utmost Madhāhibimportance, and though there are small differences between , the overarching principles remain the same. The principles apply to our four sources of law:

QURʼĀN SUNNAH2 3IJMĀʻ QIYĀS4 These sources begin firstly and most importantly with the Qurʼān since this is unchanged and the infallible Word of Allāh . What is within the Qurʼān is established undeniably within the religion and cannot be contradicted. Furthermore, the ﷺSunnah of our Messenger that is established through authentic narrations is the second of the primary sources, and these provide the majority of what forms the religion.

IjmāʻQiyāsIjmāʻThe third and fourth sources, which may be considered secondary sources, are called and . means consensus, and it refers to the consensus of learned scholars on a legal matter. We consider the agreement of the scholars Qiyāsto be binding, as we believe that Allāh would not allow for the entire Ummah to deviate. on the other hand, refers to using existing laws within the Qurʼān and Sunnah to derive principles that form the foundations of those laws, and then applying those principles on contemporary issues that are similar.

EXAMPLE OF QIYĀS The prohibition of alcohol is established in the Qurʼān, and the underlying cause behind the prohibition is also referenced which is intoxication. In performing Qiyās, scholars took the reasoning behind the prohibition of alcohol and applied it to where something similar is found. In this manner, despite drugs not being mentioned explicitly in the Qurʼān or Sunnah, their consumption is also considered impermissible like alcohol because they intoxicate as well.

TADWĪN AL-FIQH (THE DEVELOPMENT OF FIQH)

ﷺﷺDuring the lifetime of the Messenger Muḥammad , any issue would be brought directly to him. He would ﷺthen rule directly on the matter. After Rasūlullāh ʼs passing, during the period of the rightly guided Khulafāʼ, rulings would similarly be brought to the Khalīfah of the time who would check the Qurʼān for the ruling, and if he could not find it there, then he would look within the Sunnah by asking the Companions around him if any similar incident had occurred. If nothing was found in the Sunnah, then he would consult others, and pass on their judgement. Lastly, if they could not agree on a judgement, he would offer his own opinion. As Islām grew beyond Arabia however, the Muslim community grew in different countries with diverse populations. Ṣaḥābah were sent out to different cities as religious leaders and they would do as the Khulafāʼ did. Over time, as they passed, the need for a more systematic approach became apparent. Students of those Ṣaḥābah developed frameworks, methodologies and principles for interpreting and applying the Qurʼān and Sunnah, as well as what to do in the absence of any divine decree. Eventually, this led to the development of various schools of thought called Madhāhib.

TAQLĪD THE FOUR MADHĀHIB Taqlīd refers to following an Imām and 1.ḤanafīMadhab a Madhhab for their religious rulings

Imām Abū Ḥanīfah Nuʼmān ibn Thābit (d. 150 AH)رحمه الله تعالى

and the principles they use to derive them. This has been the practice of our 2.ShāfiʻīMadhab scholars of the past, and it is extremely

Imām Muḥammad ibn Idrīs ash-Shāfiʿī (d. 204 AH)رحمه الله تعالى

important we do so as well. Assuming 3.MālikīMadhab one has sufficient knowledge and

Imām Mālik ibn Anas (d. 179 AH)رحمه الله تعالىexpertise to determine the correct

ruling at every juncture for themselves 4.ḤanbalīMadhab will lead to inconsistencies, and a

Imām Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal (d. 241 AH)رحمه الله تعالى

person may fall prey to their desires on certain matters.

Khushū' in Ṣalāh

ʻ Khushū in Ṣalāh the will cover terms Khushūʻ In the early days of Islām, the five daily Ṣalāh as we know them were not performed. Then, and Iḥsān, ﷺimprovement of one night, our Messenger Muḥammad was summoned up to the Heavens (called the your prayer, Miʻrāj) for a special gift, and he was welcomed and received through all the Heavens by and angels and prophets alike, before he appeared in front of Allāh to accept the most how to prepare for Ṣalāh.incredible of gifts: the gift of Ṣalāh.

Ṣalāh is the key to success in this life and the hereafter.

As Allāh mentions in the Qurʼān:

Such ʼs omnipresence prayer will act as pitstops in our day-to-day lives, where we can recharge and refocus, as well as provide us with ample opportunity to reflect on any sins we might have committed Omnipresence: the presence of Allāh between prayers. Ṣalāh then will become like the Ṣalāh mentioned in the Ḥadīth of the ʼs knowledge ﷺProphet below, as it will cleanse us of our sins and revitalise our Īmān every time we everywhere at the race to stand in front of Allāh . same time “If there was a river at the door of any one of you and he Khushūʻ: conscious and performative took a bath in it five times a day, would you notice any dirt humility and on him?” devotion in prayer They (the Ṣaḥābah) said, “Not a trace of dirt would be left.” ﷺThe Prophet added, “That is the example of the five prayers with which Allāh blots out evil deeds.”

BUKHĀRĪ

KHUSHŪʻ IN Ṣ Khushūʻ refers to conscious and performative humility and devotion in prayer.

Successful indeed What this means is that a person performing Ṣalāh with Khushūʻ will perform are the believers: it firstly in a way that they are humble in heart and mind, by being conscious of who concentrate who they are worshipping and through their appreciation of Allāh ʼs grandeur in humility when and majesty. Secondly, Khushūʻ is displayed in the personʼs performance of the performing Ṣalāh... prayer with due humility and devotion in their body and actions: their prayer will QURʼĀN 23:1-2be slow and purposeful in all its required conditions. Allāh says: This Āyah mentions that our success as believers is not merely in our ritualistic offering of Ṣalāh, but that our concentration is a condition for that prayer to bring about that success.

Khushūʻ in our Ṣalāh makes us appreciate it as the gift it is, and it removes the idea that it is a burden or task we have to complete. The believer through Khushūʻ will feel spiritually uplifted and emotionally moved through their connection with Allāh , and eventually will come to yearn for the time of Ṣalāh so they can once again converse with their Creator. Allāh says in the Qurʼān: And seek help through patience and Ṣalāh, and truly it is extremely difficult ʻexcept for the ones who have Khushū.

QURʼĀN 2:45

Thus, through our focus and devotion in Ṣalāh, Ṣalāh not only becomes easier for us to perform but also a means of us receiving divine assistance.

KHUSHŪʻ IN Ṣ KHUSHŪʻ BEFORE ṢALĀH ﷺThe Prophet is reported to have said:

…and my joy has been made in Ṣalāh.

AḤMAD

When the time of Ṣalāh approaches, oneʼs heart should beat in excited anticipation ﷺof the coming prayer. Another Ḥadīth mentions that the Prophet would tell

رضي الله عنهBilāl to proclaim Iqāmah so it might soothe his heart in Ṣalāh, saying:

O Bilāl, call Iqāmah for prayer: grant us relief by it.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

ﷺHow incredible is it that the Prophet and the Companions saw their everyday life to be a burden, and Ṣalāh to be a relief from it? For Ṣalāh to be such for us, our worldly should cease the moment the time of prayer arrives, and the Muʼadhdhin calls out the Adhān. We should divert our full attention to the words of the Muʼadhdhin. As we grant passage to the beautiful words of the Adhān to enter our ears and hearts, we should reply to those words by repeating them to ourselves. Following the Adhān, we should recite the Duʻāʼ that follows it. The Adhān should be our call to action. From now, our primary focus is in getting ready for Ṣalāh. Khushūʻ is built up in the actions leading up to the Ṣalāh, and if we build up concentration from the Adhān, it will hopefully reach a peak during our actual prayer.

O Allāh, Owner of this perfect call and Owner of this prayer to be performed, bestow upon Muḥammad al-Wasīlah (a high and special place in Jannah) and al-Faḍīlah (a rank above the rest of creation) and raise him upon a praised platform which You have promised him.

BUKHĀRĪ

KHUSHŪʻ IN ṢALĀH Wuḍūʼ is a great way to prepare for prayer. The washing of the limbs and face WUḌŪʼ refreshes and rejuvenates us, and also serves to remove any dirt, sweat or grime we might have built up over our busy schedules. Even greater than the cleansing aspect is that Wuḍūʼ serves to wipe away our sins and increase our good deeds.

Performing Wuḍūʼ before Ṣalāh is a fantastic opportunity to build our Khushūʻ, but to do so we must perform it in a way that we are attentive to it. Performing it mindlessly will negate its benefits. TO MAINTAIN CONCENTRATION DURING WUḌŪʼ, HERE ARE SOME TIPS YOU MAY CONSIDER:

Begin with 'Bismillāh'.

Use a Siwāk to clean the teeth and gums. It is a Sunnah; it freshens the mouth; and it is pleasing to Allāh .

Avoid talking during Wuḍūʼ.

Wash each limb carefully, following the Sunnah method.

Think about the sins you may have committed with each limb as you wash it and have hope that your washing of that limb is removing that sin.

Bring forth your imagination and try to comprehend who it is you will be standing in front of. This is where the quality of Iḥsān is produced. Imagine you are preparing yourself for the most important meeting of your life.

Remember to recite the Duʻāʼs of Wuḍūʼ.

KHUSHŪʻ IN Ṣ After you have completed your Wuḍūʼ, there are some more things you can do to increase your Khushūʻ before Ṣalāh:

Understanding Ṣalāh

Our Ṣalāh will be elevated manyfold by understanding the Qurʼān. Our concentration in Ṣalāh is aided by us understanding what we are reading, and being aware of the context of the verses. In particular, knowing of those Sūrahs and verses which are commonly recited by ourselves and Imāms in Masājid, will go a long way in keeping our attention the translation cover fixed in our Ṣalāh. One should try to commit those of Sūrah al-Fātiḥah & meanings to memory, so as it is read, the meaning is the last ten Sūrahs, understood alongside it. the meanings of individual words, and the themes behind the revelation of each Sūrah.

the accursedShayṭānfromin AllāhI seek refuge I seek refuge in Allāh from the accursed Shayṭān S We ask Allāh for refuge from the devil, as we alone are unable to guarantee our safety from the whispers of Shayṭān who, with his manipulative tricks may lead us astray. Much like how we might ask the owner of a dog to leash their hound if we feel unsafe around it, we ask Allāh  to protect us against Shayṭān, and without doubt, with Allāh ʼs protection, Shayṭān will have no power over us. Our Ṣalāh begins with Taʻawwudh as we ask Allāh to keep Shayṭān away from us so that he cannot divert our thoughts, and we can maintain concentration in Ṣalāh.

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ TASMIYAH �سْبِ�

مِ�هِللا

The Very MercifulThe All-MercifulAllāhIn the Name of In the Name of Allāh, the All-Merciful, the Very Merciful S We begin, as we do in all actions, with the name of Allāh . We begin with the name of Allāh so that we may have Barakah (divine blessings) in what we are about to do. We begin with the name of Allāh to clarify our intentions, and we begin with the name of Allāh  to ask Him for help in the matter at hand.

Indeed, no task should be undertaken, journey begun, worship commenced, food eaten, or pleasure enjoyed without the name of Allāh uttered before it. Bismillāh should be our simplest and most common form of remembrance, but should reflect our utter and deepest love and Tawakkul (reliance) upon our Creator.

Bismillāh incorporates two of Allāh  most oft-used names which He loves to be remembered by, and through our utterance of it, reminds us that our Lord, the Ever-Merciful, is always with us.

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ َأّ�ٱَْْْ�

َ�مٰهنَٰلعَ تَمَٰعٰنِانِ�دِّلاطارِصِ�ِِِ

مٰهنَٰلعَ۝نَيْلاصِِلاالوبِوَُصََّعمَٰلار�عَ

those upon whom ūare they astrayand neitherupon whomnot there is anger The path of those You have bestowed ūYour favours upon, those upon whom there is neither anger nor are they astray The Opening; The Mother of the Book; The Cure; are all names of the same short chapter. These are the 'seven oft- repeated verses', recited by every Muslim in every unit of every prayer. The Fātiḥah is a comprehensive supplication which begins, as all supplications and Duās should, with the praise of Allāh . The supplication continues with the affirmation of worshipping Allāh , and Allāh alone, before asking for assistance, guidance, and salvation from becoming like those who incurred Allāh ʼs wrath and went astray by disregarding the guidance given to them.

The believer asks Allāh for guidance everyday through Sūrah al-Fātiḥah, and though they may be upon the guidance, they still ask for it so that they may be granted Istiqāmah: steadfastness and the maintenance of piety and devoutness.

They also plead to be made part of the company of those whom Allāh had favoured, and thus seek the higher stages of spirituality and divine closeness to the Creator. The beauty of Sūrah al-Fātiḥah is seen in its simple yet wholly comprehensive form, as it encompasses in seven verses the main themes found in the entire Qurʼān: Tawḥīd (the oneness of Allāh ), Risālah, Aḥkām (laws), Ākhirah (the hereafter), the Muʼminūn (believers), and the Kuffār (disbelievers). It is for this reason amongst others it is considered the essence of the Qurʼān, and why it holds such high regard.

ﷺThe Messenger of Allāh said that Allāh the Exalted had said:

I have divided the prayer into two halves between Me and My servant, and My servant will receive what he asks.

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ ﷺThe final Sūrah of the Qurʼān begins like the two preceding it, with an order from Allāh to the Prophet to recite certain verses. This Sūrah is also similar to the one directly before it, in that it includes Taʻawwudh (seeking protection  in Allāh from Shayṭān).

The Sūrah begins with mentioning three attributes of Allāh , and it is in these three attributes we are told to seek Allāh ʼs protection. These three attributes directly relate to what is mentioned later in the Sūrah, as it is firm belief in these qualities of Allāh which offer salvation from the whispers of Shayṭān, and the evil of man and Jinn. Allāh is described as: THE GOD THE LORD AND THE MASTER OF ALLSUSTAINER OF ALLOF ALL The first verse references Allāh as 'Rabb', which relates to Allāh being lord over everything, but also the active Sustainer of everyone and everything. He provides for all, regardless of their belief in him. The second verse references Allāh as 'Malik', that He is truly the only Sovereign Power above all. Allāh ʼs Kingdom and Dominion encompasses all which is in the Heavens and Earth, and all are subjects to Him, including the Shayāṭīn.

The third verse mentions how Allāh is the God of all people, and this is regardless of allegiance in this life, for they accepted once prior, and they will definitely accept again in the life to come. This includes those devilish of men and Jinn, as they recognise their true Creator, but it is only due to arrogance that they purposefully reject Him. The Sūrah then continues to the things from which one should seek protection, namely from the whispers of the 'Khannās'. The word in Arabic comes from a root word which means 'to sneak, recede or withdraw stealthily'. The habit of Shayṭān is that when a person is engaged in the remembrance of Allāh , and is active in worship, Shayṭān withdraws.

Then, when the same person becomes heedless, and ceases in their remembrance of their Lord, Shayṭān returns to whisper his evil on the heart of such a person.

  • Always be careful of Shayṭān. Rasūlullāh ﷺ warned,

Indeed, Shayṭān runs through the body of man as blood flows through the veins.

MUSLIM

  • Shayṭān will whisper within everyone and cause all to have evil thoughts. The presence of spontaneous

evil thoughts does not make a person sinful, it is only when a person decides to act upon it that they will be sinful.

  • The Sūrah teaches us that Shayṭān has no power over a person so long as they are continuous in their

Duʻāʼ, and their remembrance of Allāh . One has nothing to fear from Shayṭān so long as they are connected to their Lord, the Lord of Shayṭān and all mankind and Jinn.

•In Sūrah al-Fātiḥah we asked Allāh for guidance, and the entire Qurʼān is filled with that guidance. The last two Sūrahʼs speak of seeking Allāh ʼs protection from Shayṭān, as a person can still be distracted and removed from the right path through the whispers of Shayṭān. We are as in need of guidance from Allāh  as we are in need of his protection from those things which will distract us from following his guidance.

SŪRAH AL-FALAQ - THE DAYBREAK

ََُْْٱأ� بِرَّ�لُقَ۝قَُلْ�ْلادوَُ�ا�

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ The penultimate Sūrah of the Qurʼān is named after the daybreak, and whilst it was revealed in reference to an incident ﷺin the life of the Prophet , it should be recited by every Muslim for protection.

ﷺThe Sūrah was revealed when, for a period of time, Rasūlullāh would misremember or forget things pertaining to ﷺworldly matters. He prayed to Allāh for help, and the Ḥadīth mentions what happened next:

Two men came to me and one of them sat near my head and the other near my feet. One of them said to his companion, "What is the disease of this man?" The other replied, "He is under the effect of magic.” The first one asked, “Who has worked the magic on him?” The other replied, "Labīd ibn al-Aʼṣam.ʼ The first one asked, “What material did he use?” The other replied, “A comb and the hairs stuck to it and the skin of pollen of a male date palm.” The first one asked, “Where is that?” The other replied, “(That is) in the well of Dharwān.”

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺThe Prophet ordered for the removal of the items of magic, and then ordered for the well to be covered up. Following this incident, he would recite the last two Sūrahs for protection as well.

 The Sūrah begins with a command of Taʻawwudh (seeking protection in Allāh ), and the attribute of Allāh mentioned here is of Him being the Lord of the Daybreak or Morning. The morning shows the passing of time and the coming of a new day, and one who is so powerful to bring that into being, surely is worthy of having His protection sought. From the second verse, those things from which one should seek protection are mentioned. In the second verse, we seek protection from the evil of the creation. The Āyah tells us that the evil is within the creation, and this verse should give us reassurance as we know that the Creator can easily protect us from the harm of that which He has complete control over. The evil in this verse may refer to Jahannam, Iblīs (Shayṭān) and those of the Jinn and mankind who are inclined towards evil. This verse is general, and the following verses are more specific. The third verse speaks on the evil of the night, under whose blanket many evils are committed. The night brings darkness, and cover for the evil of mankind, Jinn and animals. In this verse, we seek protection in Allāh from evil which we cannot see and which seeks to affect us from places we do not know. The fourth and fifth verses refer to specific kinds of evil of people. The fourth Āyah describes sorceresses and their magic, ﷺparticularly their blowing into knots. This directly references what happened to the Prophet , and how he was affected. For safety and protection from any similar kind of evil, we should recite Sūrah al-Falaq as well. The last verse speaks about the evil of a very common trait: envy. The first crimes committed, that of Qābīl on Hābīl, were committed in envy. Furthermore, the evil it brings through the evil eye is mentioned in Ḥadīth. We should use this Sūrah for protection from envy, but also take active steps to ensure we do not become subject to envy, by avoiding any unnecessary show of wealth or success, and keeping the bounties given by Allāh private.

  • The Messenger of Allāh ﷺ was affected by the evil of another. If he, despite his status, can be affected by

the evil of another, so can we. The effect of the evil was removed only through Allāh ʼs help, and we should remember that any evil can be countered, so long as Allāh  is on our side. Therefore, we ought  to trust in Allāh wholeheartedly.

  • We should make a habit to recite the last three Sūrahʼs every night and morning, and if possible, after
  • Envy is a powerful force within people. Never post or show off what Allāh  has given you, as not all will

SŪRAH AL-IKHLĀṢ - SINCERITY the Oneūis AllāhHeSay Say, ūO Prophet, “He is Allāh – The One” The Independent MasterAllāh Allāh – The Independent Master

۝دِّلوَُنِدِّلَّٰتُ�مٰلو�مٰل

He was bornand notHe gives birthNot He neither gave birth, nor was He born to

۝دحِااوَُ�ُكُهِلنِكْيَمٰلو�

ūany oneequivalentfor himisAnd not and none is comparable to Him

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ One of the key themes of the Qurʼān, and purposes of prophethood is the establishment of Tawḥīd. The belief in Allāh ʼs oneness and that He is the only one worthy of worship is a key tenet of our faith and belief, and it is a concept emphasised in the Qurʼān. This Sūrah is a concise statement of that belief, and it encompasses it in the simplest of terms.

ﷺSūrah al-Ikhlāṣ begins with a command to the Prophet to say, and this was in response to the polytheists of Makkah ﷺasking the Messenger to detail the lineage of Allāh . To this, Allāh replies, He is Allāh , the One. Allāh is one in His attributes, His being, His uniqueness, His power and might, and He is the one above all else. He is one in that he has no partners, and none resemble Him.

The second verse mentions that He is aṣ-Ṣamad. Ṣamad means independent or self-sufficient, and Allāh is a being which is in need of none other for existence, sustenance or assistance, and all are in need of Him. Allāh does not need our worship and obedience, and His majesty is not increased in the slightest from our offerings. We, however, are dependent on Allāh , not only for our existence and sustenance, but also for worship. It befits mankind that they are engaged in worship and gratitude towards their Creator, and thus, where Allāh is self-sufficient, He is also sufficient for us.

The final two verses are direct responses to the questions of the Quraysh of Makkah, and Allāh states clearly that he has no children, nor was he the child of any other being. Attributing lineage, or the quality of being born, and thus dependency, infancy, childhood and time to Allāh would be to attribute a change in Allāh ʼs state, which is a weakness, and Allāh has none such weaknesses. Allāh denies any dependency for His existence, and denies that He might ever beget children.

The last verse speaks of Allāh ʼs uniqueness, and that there is none equal to Him. Allāh does not have an equal, in any sense. He is alone, and He is the only one worthy of our worship. His attributes are also unique, and in every attribute of Allāh there is no equal or any being with a similarity to Him. Every share in a quality of Allāh by any of the creation is imperfect, and Allāh ʼs quality is absolute and perfect. For example, whilst the creation can know, they can only know imperfectly, and only Allāh can know perfectly. The creation may see, but their sight is limited, and Allāh  sees all.

S ﷺ•Rasūlullāh said:

ʻProclaim: “Say: He is Allāh, the One” (Sūrah al-Ikhlāṣ) and Al-Muawwidhatayn (Sūrah an- Nās and Sūrah al-Falaq), when you reach evening, and when you reach morning, three times, they will suffice you against everything.

TIRMIDHĪ

  • Sūrah al-Ikhlāṣ negates all forms of Shirk (ascribing partners with Allāh ) and establishes the oneness

of Allāh . Our belief in Allāh  should be that He is One, and that He is the only one we call upon for aid and help.

  • Sūrah al-Ikhlāṣ has a depth of meaning despite being a very short and concise chapter. This Sūrah shows

us the importance of delving deep into the meanings of the Qurʼān, and how much we can gain from doing so.

SŪRAH AL-MASAD - THE PALM FIBRE

palm fibrefromūwill be a ropeHer neckIn Around her neck there is a rope of twisted palm-fibre

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ ﷺIn the first three years of Prophethood, Rasūlullāh kept the Dīn of Islām private and only preached to those people he ﷺwas confident would accept his invitation to the faith. Then, Allāh commanded His Messenger to call the Quraysh to Islām.

ﷺHe stood on top of the Mount Ṣafā, and called upon the tribes of Quraysh. When they had assembled, he asked them whether they would believe him if he were to inform them that there was an army behind the mountain about to ﷺﷺattack them. They replied in the affirmative, as they knew of Rasūlullāh ʼs reputation as a truthful man. He then proclaimed to them the purpose of gathering them, “I warn you of a terrible torment. Save yourselves from the fire.” ﷺAbū Lahab, whose real name was ʻAbdul ʻUzzā and was one of the uncles of the Messenger stood and said, “May you be destroyed ūO Muḥammad!, is this why you have gathered us?” On this statement, and due to his outright rejection of ﷺthe faith, and his consequent attacks on the Messenger and the believers, Allāh revealed this Sūrah.

Allāh curses Abū Lahab in the first verse, stating that he will be destroyed. Allāh references his hands to mean his work and efforts, as well as a representation of the entire body as we perform most of our tasks with our hands. Indeed, as Allāh had predicted, Abū Lahab would see himself succumb to a terrible disease after the Battle of Badr, which would result in him suffering a horrible death. For three days, no one would touch his body and only after it began to decompose, some slaves moved it with sticks and pushed it into a hole to be filled with rocks. The next verse refutes a belief of his, that his wealth and children may aid him against punishment if the religion of Islām is true. Allāh rejects this notion entirely, and in the following verse we are told of his impending punishment in the hereafter. The first two verses spoke of his worldly destruction, and the third verse details his coming punishment. Allāh  chose to use a word from his title (Lahab) as well to describe the punishment he will receive, which humiliated him further. The last two verses are about Abū Lahabʼs wife, Umm Jamīl. She is described as a carrier of firewood, which could refer to her being a tale bearer as tale bearing is akin to lighting fires of hatred between families. It may also relate to her ﷺcarrying material to place in the path of the Prophet to cause him difficulty and pain, or that in Jahannam, she will carry firewood to increase her husbandʼs punishment. She will be bound with a rope, and how she wore necklaces of jewellery in this life, she will wear necklaces of disgrace and punishment in the hereafter. This Sūrah also contains a prophesising miracle. It effectively predicts that Abū Lahab would die as a disbeliever, as the curse of hellfire for him could only be true if he dies as such. So, if Abū Lahab only turned around and accepted Islām, he  would have shown the words of the Qurʼān to be untrue. However, Allāh had not written guidance for him for what he had done, and the prophecy of the Qurʼān is that he would remain a disbeliever remained true.

  • Rasūlullāh ﷺ began with preaching privately, starting from his own home expanding outwards. The

stages of rectification for when one sees wrong is to begin with oneself, then move to those closest, and then further on.

  • Rasūlullāh ﷺ preached openly to his people. This is the responsibility of our Messenger ﷺ, and of this

Ummah. We have a role to play in calling others to Islām, through our words, actions, and character.

  • A married couple should be partners in good, rather than in evil and sin. Good company is also extremely
  • The Messenger of Allāh ﷺ is Allāh ʼs beloved, and those who choose to insult the Messenger of Allāh ﷺ

SŪRAH AN-NAṢR - THE DIVINE ASSISTANCE َْٱَٱ�َْ

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ This chapter is titled 'The Divine Assistance', for the help and support Allāh gave the Muslims against the Quraysh of Makkah through the years leading up to the eventual conquest of Makkah, and for the support Allāh had given His ﷺMessenger over the course of his life and the period of Prophethood.

The Sūrah begins with mention of Allāh ʼs help and 'The Victory'. This victory is commonly known to be referring to the conquest of Makkah, after which Allāh opened the doors of Islām to the various tribes of Arabia. This is indicated to in the second verse, where Allāh mentions how people are accepting the religion of Islām in crowds. Though many knew of the truth of Islām prior to the conquest of Makkah, they only chose to accept Islām after.

 ﷺAllāh then instructs the Prophet to glorify Him, and to seek His forgiveness, and Allāh ends the Sūrah with a name from His beautiful names: at-Tawwāb (the Most Forgiving). This Sūrah alludes to the ﷺapproaching demise of Rasūlullāh , as the acceptance of Islām by the people signifies the completion of his mission.

Furthermore, it is at the completion of a task that a person should ask forgiveness for the ﷺshortcomings in his efforts, and Allāh instructing Rasūlullāh to glorify Him and ask for forgiveness alludes to the ﷺclosing stages of the Prophet ʼs worldly life.

ﷺ Our belief is that the Messenger of Allāh is without sin, as are all Prophets. Where Allāh instructs His beloved to seek forgiveness here is not for any sin, but rather for the imperfection of actions done for Allāh , as every action done for Him is in reality deficient when considering His Greatness and Majesty.

  • We should also make a habit of glorifying Allāh  and asking for forgiveness at the end of discharging

any religious duty, as we undoubtedly would not have been able to complete it to the degree of perfection deserving of Allāh .

  • Allāh ʼs divine assistance is with the believers, and one should never lose hope when performing

any good, or starting something with the intention of spreading good. If at first it fails, then one should ﷺremember the life and perseverance of our Messenger , and how Allāh ʼs help reached him.

  • Our every success should be attributed to Allāh  and Allāh  alone. It is only through His assistance

that we may achieve something notable, and we should attribute to Him what He deserves. Glorifying Him, thanking Him, and seeking His forgiveness will ensure our continued success in this life, and guarantee our success in the hereafter.

SŪRAH AL KĀFIRŪN - THE DISBELIEVERS

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ ﷺAfter some years of the Messenger of Allāh preaching in Makkah, the disbelievers came to him with a compromise.

ﷺThey offered, in exchange that the Prophet cease preaching, that they will worship Allāh for a year if he worshipped their gods for a year, and they will alternate annually to remove the strife between them. To this, Allāh revealed this Sūrah.

In this chapter, Allāh mentions the clearest distinction between Īmān (belief) and Kufr (disbelief), repeating twice that ﷺthere will not be, and never will there be any worshipping of their false gods. Rasūlullāh is commanded to tell them in no uncertain terms that there will be no compromise in the religion of Islām, and that this will remain the case for all time. The Sūrah begins with the address directly to the disbelievers of Makkah, though this may be directed at anyone who ﷺseeks to dilute the truth of Īmān and Islām with Kufr and Shirk. Rasūlullāh is ordered then to address them as they are, and to tell them that he refuses their offer and will not worship what they worship.

ﷺThe chapter then continues by mentioning that they (the disbelievers) will not worship what he worships. This is a prophecy in itself to certain members of the Quraysh that they would die upon their disbelief disgraced and humiliated.

It also responds to their offer, that it is not possible for you to worship Allāh whilst also worshipping another deity or idol. This verse and the one before it is then repeated to emphasise the point, that worship of Allāh was never compromised, and will never be compromised with worship of anything else.

 Allāh ends the Sūrah with the powerful verse that maintains the definitive line between the religion of truth, and falsehood: “For you is your religion; for me, mine.” S

  • We should have a similar distinction in our lives between Īmān and Kufr, and our reaction to any call to

disbelief should be a very firm answer: “For you is your belief, and for me is mine”.

  • Our identity as Muslims and people of faith should be strong, and our belief should be firm. If we are ever

presented with Ḥarām, the strength of our belief should lead us to state our position proudly and firmly, and we should refuse to commit to something prohibited.

  • There is no compromise in our religion. We should never let anyone dilute our teachings, or ruin our

SŪRAH AL-KAWTHAR - THE ABUNDANCE آ�أَّ�

۝رَّ�وَُكُلاا�اإكـٰيْٰتَظ�ْ�ا

al-KawtharWe have given youIndeed, We Indeed, ūO Prophet, We have given to you al-Kawthar.

كتُرَّٰللُصِْقَ۝رََّحَبِاو�ِ

and sacrificeto your LordSo, pray So, pray to your Lord and sacrifice

ّْأٱَََُ وَُهُ�اإ۝ر�تُالاكٰ��اشِ�ِ

the one cut offhe ūisṣyour enemyIndeed Indeed, it is your enemy who is truly cut off When you next pray your Ṣalāh, reflect on the translation of each part. Check to see how much you can recall.

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ Sūrah al-Kawthar contains glad tidings, two commands, praise, prophecy, response to mockery and humiliation for the disbelievers, all in three short verses of equal length, and in eloquent poetic rhyme. It is a miraculous Sūrah of the Qurʼān for its eloquence and depth of meaning, which is composed into an incredibly short yet comprehensive chapter. The Qurʼān challenges the disbelievers on multiple occasions to produce even a chapter similar to one in the Qurʼān, and they were unable to produce anything, even a chapter as short as this Sūrah. The Sūrah was revealed to respond to the taunts of the Quraysh upon the passing of the ﷺMessenger ʼs son, as they argued that the only way the religion of Islām and his lifeʼs work would continue when he passed away would be through male heirs. They taunted the ﷺProphet by saying that he and his progeny are 'cut off', and will bear no significance in generations to come. To this Allāh replied that in reality it was the disbelievers ﷺwho would be 'cut off', and that the Prophet and his message would live on, a prophecy the truthfulness of which we are the evidence.

ﷺThe Sūrah begins with Allāh consoling Rasūlullāh with the gift of al- Kawthar, which could mean many things, including and yet not limited to: the fountain of Kawthar which will benefit his followers on the Day of Judgement; Prophethood; the honour of being the best of the Prophets; the largest Ummah; intercession on the Day of Qiyāmah, and much more. This gift was ﷺa source of comfort for the Messenger , and reiterates the station the ﷺMessenger enjoys as the greatest of Prophets.

ﷺThe second verse commands Rasūlullāh to perform Ṣalāh and offer animal sacrifice. Ṣalāh is the highest form of worship, and sacrifice is the best of monetary worship. They are also two forms of worship performed by many Prophets before, and in this is an indication to the Prophet ﷺ of his noble lineage in prophethood. The Sūrah ends with the verse responding to the Quraysh, and the prophecy which promises their destruction and the continued flourishing of Islām and the efforts of ﷺRasūlullāh after his death.

  • Ṣalāh is a foundational pillar, and even in a Sūrah as concise as Sūrah al-Kawthar, mention is made of

this incredible act of worship. Our lives should revolve around our Ṣalāh, and we should make efforts to improve our prayer to the point of perfection.

  • The enemies of the Prophet ﷺ insulted him during his blessed life, and others continued after his passing.

Nevertheless, there is no person more fondly remembered and loved, about whom as much has been written, and whose example so many follow as the Messenger ﷺ. His detractors have found nothing but disgrace, and in the hereafter a greater punishment awaits them. As Allāh  says, Surely We suffice to deal with those who mock you.

QURʼĀN 15:95

SŪRAH AL-MĀʻŪN - THE LITTLE ACTS OF KINDNESS َٱَّّٱَ ّ��أْْ�ََْ

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ

۝�وَُ�امَٰلا�وَُعٰتَْمَيْو�

the small kindnessesAnd they deny and refuse to give ūeven the simplest aid Sūrah al-Māʻūn details four evil actions of disbelievers and hypocrites, for which they will be punished for eternity. This Sūrah is also for us as Muslims, informing us that it is below the standard of a believer to do any of the actions mentioned. The first verse opens with a question, as to whether one has seen those who reject and deny the day of Qiyāmah. Allāh  uses the word Dīn here, which could also mean religion, as they have rejected the true message. Both meanings may apply, as the Qurʼān is such that in many places a word will be used with two or multiple meanings, and all are relevant to the context.

Allāh then mentions qualities of such a person, that they repel the orphan, and do not encourage the feeding of the poor. A person who does not believe in a day of recompense where their good and bad will be weighed will not feel the need for good deeds, nor care for their attitude to those they consider beneath them.

Allāh mentions orphans and encouraging the feeding of the poor to emphasise the hard-heartedness of such people, as orphans often need kindness and love more than anything which costs nothing, and encouraging others to feed is also without cost when one cannot feed themselves. Furthermore, such a person may be so miserly that let alone spending themselves, they cannot even bring themselves to encourage others.

Allāh then mentions those who perform Ṣalāh seeing it as a burden, performing it lazily and carelessly. This verse is explicitly about the hypocrites, as Allāh continues that they perform Ṣalāh only to be seen by others. The hypocrite will perform good actions to please others, and will have no sincerity in their actions. For such people, Allāh promises destruction. The Sūrah ends with a verse stating that those described above are people who withhold even the smallest of kindnesses.

The word Allāh uses is used to refer to small and simple actions or things which may benefit another, and one would not be affected from giving or doing. It could also be a reference to Zakāh, as it is only a small proportion of oneʼs wealth, and the hypocrites found it very difficult to give.

  • As Muslims we need to ensure we do not have the qualities mentioned in the Sūrah. These are qualities

of disbelievers and hypocrites, and this chapter is a manual of sorts of what we should not do or become.

•Sincerity should be the essence of every action. We should not do anything except for Allāh ʼs sake. it was a quality of the hypocrites that they would perform actions for people, rather than for Allāh .

  • We should not hesitate in performing even the slightest or smallest of good deeds. Being miserly on small

acts of charity, whether that be through words, money, action, or kindness is the quality of a disbeliever. We should open our hearts for everyone to benefit.

  • Our Ṣalāh should be performed with Khushūʻ, and we should be extremely particular about performing it

SŪRAH AL-QURAYSH - THE QURAYSH

۝شٍبِرَّقَفُـٰلتُال�ِ�إِ

ūof the QurayshFor ūthe familiarity Because of the familiarity of the Quraysh �َٱَّٱَ

مٰهقَـٰلاإ۝فُْتَٰصَِّلاوءٍاٰتَٰهِلَّٰحِرَسَّلاِ�ِِ

and summerūof winterūwith the journeyTheir familiarity that is, their familiarity with the trips of winter and summer

بِرَادْهُ۝تَيْْيْلا�اودٰتَٰعْيْلَقَ

houseūof thisūthe LordSo, they must worship So, they must worship the Lord of this ūSacred House

ّْأٱُّْ عوََحَنِمِ�ِمْهمَٰعظطَايْدِّلا

ūagainst hungerūfromṣhas fed themthe One who fearfromand gives them security the One who has fed them against hunger and made them secure against fear

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ The Quraysh were a noble tribe whom Allāh had chosen as the inhabitants of the city of Makkah, and from whom He ﷺhad sent the final Messenger . Prior to the advent of Islām, the Quraysh were known for their hospitality, nobility in lineage and character, and for the fact that they were custodians of the Ḥaram. In Sūrah al-Quraysh, Allāh enumerates His bounties upon them for them to reflect upon and as proofs to convince them that He is truly worthy of worship. The first two verses refer to the travels of the Quraysh, where in the summer they would travel to Syria and in the winter, to Yemen. Due to Makkah being geographically isolated without much vegetation, fruits, vegetables, and other food,  they would need to be brought to Makkah from other regions. Allāh enabled the Quraysh to travel safely for business to purchase these commodities, by which they became very wealthy. This was a favour of Allāh upon them, and the

عليه السلامfulfilment of the Duʻāʼ of Ibrāhīm .

The next verse alludes to another favour which they had been given in that they were custodians of the Ḥaram, and they had been given nobility through the Kaʻbah. It follows naturally that as custodians of the House of Allāh which gives them honour, they ought to worship only Allāh in gratitude, and this verse instructs them to do so. The final verse references two further bounties which Allāh had given them: Allāh saved them from hunger, and granted them safety from any kind of fear. The first part refers to the fact that despite Makkah being barren, they were fed by every kind of food, and also to the fact that they were hosted by various tribes on their journeys who fed them and gave them lodging due to their nobility. The second part refers to their safety and security, as they were spared from attacks on their travels due to their stature in the eyes of others, and also for the safety of Makkah, in that it was given divine protection from enemies, like in the famous incident mentioned in Sūrah al-Fīl.

  • Allāh  had blessed the Quraysh with so many favours and bounties, for which they should have

showed gratitude to Allāh . In our lives, we should contemplate over the bounties that Allāh  has given us, and reflect over how much gratitude we show Him.

•A person being blessed with favours from Allāh is not a sign of their acceptance in Allāh ʼs court, nor is being deprived of worldly things a sign of being distanced from Allāh . We should not look at wealth as indicators to piety, and adopt the two methods we have been given for prosperity and austerity: Ṣabr (perseverance) during hard times, and Shukr (gratitude) during easy times.

SŪRAH AL-FĪL - THE ELEPHANT

ِ�۝لُٰتََحَسِنِمِةَرَاْخَْحَبِمٰهنَمِرَّ��ٍ�ِِِ�ِ

۝لِوَُكامِفُْصََّعْكُمْهٰلٰعَخَفَ�ٍ

eaten uplike strawThen He made them Then He made them like chewed up straw

UNDERSTANDING Ṣ This Sūrah recounts the famous tale of the elephants of the viceroy Abrahah, who had set out from Yemen to destroy the Kaʻbah because he considered it a rival to a religious pilgrimage site he had built himself. When he approached Makkah, the Quraysh were powerless to stop him as the army he commanded, complete with a contingent of elephants, was too strong to defeat. The Quraysh retreated away from the city in fear, and left Makkah hoping for a miracle. Allāh protected Makkah by sending birds with stones that were dropped on the army with such force that it reduced them to what resembles straw chewed by animals and spat back out. The chapter begins with a question that is directed primarily at the Quraysh, as they were witnesses to this event and benefactors of Allāh ʼs protection. Allāh chooses to direct the question at them to remind them of His favour upon them, and so that they may see the futility in ascribing partners to Him, and come to worship Him alone. Interestingly, the year of the elephants ﷺcoincides with the year the Prophet was born, and there is an indication to the Quraysh receiving two incredible gifts at one time from Allāh .

Sūrah al-Fīl highlights Allāh ʼs Power and Might, as He uses small and seemingly harmless birds carrying similarly RED SEAharmless pebbles to destroy a ARABIAN PENINSULA frightening army YEMEN of huge animals, as if to show that it matters not what the creation plans, intends or  utilises, but Allāh ultimately can bring any plan to naught with even the most harmless of means.

  • This Sūrah should bring us to recognise the power, might and majesty of Allāh , which should firstly

bring with it a fear of Allāh ʼs punishment, but also a sense of peace with the knowledge that when Allāh is on our side, there is nothing that can harm us, and we will eventually be victorious.

  • Anyone who dares to disrespect Allāh , any of His signs, or any of His beloved servants ultimately

will meet their ruin, either in this world or the next. We should be very careful about these matters, and ensure that we do not extend our joking to them. Making fun of Allāh ʼs signs, even if done without seriousness, can lead to severe repercussions for a person.

Nawāfil Ṣalāh

some of the voluntary prayers and the benefits A Muslim is required to perform five obligatory prayers daily and doing so draws of performing them, them closer to their Lord. Besides the obligatory prayers, however, there are understand their certain voluntary or optional prayers (Nawāfil) which take a person to a stage importance reflect , and beyond what can be reached by only performing what is compulsory. If the five on which prayers you can Ṣalāh are the walls of a house and its roof, then the Sunnah prayers are its doors include in your life. and windows, and the other voluntary prayers are its furniture and decoration.

On the spiritual level, voluntary prayers give us access to Allāh whenever our hearts desire, and they ought to be used to make Duʻāʼ and ask Allāh .

ﷺRasūlullāh said, Nafl (pl. Nawāfil): The nearest a servant comes to his Lord is when he is optional action of worship.prostrating himself, so be plentiful in supplication.

MUSLIM

Khushūʻ: conscious and performative humility and devotion in prayer. of Ḥadīth where the words were mentioned by the ﷺProphet , but the meaning is from .Allāh Furthermore, they also function as stepping stones to making our obligatory prayers even better. It is in optional Khushūʻprayers that our is built and maintained, and it is in them that we gain a unique station in front of Allāh .

I will declare war against he who shows hostility to My pious worshippers. My servant does not draw near to Me with anything more beloved to Me than what I have made obligatory on him. And a servant continues to draw near to Me through voluntary acts of worship ūNawāfil until I love him. And when I love him, I become the hearing with which he hears, the sight with which he sees, the hand with which he grips and the leg with which he walks. And if he asks from Me, I give him. And if he asks My protection, I protect him.

(ḤADĪTH QUDSĪ) BUKHĀRĪ

NAWĀFIL Ṣ Nawāfil also serve to compensate our Farḍ Ṣalāh if they are found to be deficient.

ﷺThe Prophet mentions this in a Ḥadīth in which he says that:

…on the Day of Judgement, the first deed that people will be summoned to account for will be prayer. Our Lord, the Exalted, will say to the angels - though He knows better: Examine the prayer of My servant and see whether he has offered it perfectly or imperfectly. If it is perfect, it will be recorded as perfect. However, if it is defective, He will say: See if there are some voluntary prayers offered by My servant. If there are voluntary prayers to his credit, He will say: Compensate the obligatory prayer with the voluntary prayer for My servant. Then all the actions will be considered similarly.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

In relation to this, a good way to ensure we build up a healthy bank of voluntary prayers is to connect every Farḍ prayer with its respective voluntary prayers. This is generally not too difficult to do as it is only a matter of a few minutes before and after, and we are in the state to perform Ṣalāh anyway.

RULES FOR VOLUNTARY PRAYERS There are not many rules for voluntary prayers, and in fact, some conditions which exist for Farḍ prayers are removed for Nafl prayers. The important rule to bear in mind is not to perform any voluntary prayer in a forbidden or disliked prayer time (e.g. during sunrise, or after having performed the ʻAṣr prayer). Besides that, one may perform prayers to oneʼs heartʼs content.

SUNAN ﷺThe Prophet of Allāh said:

ʻWhoever performs ūthese 12 Rakāt in a day and night, a house will be built for him in Jannah: four before Ẓuhr, and two after it; two after ʻMaghrib; two after Ishāʼ; and two before Fajr.

NASĀʼĪ

ﷺThese are known as the Sunnah Muʼakkadah (emphasised), and they were consistently performed by Rasūlullāh .

Besides the above, it is also Sunnah to perform four Rakʻāt before ʻAṣr and four Rakʻāt before ʻIshāʼ. These are the Sunnah Ghayr Muʼakkadah (non-emphasised).

TAHAJJUD Tahajjud is the most famous and most virtuous of Nafl prayers. In various places of the Qurʼān, Allāh describes his closest servants, and in many of those places, he references their spending of a part of the night in His remembrance as a reason for their closeness. Allāh says: ūThe servants of the Merciful are those who spend a good portion of the night, prostrating themselves and standing before their Lord.

QURʼĀN 25:64

ﷺLikewise, the Prophet is reported to have said: The most excellent of prayer is that which is offered in the depth of the night.

MUSLIM

Tahajjud is best offered in the latter part of the night, where one wakes up after having slept but one may perform it at any time after the Farḍ of ʻIshāʼ till the time of Fajr begins (Ṣubḥ Ṣādiq). After performing Tahajjud, one may go

عليه السلامﷺback to sleep before eventually waking up for Fajr. This was the practice of Dāwūd which the Prophet called

the 'most beloved prayer' in the sight of Allāh . It is also a time for supplication and asking for forgiveness, as illustrated in the beautiful Ḥadīth: Our Lord, blessed and pure, descends to the nearest heaven every night when only the last third of the night remains, saying, “Is there anyone to plead to Me, so that I may respond to his plea? Is there anyone to ask Me, that I may grant him his request? Is there anyone begging for forgiveness, that I may pardon him?

BUKHĀRĪ

Tahajjud consists of 2 to 12 Rakʻāt in units of 2.

NAWĀFIL Ṣ ISHRĀQ ﷺThe Ishrāq prayer can be performed 15 minutes following sunrise, until the mid-morning. The Prophet said:

Whoever performs Fajr in congregation, then sits remembering ʻAllāh until the sun has risen, then he performs two Rakāt, for ʻhim is the reward like that of a Ḥajj and an Umrah.

TIRMIDHĪ

Ishrāq consists of 2 or 4 Rakʻāt, in units of 2.

ḌUḤĀ Ṣalāh aḍ-Ḍuḥā is the forenoon prayer, often performed at the midway point between sunrise and noon. It is a ﷺprayer with a great reward, and the Prophet not only performed it himself but encouraged others to do so as

رضي الله عنهwell. Abū Hurayrah says that:

ﷺMy friend (the Prophet ) advised me ūto do three things:

ʻfasting three days every month; performing two Rakāt of the forenoon prayer; and observing Witr before going to sleep.

MUSLIM

Ṣalāh aḍ-Ḍuḥā consists of 2 to 12 Rakʻāt in units of 2, but one may perform more than 8.

TAḤIYYAT AL-WUḌŪʼ One should try and perform Wuḍūʼ fully with all its Sunnah actions, and then follow that with two Rakʻāt of Ṣalāh, ﷺexcept during the forbidden and disliked prayer times. The Prophet is reported to have said:

Whoever performs Wuḍūʼ like this Wuḍūʼ of mine and then offers ʻtwo Rakāt in which he does not think of worldly things ūi.e. performs them with concentration, all his previous sins will be forgiven.

BUKHĀRĪ

Taḥiyyat al-Wuḍūʼ consists of two Rakʻāt.

TAḤIYYAT AL-MASJID Pick out certain Nafl This prayer is performed whenever a person enters the Masjid, except Ṣalāh to perform ﷺduring the forbidden and disliked prayer times. The Prophet said: and log how many If anyone of you enters a Masjid, he should you perform over a period of six weeks ʻperform two Rakāt before sitting. with the intention of

BUKHĀRĪ

making them into a habit.

Taḥiyyat al-Masjid consists of 2 Rakʻāt.

AT-TAWBAH We all sin, and the best way to remove a sin is to immediately ask forgiveness after it. Allāh says in the Qurʼān: ūThe God-conscious are those who, upon committing an evil deed or wronging themselves, remember Allāh and seek forgiveness, and they do not knowingly persist in sin.

QURʼĀN 3:135

After having committed a sin, we should hasten to a good deed that

رضي الله عنهﷺextinguishes it. For this, Abū Bakr narrates that our Messenger said:

There is no servant who commits a sin, but performs Wuḍūʼ ʻwell, and then stands and performs two Rakāt after which they seek Allāhʼs forgiveness except that He forgives them.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

Ṣalāh at-Tawbah consists of 2 Rakʻāt.

ASH-SHUKR When one is blessed with some good news, or receives some bounty through the grace of Allāh , then in gratitude a prayer may be offered. This prayer is called Ṣalāh ash-Shukr.

Ṣalāh ash-Shukr consists of 2 Rakʻāt.

AL-ISTIKHĀRAH When faced with a decision, one may perform Ṣalāh followed by reciting the Duʻāʼ of Istikhārah. This prayer and its supplication are for the purpose of seeking guidance from Allāh in making the correct decision, and so that  Allāh blesses the path one chooses with good. The method of performing Ṣalāh al-Istikhārah is as follows:

  • Perform two Rakʻāt of Ṣalāh with the intention of Ṣalāh al-Istikhārah. One should not

•Supplicate to Allāh beginning by praising Him and sending salutations on the Messenger ﷺ, then recite the Duʻāʼ of Istikhārah. Complete the Duʻāʼ with praise and salutations.

  • One should mention the matter about which they are seeking guidance at the point in
  • One may perform Istikhārah multiple times.

Istikhārah does not guarantee a certain feeling or that a sign will become apparent, but it is asking Allāh for good in what one decides. Therefore, once a decision has been made, one should move forward with complete Tawakkul (reliance) in Allāh that their prayer for good has been answered.

BUKHĀRĪ

AL-KUSŪF AND AL-KHUSŪF ﷺThe Prophet said: ūThe sun and the moon do not eclipse because of someoneʼs death. So whenever you see these eclipses, perform Ṣalāh and engage in supplication till the eclipse is over.

BUKHĀRĪ

During a solar eclipse, it is Sunnah to perform two Rakʻāt of Ṣalāh al-Kusūf in congregation, lengthening the recitation, Rukūʻ and Sujūd. The recitation should be performed aloud. Likewise, it is preferable to perform two Rakʻāt of Ṣalāh al-Khusūf at the time of a lunar eclipse. This will however be performed individually.
