Ṣalāh al-Musāfir

how to perform Qaṣr Ṣalāh, the Sharʻī definition of a travellerfinding the , and When you travel through the land, there is no sin direction of the Qiblah. on you in shortening the prayer.

QURʼĀN 4:101

When a person is travelling, they are often far away from the comforts they enjoy in their own homes and cities. A person will be tired and hungry, moving from one place to another in a hurried state, whilst carrying luggage and other items, and generally with little time to rest and pray. Whilst the modern age and its various amenities Musāfir: a traveller have slightly eased that burden compared to most of human history, travelling is still Muqīm: a residentdifficult for most people. For this reason, Allāh in His Infinite Mercy has allowed for the shortening of Ṣalāh for a traveller, so that they may perform their prayers and Safar: travel Qaṣrcontinue in their travels with ease. This shortening is called .

Iqāmah: residencyA person is a Musāfir (traveller) and thus able to perform Qaṣr (shortened Ṣalāh)

Waṭan al-Aṣlīwhen they have left their home city limits () with the intention to Waṭan al-Aṣlī: travel more than 48 sharʼī miles (54.5mi / 87.7km). They will remain a Musāfir for the permanent residence duration of their journey, as well as their stay if they do not intend to stay for less than 15 days. If they do plan on staying at their destination for 15 days or more, then Waṭan al-Iqāmah: temporary residencethey will become a Muqīm (resident) of that area and must perform Ṣalāh as normal.

Waṭan al-IqāmahThis place will become their (place of temporary residence). They Qaṣr / Taqṣīr:

Safarwill only become a Musāfir again if they intend to travel the distance of again. the shortening of the prayer when Qaṣr requires a person to shorten every four Rakʻāt Farḍ Ṣalāh to two Rakʻāt, with travelling the remaining Ṣalāh left as they are. When a person is a Musāfir, they must shorten the appropriate Ṣalāh unless they are performing their prayers behind an Imām who Jamʻ bayn aṣ- is a Muqīm. It is important to note here that whilst travelling, Ṣalātayn: joining of two Ṣalāhmales should still make every effort to perform Ṣalāh with congregation. However, if one cannot do Taḥarrī: attempting so, then they must perform Ṣalāh with to find the Qiblah Qaṣr individually.

JAMʻ BAYN AṢ-ṢALĀTAYN ﷺWhen the Prophet would travel, he would sometimes perform his prayers in a way where he could reduce the number of occasions where he had to stop, dismount, and perform his prayers. He would do this between the Ẓuhr and ʻAṣr prayers and the Maghrib and ʻIshāʼ prayers only. He would do this for ease, and as this would be a more efficient mode of travelling which would allow him and the Companions to reach their destination sooner. This practice is called Jamʻ bayn aṣ-Ṣalātayn (combining of two prayers), and there is some difference of opinion in how it should be done. Before we delve into the matter, it is important to clarify a few terms first:

JAMʻ ḤAQĪQĪ Combining of two prayers fully where one prayer is performed in the time period of another (e.g. performing Ẓuhr and ʻAṣr together in one of the two respective times). This can be of two types:

JAMʻ TAQDĪMJAMʻ TAʼKHĪR Bringing forward the coming prayer and Delaying a prayer for it to be performed together performing it with the prayer of the current with the coming prayer in its time period time period(e.g. delaying and performing Ẓuhr with ʻAṣr in ʻAṣr (e.g. performing ʻAṣr with Ẓuhr in Ẓuhr time).time).

JAMʻ ṢŪRI Combining of two prayers in an apparent manner but within their respective times (e.g. performing Ẓuhr towards the very end of its time period, and ʻAṣr at the very beginning of its time period).

All the above terms and their scenarios are practiced, though in different times. As for Jamʻ Ḥaqīqī, it is done in Ḥajj firstly in ʻArafāt: where by way of Jamʻ Taqdīm, the ʻAṣr prayer is performed immediately after Ẓuhr in the time period of the Ẓuhr prayer. Secondly, in Muzdalifah, where through Jamʻ Taʼkhīr, the Maghrib prayer is delayed and performed together with ʻIshāʼ during the time period of ʻIshāʼ. However, outside of these occasions, Jamʻ Ḥaqīqī is not permissible according to the Ḥanafī Madhhab.

When a person is travelling then, they may use Jamʻ Ṣūri to combine prayers. This is done by delaying a prayer to the point of a few minutes before its time period passes, then performing it, waiting a few minutes, and then performing the following prayer as its time period commences.

DIFFERENCES OF OPINION A final point to mention here, as there is a difference of opinion in this matter, is that as Muslims we must bear in mind that differences of opinion exist within different scholars and groups, but that does not take away from the unity of our Ummah, rather it adds to it. It is through the immense efforts of the scholars of the past that our Fiqh is what it is today, and it is only natural that there will be some differences in interpretating certain matters. What is without doubt however is that those differences exist not out of malice or division, but a sincere desire to do exactly as our Messenger ﷺWhen faced with differences and the Companions did, and none can be faulted for having such lofty aspirations. or someone doing something differently to ourselves, rather than confronting or debating, we should talk to our teachers and scholars, who will explain the matter to us in a way where all are given due respect.

PERFORMING ṢALĀH WHILST TRAVELLING When performing prayers whilst travelling on a plane, train, or coach, one must firstly try and see if one can find a way to perform their prayers as normal and face the Qiblah. If, however, that is not possible, then for Farḍ prayers one should face in the direction they are, and perform Salāh seated using their head to indicate the positions (upright for Qiyām, slightly bent for Rukūʻ, fully tilted for Sujūd with hands on the knees for both Rukūʻ and Sujūd). One will then be required to reperform the prayers performed in this state, once the journey has ended or after having disembarked.

NAFL ṢALĀH WHILST TRAVELLING ﷺRasūlullāh used to perform ūNafl] Ṣalāh on his mount wherever it faced (in the direction of the destination), and whenever he wanted to perform the Farḍ prayer, he dismounted and ūprayed facing the Qiblah.

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺWhen travelling, the Messenger is reported to have performed Nawāfil Ṣalāh whilst seated on his camel, facing the direction of whatever may have been their destination. Nafl Ṣalāh is valid whilst sitting, and when one is outside of their city limits travelling, they are permitted to perform Nawāfil seated in their car, plane, train or any other ﷺmode of conveyance without facing Qiblah. This is a Sunnah of Rasūlullāh which we should try to practise.

TAḤARRĪ Taḥarrī refers to making an educated guess as to which direction the Qiblah is. A person who has no means of identifying the Qiblah will carry out Taḥarrī to perform their Ṣalāh, and their Ṣalāh will be valid even if they find out later that they had faced in the wrong direction. On the other hand, if a person does not make such an effort, and simply performs their Ṣalāh, their prayer will be invalid if they find out later that they had faced in the wrong direction.

FINDING THE QIBLAH Before we resort to Taḥarrī, there are certain methods we can use to try and accurately find out the direction of the Qiblah. Taḥarrī is only valid once other methods of establishing Qiblah have been exhausted, and if there are other local people around us, we must try and ask them to see if they can help us ascertain the direction of the Qiblah first, as they are likely to know their location and relevant directions. However, if there is no one else around, then here are some alternative methods:

ALTERNATIVE METHODS TO FINDING THE QIBLAH USE A SMARTPHONE IF YOU HAVE A SMARTPHONE AND IT CAN CONNECT TO THE INTERNET, YOU CAN DOWNLOAD APPS OR USE QIBLAH-FINDING WEBSITES TO POINT YOU IN THE DIRECTION OF THE QIBLAH. HOWEVER, SOMETIMES THESE APPS CAN BE FAULTY, OR THE PHONE MAY BE UNCALIBRATED, GIVING A FALSE READING. IT MIGHT BE A GOOD IDEA TO TRY IT A COUPLE OF TIMES TO BE SURE.

A person wishes to travel a journey of 60 miles from their home city. Prepare and deliver a five-minute They plan to be away for 30 days visiting three cities for the following speech on the ease Allāh has number of days respectively: 6, 15, 9. created within the rulings of Islām.

Calculate where they will perform Qaṣr Ṣalāh.

USE A COMPASS Create a pamphlet for a local A PHYSICAL COMPASS CAN Muslim travel agency detailing the BE USED OR ONE ON A rulings of Qaṣr Ṣalāh.

PHONE. YOU CAN OFTEN ACCURATELY ESTABLISH THE DIRECTION OF THE QIBLAH FROM WHERE YOU ARE IN THE WORLD BY CORRECTLY USING A COMPASS. FOR EXAMPLE, IN THE UK THE QIBLAH IS 119° FROM TRUE NORTH.

LOOK FOR THE SUN THE SUN RISES IN THE EAST, AND SETS IN THE WEST. IF YOU KNOW YOUR LOCATION, YOU CAN USE THAT KNOWLEDGE TO TRY AND GAUGE THE DIRECTION OF THE QIBLAH. IF YOU KNOW WHERE THE SUN HAS RISEN FROM, OR WHERE IT WILL SET, YOU CAN EASILY GET YOUR BEARINGS AND FIND THE QIBLAH. FOR EXAMPLE, IN THE UK THE QIBLAH IS APPROXIMATELY 30° SOUTHWARD FROM THE EAST. If none of the above methods work, or you have tried them, but they do not give you a definitive answer, then you may resort to Taḥarrī. Taḥarrī then is to make an educated guess as to which direction the Qiblah might be, and you may factor into consideration any clues or indications you deem suitable.

Once you do so, you can perform your Ṣalāh.

The Day of Jumu'ah

ʻ The Day of Jumuah Jumuʻah is the weekly day of celebration for a Muslim. It is a day of great rewards, which may be gained from the various acts of worship a person can perform on the day, and it is also a day of congregation, as Muslims come together to observe the Jumuʻah prayer.

رحمه الله تعالىImām al-Ghāzalī , in his great work, Iḥyāʼ ʻUlūm ad-Dīn, writes,

THE DAY OF JUMUʻAH THE FRIDAY PRAYER Friday brings with it the Jumuʻah prayer.

Jumuʻah is a special prayer of two Rakʻāt performed in the place of Ẓuhr, and preceded by a 'Khuṭbah', a speech delivered by the Imām. However, Jumuʻah is not compulsory on everyone, nor is it for every situation or location. Certain people and places will perform Ẓuhr as usual. The details regarding this are outlined below:

CONDITIONS THAT MAKE THE JUMUʻAH PRAYER OBLIGATORY ON A PERSON BEING A MUQĪM. IF ONE IS A MUSĀFIR, JUMUʻAH PRAYER IS NOT NECESSARY, THOUGH ONE SHOULD STILL PERFORM IT IF ONE CAN ATTEND A MASJID. BEING HEALTHY, SANE, AND MATURE. JUMUʻAH IS NOT OBLIGATORY ON ONE WHO IS UNABLE TO GO TO THE MASJID, IS INSANE, OR A CHILD. BEING MALE. JUMUʻAH PRAYER IS NOT OBLIGATORY ON WOMEN. BEING FREE FROM A SHARʻĪ VALID EXCUSE.

There must be at least three people apart from the Imām It must be in a city or town. who fulfil the requirements Jumuʻah cannot be offered of Imāmah of the others in a small village or in an in the congregation (male, uninhabited place. mature and sane). They must be present from the Khuṭbah till the prostration in the first Rakʻah. The Jumuʻah prayer must CONDITIONS be performed openly with FOR THE permission JUMUʻAH for others to join. It cannot PRAYER TO BE be performed in a private or VALID secluded place, or where the The Jumuʻah prayer general public is must be offered within denied entry. the time of Ẓuhr. There is no Qaḍāʼ of Jumuʻah prayer, rather one will perform Ẓuhr to make up for the missed The Khuṭbah must be prayer. delivered, and this should be prior to the prayer, but within the time of Ẓuhr.

THE DAY OF JUMUʻAH THE KHUṬBAHIt is possible that one may find themselves in the position where they are required to deliver the Jumuʻah Khuṭbah, in which case the following are some Sunan to bear in mind. One should:

Stand for the Khuṭbah (a speech, which may be read from a book or text), which should be split into two sections with a short sitting in between. Be pure from any impurity and in a state of Wuḍūʼ.

Face the congregation and speak so that all present can hear.

Deliver the Khuṭbah from the Minbar if available, otherwise one may stand on the ground.

Refrain from making Khuṭbah overly lengthy nor too short.

The Khuṭbah must contain some form of glorification and praise of Allāh and should amount to at least the duration of three verses of the Qurʼān. Below are certain things which are Sunnah for the Khuṭbah:

Praise of Allāh Gratitude to Allāh Testifying to the Oneness of Allāh  and the Prophethood of Muḥammad ﷺ Salutations on Rasūlullāh ﷺAdvice on having Taqwā Advice to do good and Recitation of verses from the caution against evilQurʼān Repeat of all the above in the second section of the Khuṭbah Supplication for the Muslims in the second section of the Khuṭbah In the two Rakʻāt Ṣalāh that follows the Khuṭbah, the Sunnah is to recite Sūrah al-Aʻlā and Sūrah al-Ghāshiyah, or Sūrah al-Jumuʻah and Sūrah al-Munāfiqūn, or Sūrah al-Jumuʻah and Sūrah al-Ghāshiyah in the first and second Rakʻah respectively.

Ṣawm

the definition cover and importance of Fasting is the foregoing of food, drink, and sexual intercourse from Ṣubḥ Ṣādiq (true fasting, different types dawn) till Ghurūb (sunset). In a famous Ḥadīth Qudsī, Allāh says, of fasts, the issue of moonsighting and The fast is for Me and I will give the reward for it, as some rulings regarding he (the one who observes the fast) leaves his sexual fasting. desire, food and drink for My Sake.

BUKHĀRĪ

Fasting has such a great reward that Allāh promises that He Himself will reward the fasting person for their fast.

Hilāl: the crescent moon visible after a new moon, which indicates the beginning of a new month in the Islamic calendar.

Fidyah: the donation of food or money given in lieu of fasts missed due to an inability to fast.

There are many benefits mentioned in the Qurʼān and Ḥadīth regarding fasting. One of those benefits mentioned is the increase in Taqwā. Allāh says in the Qurʼān, The fasts have been enjoined upon you as they were enjoined upon those before you so that you be God-conscious.

QURʼĀN 2:183

Taqwā is created because a person has no one to look over them when they are fasting, and it is only their recognition ﷺthat Allāh is watching them that stops them from secretly breaking their fast. Furthermore, the Prophet advised the young men of the Muslims to fast, as it tends to restrain and curb the desires inherent in youth.

For Muslims, fasting is of many types. We have the Farḍ fasts of the blessed month of Ramaḍān, and alongside those, we may keep voluntary fasts throughout the year. The Farḍ fasts of Ramaḍān are incredibly blessed not only by virtue of their being in Ramaḍān, but also for the fact that we perform many other acts of worship in that same month. On the other hand, voluntary fasts are plentiful in reward. Allāh says in a Ḥadīth Qudsī, There are two moments of joy for a fasting person: one at the time of breaking their fast, and the other at the time when they will meet their Lord.

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺIn another Ḥadīth, our Messenger mentions MOONSIGHTING that those who are abundant in their fasting will be given the unique honour of entering Jannah The Islamic calendar is based on the lunar cycle. Thus, through a special gate called ar-Rayyān, and every month depends on the new moon to be sighted for none but those who observe fasts will enter it to begin. Sighting the moon for the coming month is a through it.

ﷺSunnah of the Prophet which we should try to do, especially for the blessed months as it ﷺheralds their coming. Rasūlullāh said, Begin fasting on seeing the crescent ūof Ramaḍān and give up fasting on seeing the crescent ūof Shawwāl, and if the sky is overcast (and you cannot see it), complete thirty ʻdays of Shabān.

BUKHĀRĪ

Thus, Ramaḍān begins with the sighting of the crescent moon, or by the completion of thirty days of Shaʻbān if the moon cannot be sighted.

QAḌĀʼ AND KAFFĀRAH Actions that break the fast are of two types: al-Bīḍ (13th, 14th, 15th). Make a class intention to fast together Those which necessitate when they come around.

Qaḍāʼ. Qaḍāʼ means to repeat, and it would require the person to keep one fast in place of the broken or missed fast. Those which necessitate Kaffārah. Kaffārah is a penalty to make up for the fast that was broken. A Qaḍāʼ fast is also necessary when Kaffārah is required.

There is a difference between accidentally and forgetfully doing something. If one forgets they are fasting and eats, then the fast will remain valid. If on the other hand, one is fully aware of the fact that one is fasting, yet accidentally consumes or swallows something without meaning to, that fast will be invalidated. For example, if one were to attempt to gargle water for Ghusl and accidentally swallowed some water, the fast will break. However, there is no requirement to perform Kaffārah: rather that person will have to perform Qaḍāʼ. If one intentionally breaks a Nafl fast, they will have to perform Qaḍāʼ. On the other hand, if one was to intentionally break a fast of Ramaḍān without a valid reason by eating, drinking, or having sexual intercourse, they will need to complete a Qaḍāʼ fast, as well as Kaffārah. The Kaffārah in this case is to keep 60 consecutive fasts. If there is a valid reason for a person disallowing them from doing these consecutive fasts, then they may either:

Give 60 poor people Feed 60 poor people two Feed one poor person 1.75kg of wheat, barley, full meals.two meals for 60 days.dates, raisins or its equivalent in money.

ETIQUETTE OF THE ḤARAM ḤaramThe of Makkah is a sacred place, subject to rules that govern behaviour within its boundaries. Beyond the rules however, the Ḥaram deserves our respect and the greatest standard of etiquette. We should refrain from spending our time in frivolous whilst visiting the two blessed cities such as shopping beyond what is necessary, or doing that which is inappropriate, such as taking selfies or photos for social media, or video calling others to show them.

IḤRĀM Iḥrām is the state a person enters into before going for Ḥajj or ʻUmrah. Iḥrām is not only the wearing of certain clothes, but rather it involves the voluntary entering into a state where a person restricts themselves from doing particular things, and fixates upon performing a great act of worship.

HOW TO ENTER IḤRĀM Before entering the state of Iḥrām, one should perform Ghusl, trim the nails. Then for males they should apply perfume and must wear the sheets of Iḥrām. Thereafter, one will perform two Rakʻāt of Ṣalāh, followed by making the intention of entering Iḥrām for Umrah or Ḥajj and reciting the Talbiyah. This commences the state of Iḥrām.

CLOTHING OF IḤRĀM Men will wear two sheets of loose cloth which should preferably be white. No other items of clothing may be worn during Iḥrām. For footwear, men should wear slippers which do not cover the instep of the foot.

Women must cover the entire body except the face. This may be done with an ʻabāyah and a scarf which fully covers the hair. The face should not be covered with any cloth that touches the face. Niqāb may still be worn by using something similar to a cap and draping the veil over it. Women may wear normal shoes.

PERMISSIBLE ACTS IN IḤRĀM Injections and Wearing Using vaccinations, glasses, Washing unscented or the Wearing sunglasses, Changing the oneself for soap (it is removal of watches or contact Iḥrām for a purification or preferable blood from wristbands lenses, new set to keep coolnot to do so the body for identityhearing aids however)through or teeth cuppingretainers Using a belt or pouch Using a Killing Slaughtering Using to secure plaster or potentially domestic sanitary the lower bandage for harmful animals for productsgarment injuriesanimalsfood or hold valuables IMPERMISSIBLE ACTS IN IḤRĀM Wearing Covering stitched Sexual the face clothes that relations with Cutting or Using any follow the and Trimming something Huntingshaving fragranced shape of intimacy nailsthat hairproductthe body or with oneʼs touches the covering the spouseface for a head and woman face with something for a man

ḤARAMPOINTS OF MĪQĀT ḤaramThe is a sacred area marked by a MADĪNAH boundary (see map) in Makkah in which DHUL HULAYFAH OUTSIDE MĪQĀTcertain actions are prohibited. The locations forming the boundary are as follows:

Ḥudaybiyah, Jiʻirānah, Tanʻīm (Masjid ʻĀishah), and ʻArafāt.

MĪQĀT The Mīqāt is a large geographical boundary which surrounds the Ḥaram of Makkah, AL JUḤFAH marked by points of entry from different routes to Makkah. For those intending to travel to Makkah, this may only be passed whilst in Iḥrām. Entering the state of Iḥrām DHĀT ʻIRQ is compulsory prior to arrival at any of the MAKKAH QARN AL MANĀZILpoints of the Mīqāt. Travelling past the Mīqāt JEDDAH boundary intending to travel to Makkah INSIDE MĪQĀT without Iḥrām necessitates the payment of Dam.

ḤIL YALAMLAM ḤilThe is the area between the boundaries Ḥaramof the Mīqāt and the boundaries of the of Makkah. Residents of Ḥil who wish to enter the Ḥaram for ʻUmrah or Anyone within the Ḥaram who wishes to perform an ʻUmrah must travel to the boundary of the Ḥaram and enter Iḥrām there. Residents of Makkah and those pilgrims performing Ḥajj Tamattuʻ may enter Iḥrām from within the Ḥaram for Ḥajj.

THERE ARE THREE TYPES OF ḤAJJ Ḥajj QirānḤajj and ʻUmrah will be performed in one Iḥrām.

Ḥajj TamattuʻḤajj and ʻUmrah will be performed in two separate Iḥrāms.

Ḥajj Ifrād Only Ḥajj is performed.

ﷺMadīnah out of love of the Prophet . A journey to Madīnah is ﷺone of love, for visiting the greatest Messenger , walking in his city, and praying in his Masjid is a deeply moving experience.

A Muslim Identity

Expressions of Faith

The greatest blessing that Allāh can bestow upon any person is the blessing of Īmān. Likewise, the glad ﷺtidings of the Prophet are what we should aspire to be deserving of. We will be rewarded by Allāh for standing up for our religion, and more so where it may be more difficult to do so.

The greatest badge of honour we can wear is the emblem of Islām; the most noble of associations we can claim is to the ﷺMessenger Muḥammad . Sacrificing our identity to 'fit in' with others out of embarrassment not only destroys our self- esteem, but also causes the displeasure of Allāh . Often, we are more likely to gain honour and respect from others by preserving our identity than surrendering it. Furthermore, Daʻwahour identity as Muslims serves as a source of . Upon observing our adherence to our faith, other Muslims may receive encouragement and courage through our expression of Islām, and non-Muslims may be drawn towards Islām by seeing us.

MODESTY IN DRESS: AN EXPRESSION OF FAITH Allāh has ordained that Muslims show modesty in their dress. Clothing serves two purposes: to cover ourselves, and to beautify ourselves. Allāh says, O children of Ādam, We have sent down to you clothing that covers your shame and provides adornment. As for the dress of Taqwā (piety), that is the best.

QURʼĀN 7:26

This verse highlights the above two purposes but points out a very valuable point: that piety and righteousness is the best thing a person can have. This in itself is an expression of faith.

Piety in dress and clothing for men and women is shown in modesty and simplicity. A believer follows ‘Awrahthe commands of Allāh in covering their and wearing appropriate and suitable clothing.

Clothing that is tight around the areas of the ‘Awrah by which the body form can be seen goes against modesty and the rules of covering the ‘Awrah. The differences between men and women are also important, with the ‘Awrah of both respective genders being different.

One ruling regarding clothing is the commandment of Ḥijāb. Ḥijāb is a woman’s covering of her body, Maḥramshair and beauty from non-, and it is compulsory for every Muslim woman. This means wearing such clothes that cover the body and hair fully, and which do not allow for one’s figure to be seen. It also includes not beautifying oneself (by certain clothes, makeup, or other adornments) when one is to be in the presence of non-Maḥrams.

Wearing the Ḥijāb is a great commitment, and it is an expression of faith for every Muslim woman. In some places and situations, where one may feel pressured to fit into certain norms, it may seem difficult to maintain the principles of Ḥijāb, but one should remember firstly that Allāh has promised greater rewards for greater sacrifices, and secondly, that one’s respect and honour is worth infinitely more than any social status or online admiration.

ḤIJĀB IN THE QUR’ĀN AND SUNNAH ūThe Believing Women must not expose their adornment, except what normally appears. Let them draw their veils over their chests, and not expose their adornment… And let them not stamp their feet (draw attention to themselves) in a way that the adornment they conceal is known.

QURʼĀN 24:31

O Prophet! Tell your wives, daughters, and believing women to draw their outer garments (low) over their bodies. That will make it more likely that they are recognised (as virtuous) and not be harassed.

QURʼĀN 33:59

The believing women used to perform the Fajr prayer with the Messenger of Allāh and then return wrapped in their veiling garments; no one could recognise them.

ROLE MODELS Travelling a trodden path is easier than carving your own, and in a similar manner, following the path of someone successful is easier than carving our own life paths. For us as Muslims, success is defined primarily by our spirituality, connection with Allāh , and success in the hereafter. Whilst it may be useful to look up to certain people for worldly achievement so long as our following them does not violate Islamic values, ultimately we should aim to place those on a pedestal who we are certain have succeeded in the hereafter. We know of who these people are through the Qurʼān and Sunnah, and we should their lives and build our character and personalities around them.

رضي الله عنهمﷺThe Ṣaḥābah of our Messenger were exemplary figures of

extraordinary piety, resoluteness, and bravery. Allāh says about them in the Qurʼān that, Allāh is pleased with them, and they are pleased with Him.

QURʼĀN 9:100

This verse, and others like it show that they are not only guaranteed eternal success, but that their lives are

رضي الله عنهمtemplates for us to follow. Following the Ṣaḥābah

and other figures mentioned in the Qurʼān, whose stories Allāh has provided us with as examples to follow, is then worthy of our attention and imitation, and we should endeavour to do just that.

Besides those mentioned in the Qurʼān and Sunnah, having other role models who reflect what we as Muslims value is also important.

There are figures from our vivid and diverse history who persevered in the face of extreme oppression, and besides them, learned scholars, noble warriors and leaders, and men and women of piety who exemplified what it means to be Muslim. Looking up to such figures to draw s from their lives, and to take inspiration so that we can better ourselves is part of being a Muslim and building oneʼs Muslim identity.

FAMOUS EXAMPLES THE BELIEVING MAN The 40th Sūrah of the Qurʼān, known as Sūrah al-Muʼmin or Sūrah Ghāfir, is named after an incident of remarkable bravery shown by a man in the court of one of historyʼs greatest oppressors: Firʻawn. Allāh  calls him 'The Believing Man', a truly esteemed title bestowed upon him for his admirable courage in the face of evil and disbelief. A total of 19 verses are allocated to narrating his story, which indicates the significance Allāh places in his defiance being a for us all. His case shows us how we can be Muslims proudly in even the most hostile of environments, and how no amount of external pressure exerted, directly or indirectly, should alter our firm stance on maintaining our Islamic identity and beliefs.

ʻA believing man from among the kinsfolk of Firawn, who had kept his faith hidden, spoke out, “Would you kill a man merely because he says: My Lord is Allāh?

Whereas he has brought clear Signs to you from your Lord. If he is a liar, his lie will recoil on him, but if he is truthful, some of the (dreadful) things with which he threatens you will certainly befall you. Allāh does not guide the one who is a transgressor and a liar. My people! Today you possess the kingdom and are dominant in the land, but who will help us if we are visited by Allāhʼs punishment?” ʻFirawn said, “I am telling you the same which I think is proper, and I am only guiding you to the way which is right.” The man who had believed, said, “O my people! I fear that you may be overtaken by the day that has already overtaken many groups; a day that overtook the people of ʻNūḥ and Ād and Thamūd and the peoples after them. And the fact is that Allāh does not seek to wrong His servants. My people! I fear for you the day of wailing, when you will cry out to one another and run about, but there will be none to protect you from Allāh; the truth is that there is none to guide the one whom Allāh lets go astray.” "And before this Yūsuf had brought to you clear Signs, but you continued to be in doubt concerning his teachings. Then, when he died, you said,'Allāh will never send another Messenger after him.'”

“That is how Allāh lets go astray those who transgress the limits and live in doubt. Those who quarrel in the matter of the verses of Allāh without any authority having reached them. How despicable is that to Allāh and the believers! In this way, Allāh seals the heart of every arrogant tyrant.” ʻFirawn said, “O Hāmān, build for me a tower that I may reach the paths - the paths of the heavens - and peep at the God of Musā, for I indeed deem him a liar.” ʻAnd that is how his evil deeds were made attractive to Firawn and he was barred from the Right Way: And the evil design of ʻFirawn was (to end) in nothing but ruin. The man who had believed, said, “O my people! Follow me: I shall show you the right way. My people! The life of this world is of temporary benefit and the Hereafter is the Abode of Permanence. Whoever does evil shall be recompensed to the extent of the evil done; and whoever does good, whether man or woman, if they be a believer, all such people shall enter Paradise wherein they shall be provided without measure. O my people! How is it that I call you to salvation and you call me to the Fire! You call me to deny Allāh and associate with Him those whom I do not know, while I am calling you to the All-Mighty, the All-Forgiving. There is no doubt that whatever (idols) you invite me to ūworship are not worthy to be invoked either in this world or the Hereafter. And undoubtedly, our return is to Allāh, and the transgressors will be the inmates of the Fire. Soon you will remember what I am saying to you, and to Allāh I entrust my affairs. He is ever Watchful over His servants.” Then Allāh protected him from what evils they plotted, and the ʻevil punishment besieged the household of Firawn. The Fire; they will be shown to it morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour takes place, ūit will be said ʻ'Take the Household of Firawn into the most severe of punishment'.

QURʼĀN 40:28-46

رضي الله عنهاMARYAM BINT ʻIMRĀN Maryam رضي الله عنهاspent her life in devotion to

Allāh  in the sanctuary of al-Quds. Her modesty was not dictated by those around her, but rather by Allāh ʼs command. When she miraculously gave birth to

عليه السلامرضي الله عنهاʻĪsā , despite Maryam being

one of trusting Allāh  and perseverance in the face of societal pressure. Today, she serves as an example of Ḥayāʼ to women across the world.

رضي الله عنهJAʻFAR IBN ABĪ ṬĀLIB When some Muslims migrated from Makkah to Abyssinia to escape persecution, Jaʻfar رضي الله عنه, the

ﷺcousin of the Prophet , went with them. The Quraysh sent messengers to the King of Abyssinia with gifts to persuade him to send them back, and the Muslims were summoned to the court to

رضي الله عنهplead their case. In a famous story of the earlier Muslims, Jaʻfar stood proudly proclaiming

the various blessings accepting Islām had brought them. He then read a portion of the Qurʼān in front of the King and his ministers. The King, upon hearing the Qurʼān and the speech of

Jaʻfar رضي الله عنه was greatly moved and accepted Islām. He rejected the messengers of the Quraysh,

and allowed the Muslims to live peacefully in his land.

“O King, we were a people in a state of ignorance, worshipping idols and eating carrion, committing every type of shameful deed, breaking the ties of kinship, unheeding the neighbour, and the strong among us exploited the weak. We remained in this state, until Allāh sent us a Prophet from amongst us whose lineage, honesty, trustworthiness, and chastity were well- known to us. He called us to worship God alone and to renounce the stones and the idols which we and our ancestors used to worship besides God. He commanded us to speak truthfully, to fulfil our trusts, to maintain ties of kinship, to be kind to our neighbours; to cease forbidden acts and bloodshed. He forbade obscenities and false testimony; to not appropriate an orphanʼs property nor slander chaste women. He ordered us to worship God alone and not to associate anything with Him, to perform prayer, to give charity and to fast. We believed in him and what he brought to us from Allāh and we follow him in what he has asked us to do and we keep away from what he forbade us from doing.

Thereupon, O King, our people attacked us and punished us severely to make us renounce our religion and take us back to the worship of idols, and to that we commit of immorality what we used to commit. So when they made life intolerable for us and oppressed us, constricted us and obstructed us from observing our religion we left for your country, choosing you above anyone else, desiring your proximity and hoping to not be persecuted in your jurisdiction, O King.”

AḤMAD

رضي الله عنهʻUMAR IBN AL-KHAṬṬĀB

In the early days of Islām, the Muslims were still hiding their religion from the Quraysh out of fear of persecution.

However, ʻUmar رضي الله عنه upon accepting Islām went to all the

Quraysh to announce his conversion proudly. Similarly, when the order of Hijrah was given, the Muslims left secretly fearing reprisals from the disbelievers.

رضي الله عنهʻUmar on the other hand, boldly announced his

intention to migrate in front of the strongest of the Quraysh challenging them to stop him if they so dared.

رضي الله عنهBILĀL IBN RABĀḤ Bilāl رضي الله عنهʼs story of endurance and

hardship of the most incredible degree is a lasting for all Muslims. As an African slave living in the ownership of Umayyah ibn Khalaf, a staunch enemy of Islām, his conversion to Islām meant that he was

رضي الله عنهafforded no mercy. Bilāl was

dragged through the streets of Makkah, before being bound and whipped under the scorching Arabian sun, and then left to swelter in the unbearable heat with hot desert rocks placed on his chest. His only response, staunch and firm, was “Ahad, Ahad” (Allāh  is One, Allāh  is One).

رحمه الله تعالىMAWLĀNĀ MUḤAMMAD QĀSIM NĀNOTWĪ

Facing colonial repression in India, Mawlānā Qāsim Nānotwī understood how Muslims may suffer and lose their Islamic identity whilst being under British colonial rule. He set up an institute, known as Darul ʻUlūm Deoband, which was replicated in other parts of India, which taught Islamic sciences and developed young Muslim leaders to guide the Muslim population. His efforts would blossom into a worldwide network of Islamic institutes and scholars, developing and deepening our understanding of Islām, and spreading the message of our Messenger ﷺ to every part of the world.

THE GREATEST OF EXAMPLES OUR BELOVED MESSENGER MUḤAMMAD ﷺ Climbing the mountain paths to Ṭāif on foot during the early days of Islām, the Prophet ﷺ was expectant of some support from the leaders of the town. But after he spoke to them, they ordered for him to be pelted with stones until he was driven from the town. Bloodied, beaten and severely injured, our Beloved Messenger ﷺ did not wilt in the face of such tribulations, nor was his spirit dampened, or his kindness dulled. Our Messenger ﷺ was unwavering when it came to the laws of Allāh , and when offered wealth and power to stop his preaching and end his faith, he chose steadfastness and courage over a life of ease. His life is the greatest for us in standing up for what it means to be a believer.

LOVE FOR ALLĀH  AND HIS MESSENGER ﷺ ﷺLoving Allāh and His Messenger is a part of our faith, and forms a crucial part of a believer's character. Khubayb

Self Reformation

Self-Reformation the will cover meaning of Tazkiyah is a word meaning purification and cleansing, and it is used to refer to the spiritual Tazkiyah, the Nafscleansing of the (soul/ego) from its base desires to growing in recognition of Allāh concept of the , attaining closeness to Him, and developing spiritually. Tazkiyah is self-reformation soul in Islām, and that brings a believer closer to everlasting success. Allāh says in the Qurʼān, how to work on reforming oneself.Successful indeed is the one who purifies (does Tazkiyah of) their soul, and doomed is the one who corrupts it!

QURʼĀN 91:9-10

The importance of Tazkiyah then cannot be understated, as it is the continuous effort of the believer to increase their Īmān and their connection with Allāh . As Muslims we believe in improving in every aspect of life to achieve perfection (Iḥsān), and especially in matters of spirituality where improvement may be the difference Tazkiyah: between eternal salvation or damnation. Tazkiyah is the road for that improvement, purification (of the and it may be done under the guidance of someone more knowledgeable, or through soul) self- and worship.

Nafs: soul Iḥsān: perfection Iṣlāḥ: reformation; correction Murāqabah: meditation Muḥāsabah: correctional self- WHAT IS THE NAFS? The Nafs is often translated as soul or ego, and it is the inner part of a person which is responsible for their committing of good or evil. Allāh takes an oath by the Nafs in the Qurʼān, saying, And by the soul and ūthe One Who fashioned it, then inspired it with its (instincts) of evil and piety.

QURʼĀN 91: 7-8 The Nafs was created with base desires and noble attributes, and a person must strive to work against the base desires ﷺand cultivate the noble attributes. Rasūlullāh said, The Mujāhid (striving believer) is the one who fights against his Nafs (in the obedience of Allāh).

TIRMIDHĪ

The Nafs is a product of nurture, and though in its original state it recognises Allāh as the Creator worthy of singular worship, the lifestyle it experiences can obscure it from seeing the truth, and from repeated misdeeds, it can become accustomed to sin. A person must purge sinful traits from their habits to purify their Nafs, as continuing down a path of sinfulness creates a Nafs which desires to be fed by more and more sin. IN THE QURʼĀN, ALLĀH  OUTLINES THREE TYPES OF SOULS:

Nafs This type of soul is the one that is steeped in sins. The Qurʼān describes it al-Ammārah as 'ever inclined to sin' as it is so acclimatized to it. A person with such a َsoul is unlikely to feel regretful over their sins or wish to seek forgiveness. Muḥāsabah- Each night as you lay down to sleep reflect on your actions.

Recite 'Alḥamdulillāh' on the good that 'Astaghfirullah'was done and for every wrong action that was carried out and plan to ask for forgiveness from those you may have wronged.

HOW DOES ONE PURIFY THEMSELVES? As Tazkiyah is self-reformation, one must firstly cleanse the soul from sins, vices, and spiritual maladies to make way for cultivating higher qualities and virtues. For this, one may ask an expert for advice over their own spiritual illnesses, such as greed, jealousy, dishonesty, and similar shortcomings. Furthermore, this is strengthened Muḥāsabahthrough , where a person will contemplate over their own character and actions, and seek to reflect over what they see as their own failings. Then it is a matter of initiating action over perceived character faults of oneself, through continuous daily Muḥāsabah. One may keep a tracker, or inform another of their progress to ensure they are continually improving. Tazkiyah may be difficult to do as it is uncomfortable looking at our own faults, but it is through this that a person gains control over their Nafs, suppresses its lower urges, and turns it to the obedience of Allāh .

The other side of Tazkiyah is the effort to achieve a noble station in the sight of Allāh through His remembrance by way of Ṣalāh, recitation of the Qurʼān, Dhikr, and Duʻāʼ. Furthermore, it is the cultivation of noble character (Akhlāq) and virtues, such as a consistent level of Taqwā, Ṣidq (honesty), Ṣabr (forbearance/patience), Ḥayāʼ (modesty) and similar attributes.

MURĀQABAH Murāqabah is contemplation and meditation that a person practises to better connect to Allāh . Murāqabah may involve a person fully imagining themselves in certain states or places, such as the process of dying or being resurrected on the day of Qiyāmah. This is done to build greater Taqwā and a realisation of Allāh , the reality of life, and the hereafter. Murāqabah is a great tool to detach oneself from the materialism of this world and refocus oneself on the ultimate aim of life. WHO CAN I APPROACH?

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺHe did not allow adversity to overly affect him, but consoled himself with words pleasing to Allāh , and comforting to himself.

Another from his story for good mental wellbeing is that of

From the belief in Qadr which promises us that Allāh is forever aware of our situation, and that everything is predetermined by the All-Powerful and All-Knowing, to Ṣalāh, Dhikr and Duʻāʼ, which are sources of comfort and solace. Likewise, Islām encourages the maintaining of ties of kinship with our immediate and extended families who can be pillars of support for us.

Muslim Contributions

Part of being proud for who we are is recognising our past, understanding it, and celebrating our achievements. If we as Muslims do not our rich history to see how Islām heralded golden ages in Muslim will cover of inferiority, but we fail to find our place in the halls a European contributions of humanityʼs greatest accomplishments. Muslims intellectual to the world, in the past, and Muslims today, whilst retaining their movement which Islamic identity, changed and are changing the course emphasised reason their importance of human history. over tradition todaywhy , and beginning in the 17th it is important century to study these EXPLORATIONachievements.Polymath: a learned scholar whose knowledge spans Setting out from his hometown in Tangier, many fields Morocco for Ḥajj, Muḥammad ibn Baṭṭūṭah had little idea that he would not return home Gothic: an for another 24 years. Over that period of time, architectural style he would travel an unprecedented 117,000 from the Middle Ageskm (73,000 mi) over land and sea and become one of the most famous travellers in history.

Classical Age: refers Ibn Baṭṭūṭah penned the details of his travels to the flourishing of in later life, in a book commonly referred to as the Greek and Roman The Riḥlah. civilisations during a period between the 8th century BCE and the 5th century CE CARTOGRAPHY The making of maps is a complex and intricate enterprise, which involves collating a huge amount of information on places, cities, and oceans from scores of travellers, then sifting through it to determine what is accurate, and finally sketching a proportionate image of the data. Muslims made headway in this field with the likes of Al-Idrīsī and his atlas of 70 maps, producing the Nuzhat al-Mushtāq fī Ikhtirāq al-Āfāq (or Tabula Rogerina). Al- Idrīsiʼs monumental work was relied upon for three centuries after him, and with his work began the shift of cartography to a scientific endeavour requiring ever-increasing precision.

MEDICINE Whilst we believe as Muslims that Allāh is the ultimate grantor of health and cure, we have been instructed to apply our efforts to find treatment, and rely upon Allāh for it to work.

Muslims throughout the centuries understood this principle, and encouraged with the belief that Allāh would reward their efforts to help others, pushed the field of medicine forward immensely. The first organized hospitals offering free treatment would be built by Muslims, followed by hospitals which included lecture rooms, in-house pharmacies, and running water. On the academic side, the likes of Ibn al-Haitham (Alhazen) and Ibn Sīnā (Avicenna) wrote monumental books such as Kitāb al-Manāẓir (The Book of Optics) and Al- Qānūn (The Canon), the latter of which would be used as an authority in medicine for over six centuries.

Anyone who practises medicine when they are not known as a practitioner will be held responsible.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

THE ASTROLABE The need to navigate the seas and land, as well as the Islamic requirement to find the direction of the Kaʻbah and the precise timing for every Ṣalāh led Muslims to develop a handheld, reproducible, astronomical instrument called the 'astrolabe'. The astrolabe was invaluable to travellers and sailors who needed it to determine their latitudinal location. One Muslim astronomer listed around 1000 applications for it, and in a world without computers, it was one of the most advanced and sophisticated instruments in existence.

MATHEMATICS that the word 'algebra' comes from Arabic? The word is actually 'al-jabr', and the discovery of algebra is attributed to a man named Muḥammad ibn Mūsā al-Khawārizmī.

Modern day technology, phones, computers, planes and so many inventions and everyday mechanisms we rely upon today depend on the work of Muslim mathematicians. Muslims took the work of previous mathematicians, developed, refined, and added to it, and passed it on to the next generation.

PHILOSOPHY Philosophy as we know it today would be very different were it not for the timeless contributions of Muslims of the past. The knowledge and musings of the ancient Greeks were translated first by Muslims, who then wrote commentaries before expanding on the corpus of knowledge with their own Islāmically-infused thoughts. The likes of Ibn Sīnā (Avicenna), Al-Rāzi (Rhazes), Ibn Rushd (Averroes), Ibn Bājja (Avempace) and others provided the foundation for The Enlightenment, and many prominent scientists and philosophers (with whom we may be familiar) would cite the aforementioned polymaths as authorities.

TRANSLATIONS The thirst for knowledge was and should be the cornerstone of every Muslim civilization, ﷺenshrined in the Ḥadīth of our Messenger , Seeking knowledge is a duty upon every Muslim.

IBN MĀJAH

It was this thirst then, that drove Muslims to translate the received wisdom of ancient peoples, from works on astronomy to botany, mathematics to philosophy and everything in between. The 'House of Wisdom' in Baghdad was filled with tomes of translated manuscripts; and from the capital city, the infectious curiosity spread far within the Muslim world, where even in the far reaches of Andalusia (modern day Spain), Muslims strove to translate works. They then aided in translating those works into Latin to be taken to the Western World, where they would eventually revive Europe, dragging the continent out from the Dark Ages.

ARCHITECTURE Building on the foundations of those before them, Muslim architects, masons, and engineers advanced humanityʼs construction capabilities by several storeys. Across the Muslim world there came beautiful and ornate Masjids, elaborate Ḥammāms (public baths) and intricately designed complexes defined by their setting and the staggering geometry that governed their construction.

Muslim architecture influenced movements such as the Gothic style in the western world, and architects such as Sinān pioneered engineering principles and ideas which we see in his magnificent buildings today.

TRADE Trade routes are not only important for the economy, but it is along these routes that ideas are exchanged, knowledge passed on, and one societyʼs advancement shared with the rest. Muslim traders developed new and consolidated existing trade routes, and brought their Islām along with them on their travels. These traders would serve as the first representatives of Muslims in certain places, and would leave such an impression on some through their honesty and kindness that many would accept Islām.

CHEMISTRY The word chemistry comes from the Arabic word kīmiyā, and much like how the word has Arabic origins, the science similarly owes much to the work of Muslim chemists. Through developing methodical scientific processes, Muslim scientists worked on the classification of substances, developing acids, the processes in chemistry, precise scales, metal refinement and more. Alongside their practical work, they wrote books detailing their efforts, which would eventually be translated to form the basis of early modern chemistry.

EDUCATION One of the earliest universities in history is the University of Al-Qarawiyyīn in Fes, Morocco built in the 9th century. The Muslim world similarly hosted many other world-renowned destinations for learning, such as the Bayt al-Ḥikmah (House of Wisdom) in Baghdad which contained one of the worldʼs largest public libraries at the time. For centuries, Muslim lands were renowned destinations for learning, bridging the intellectual gap between Classical Agethe and the Enlightenment.

Muslims Around the World

Muslims Around In this you the World about will learn the expansion of Islām by the Ṣaḥābah, how and when Muslims When the Messenger reached certain ﷺ passed away, regions, and the Companions gain an you will immediately took Indigenous: native, appreciation of to the task of original inhabitants Muslims around taking Allāh ʼs of a land the world.message around the globe. They Dīn: religion were fearless in their efforts, taking on the Tābiʻīn: (lit. the superpowers of the world at the successors) the time, and unapologetically proclaiming Tawḥīd generation of from the warm sand dunes of West Africa to the believers after the gates of the far-east in China.

Ṣaḥābah Today, Muslims make up almost a quarter of the worldʼs population. Muslims can be found in almost every corner of the planet, and for a time, even in orbit. The diversity of the Ummah is a source of unity ﷺand pride, and the product of the efforts of Rasūlullāh , his Companions, and our pious predecessors who strove to spread the message of truth as far as possible.

UNITED KINGDOM Islām was known to the people of England long before Muslims settled on the British Isles, with even Shakespeare having Muslims in some of his plays!

Many of the first Muslims in Britain were reverts, and with later immigration, many Muslims moved to the UK, over time building a vibrant and active Muslim community.

WESTERN EUROPE Muslims first reached Europe in 711 AD (92 AH: not even a century from the Hijrah!) when they conquered al-Andalūs (the Iberian Peninsula). Over time, Muslims in Western Europe would bring Europe from its Dark Ages to its Renaissance, helping in building the modern world today. In the modern era, migration from former colonies has seen Muslim populations increase in Western Europe, and although they may face discrimination in some parts, they strive to maintain their Islamic identity.

RUSSIA The Ṣaḥābah were the first to reach the borders of modern-day Russia, and over the years, Muslim influence in the area would build a Muslim presence. Today, despite suffering repression under communism, Russia has the largest Muslim population in Europe, and they have built a distinct Muslim identity over the centuries they have lived in the region.

CENTRAL EUROPE Muslim populations in Central Europe grew through the Ottoman empire, and in later years, they have migrated to this area from different parts of the Muslim- majority world. Despite facing challenges, particularly during communist rule, Muslims in the area have seen a resurgence in faith and practice. Today, whilst many face difficulties in expressing their faith openly, Muslims are defiantly proud of their faith, continue to practise it and push to retain the right to do so.

CENTRAL ASIA This is an area steeped in Islamic heritage from the early Ṣaḥābah, with a legacy of Muslim scholars, students, institutions and stunningly beautiful Masājid. When this region suffered under Soviet communist rule, Muslims fought back to preserve their religion and secretly passed on their Islām to their children despite it being punishable to do so. Today, a resurgent Islām is part of the peopleʼs everyday life, bound to their culture and practices.

LEVANT Muslims reached this region under the Khilāfah of

رضي الله عنهʻUmar and have

remained ever since.

Palestine specifically, is close to the heart of every Muslim: being the birthplace and home for numerous Prophets, the first Qiblah of Islām, and the point from which the Messenger ﷺ ascended to the Heavens.

Today, Muslims remain a majority, and the region remains a place in which Muslims around the world yearn for peace and SOUTH ASIAN stability.

SUBCONTINENT From Muslims first reaching the ARABIAN PENINSULAarea through trade over the Indian Ocean, today the subcontinent, The birthplace of Islām, and the consisting of India, Pakistan, ﷺhome of the Prophet . The Bangladesh and other countries, Arabian Peninsula is largely hosts a significant percentage of uninhabited, due to it being mostly the worldwide Muslim population. covered in desert, but the few Muslims in this area have lived places where civilisation exists, there for over a thousand years, Muslims are the vast majority. and have developed a strong Islām reigns supreme over the land identity, established centres of of the Revelation, as it has since learning which branch across the the time of Rasūlullāh ﷺ. world, and began movements that have spread the message of Islām.

EAST ASIA Muslims reached China through the Silk Roads in the first few decades following the passing of Rasūlullāh ﷺ. There are even records of certain Ṣaḥābah reaching China, and supposedly meeting with the Chinese emperor at the time. Today, there are approximately 25 million Muslims in China, with the majority being Uyghur Muslims living in the Xinjiang province. Muslims in China continue to strive to be proud of their faith, and display it in their culture, their dress and everyday life.

SOUTHEAST ASIA This area includes Indonesia, Malaysia, Singapore, Thailand, and a host of countries and islands surrounding it. Muslims reached this region through trade, and now Southeast Asia contains the highest number of Muslims in the world with the identity of Muslims here unique and infused into their culture.

OCEANIA Australia and New Zealand boast vibrant and active Muslim communities, which have moved to these areas in recent years and centuries. Whilst most Muslims in these areas are immigrants who have moved for economic opportunities or for safer lives, they have established themselves within their new communities and become successful, contributing citizens.

NORTH AND WEST AFRICA North and West Africa is home to several countries with distinct traditions and cultures though they share a Muslim identity.

Islām first reached these lands under the Sahābah, Tābi‘īn and successive generations, and the people have remained upon the truth since the golden generation. Visiting these lands provides for an experience rich in history, hospitality and Islamic spirit.

NORTH AMERICA Whilst the first Muslims came to the North America via slavery, many Muslims who live there today arrived through immigration, though many are reverts from different communities. In a short span of time, Muslims have developed their own sense of identity, established themselves, and made their voice heard advocating Islamic values.

SOUTH AMERICA Muslims likely first reached South America even before Columbus. Muslims here comprise of a mix of migrants and indigenous converts, and there are continuing efforts to spread the Dīn of Allāh  to this Pick a region of interest & corner of the world as well.create a tourist pamphlet for a Muslim-friendly holiday package. Include historical sites and explore the areaʼs history.

CENTRAL AND EASTERN AFRICA During the Prophet ﷺʼs time, companions had migrated to parts of Eastern Africa, and over the centuries that would follow, Islām would find its way into these lands over the narrow Red Sea from Arabia.

Central Africa, whilst historically having a majority Christian population in the region, is home to a large and flourishing Muslim community.

SOUTHERN AFRICA Southern Africa boasts an influential population of Muslims who have built themselves a place to express their Islamic identity proudly in the past few centuries.

Muslims in South Africa have worked on significant contributions to the Muslim Ummah, for the lay person and the scholars, and continue to aid Muslims around the world in many different ways. We are very fortunate to be part of an Ummah which spans the entire globe. The Ṣaḥābah and many in our past spent their lives spreading the Dīn of Allāh , and we enjoy the fruits of their efforts today. Wherever in the world we go, there will be someone to whom we can offer Salām, with whom we may eat, and beside whom we may pray. Our only uniting ﷺfactor is our unwavering belief in Allāh and His Messenger . The beauty of Islām is found in the Ummah of the ﷺMessenger , as he himself said:

Whoever possesses the following three qualities will experience the sweetness of faith: The one to whom Who hates to revert Who loves a person Allāh and His to disbelief as and loves them Apostle becomes much as they hate only for Allāhʼs dearer than to be thrown into sake. anything else.the fire.

Living Islām

Family

the will cover need for family, We as human beings are social beings, and Allāh has created us with the need to be the status of with others. We need to laugh, smile at one another, enjoy good company, love, and share maintaining happiness. We also need people to lean on during hard times, help from those close to us, and people to share our sadness and grief with. For this, Allāh has created our Islām, and what is family bonds and ties, and then embedded them into communities, tribes, and people. considered family.

Islām places great importance on maintaining those ties: of family and of community, not only for the rights they have over us, but also for the benefit we gain in keeping those relationships strong.

Ṣilat ar-Raḥim: maintaining ties of kinship Kabā’ir: major sins As we get older, we may move away from our parents and families to build our own, or to pursue career ambitions or opportunities. It is likely that we see less of those whom we were so familiar with earlier. Whilst this may happen, we should take care to remember that Islām still asks us to maintain close family and communal relations. Modern technology has allowed us so many avenues to keep up our family ties, and we should utilise them. Our families are the pillars that hold us up, and regardless of where we are in the world, we as Muslims are expected to keep them close.

The Qurʼān and Sunnah place a special emphasis on maintaining ties and close family bonds. On one hand, there is ﷺmention of great reward for those who keep good ties of kinship, as when the Prophet said, Whoever loves that he be granted more wealth, and that his lease of life be prolonged, then he should keep good familial relations.

MUSLIM

On the other hand, severing the family bonds is considered a serious offence, one which warrants punishment in this ﷺworld and the hereafter. The Prophet said, There is no sin more worthy of Allāh hastening the punishment upon its practitioner in the world – in addition to what is in store for him in the Hereafter – than tyranny and severing the ties of kinship.

PARENTS There are no people in our lives who deserve our love, respect, kindness, and mercy as much as our parents. Allāh says, For your Lord has decreed that you… honour your parents. If one, or both of them reach old age in your care, never say to them ūeven ‘uff’ (the slightest sound of displeasure), nor yell at them. Rather, address them respectfully. And be humble with them out of mercy, and pray, ‘My Lord! Be merciful to them as they raised me when I was young.’ QUR’ĀN 17:23-24 Our parents brought us up, nurtured and loved us when we were young and fragile, unable to support ourselves. They deserve the best of ourselves, at every stage in our lives regardless of circumstance. The status of parents in Islām is highly emphasised. Often, as we grow out of their protective shade from being children to adolescents and then adults, one may feel their connection with their parents weakening as they become more ﷺindependent. This is opposite to what Islām asks of us, however. Rasūlullāh once said, Let him be humbled into dust! Let him be humbled into dust! Let him be humbled into dust! It was said: Oh Allāh's ﷺMessenger, who? He said: He who sees either, or both of his parents during their old age, but he does not enter Paradise (through serving them well).

MUSLIM

ﷺRasūlullāh said, People are like mines of gold and silver.

MUSLIM

This Ḥadīth points to the fact that every person has a talent which they may utilise, and thus every person has something, regardless of how seemingly small, to contribute to their community. As Muslims it is our responsibility to contribute and seek out those talents for collective benefit, so that we may have a wide range of expertise contributing to the good of society.

Islām places a special focus on taking advice from others, and especially the advice of those more experienced than ourselves. The Prophet of Allāh took advice from his uncles before marriage, from his wife after revelation, and from the Companions on innumerable occasions. Those who are older are undoubtedly more experienced, and as the

رضي الله عنهKhalīfah Muʻāwiyah observed,

There is no wise man except through experience. The wisdom of the elders is a resource, a 'wellspring' that we should nourish ourselves from, by seeking their company and counsel.

Another important aspect of being part of a community is making good with our ﷺefforts to assist others within that community. The famous Ḥadīth of Rasūlullāh mentions that, None of you will have ūcomplete faith till he wishes forhis ūMuslim brother what he likes for himself.

BUKHĀRĪ

This Ḥadīth not only illustrates the altruism and generosity that we should show to each other, but also the camaraderie and unity, where we sincerely desire and hope that good reaches others, even if it may be at our own expense. A true believer is one who wishes well for others, helps them when they are in need, and works to actively improve the lives of others within their vicinity.

HOW CAN I HELP? disenfranchisedIt is natural that at times we may feel from the communities we live in, or that we have little power to help despite really wanting to. At times, we may become frustrated at stagnation around us, and wish to impact huge changes. In those moments, we should take a second to reflect. Change comes through calculated and measured actions which are made through consultation Mashwarah() and deliberation, and we need to take heed of that. We should try and consult with others who may have expertise and knowledge, and leverage that to improve our communities. Communities flourish when individuals with various specialities in different fields come together for a common good, and our aim should be to create an environment that actualises that.

The Muslims left everything: wealth, over themselves, homes, and families, and migrated to Madīnah with nothing but what they could carry. However, in an example so extraordinary even though they that it was preserved in the Qurʼān, the Anṣār of Madīnah gave up may themselves be their livelihoods, families, and homes to accommodate for their afflicted by poverty.

arriving brethren. Allāh makes a special mention of them in the Qurʼān by describing them as such people who...

QURʼĀN 59:9

Anṣār literally means helpers, and they are called as such due to the incredible sacrifices they made to accommodate their Makkan brothers and sisters.

DA‘WAH ﷺThe Ummah of Rasūlullāh has been sent with a responsibility to assist each other by enjoining good and forbidding evil. We have a duty to advise fellow Muslims, whether that be in telling them about good they must or can do, or in evil Da‘wahthey must refrain from. Calling others to better their practice of Islām is called .

TawḥīdWe also have a responsibility to invite others to Islām and welcome them into the community of . Allāh says, You are the best Ummah ever raised for mankind. You enjoin good and forbid what is wrong, and you believe in Allāh.

QURʼĀN 3:110

We are fortunate to be blessed with Īmān, and this is a blessing we should wish to share with every human alive so that they may be saved from eternal ruin. The effort to spread our religion to others is also called Da‘wah, and it is an invitation we can make through various means. Firstly, we give Da‘wah of Islām to non- Muslims through our character and morals by exemplifying the beauty of our Dīn in our everyday interactions. In this, ﷺour Messenger was the greatest of examples, and he showed us how it was good character, more so than good arguments, which won over people to Islām.

Secondly, we give Da‘wah through our actions. Actions speak louder than words, and our disciplined practice of our Dīn which does not change with time, place, person or occasion will show how much Islām means to us, and inspire respect of it within others. On the other hand, if a person preaches Islām, but does not follow the commandments they preach, their words will certainly lack effect.

Lastly and most importantly, it is our responsibility to spread our Dīn through actively calling others to Islām. This is the ﷺresponsibility given to prophets, and for this Ummah, it was passed down from the Messenger to every member of the Ummah. Allāh says, And whose words are better than someone who calls ūothers to Allāh, does good, and says, ‘I am truly one of those who submit.’

QURʼĀN 41:33

WHEN GIVING DA‘WAH, WE SHOULD REMEMBER:

Be sincere and only give Da‘wah for the sake of Allāh Speak kindly following the example of Rasūlullāh ﷺ Use tact and wisdom when giving Da‘wah Invite to the Way of your Lord with wisdom and kind advice, and only with them in the best manner.

THE OTHER SIDE As Muslims, it is our responsibility to ensure we surround ourselves with good people and remain far from those who would have a negative influence. A common slippery slope that youngsters fall into is gang culture, leading them to knife and gun crime, consumption and supplying of drugs, violence, and in many instances, the heinous sin of murder.

Getting involved in gangs is a deadly trap, and once joining, it is often very difficult to leave as many gangs will use blackmail and threats to force compliance. There is no real reputation or honour to be gained through hurting and terrorising others, and we should maintain our honour, the honour of our family and our we never involve ourselves in such terrible practices. If one is involved in gangs or similar criminal , remember there are ways out.

Make constant Duʻāʼ to Allāh , seek professional help, and never lose hope. In groups, mindmap ways to improve your local community.

Share ideas with other groups and decide on three projects as a class to create positive change. Collaborate, inspire, and make a difference!

Every step taken in walking to the Masjid brings reward.

Rasūlullāh ﷺ mentioned that the greater number of steps taken in walking to the Masjid bring about forgiveness of sins and a weighty increase in good deeds.

Itʼs good exercise! For those of us who can walk to the Masjid, the walk is beneficial to us physically. AT HOME Masjid literally means ‘a place of prostration’, and we should have such a place dedicated to worship in our homes ﷺif possible. The Messenger encouraged performing good acts within the home, and he himself would perform Nafl at home. Performing such acts brings barakah and encourages the rest of the family. For a woman, the best place for her Salāh is her home, and she should set a place aside for herself so she may perform it calmly with Khushū’ and devotion.

THE THREE MASĀJID Do not set out on a journey (for religious devotion) but for the three Masjids: for this Masjid of mine (at Madīnah), the Sacred Masjid (at Makkah), and the Masjid al-Aqṣā (Bait al-Maqdis).

MUSLIM

MASJID AL-ḤARĀM, MAKKAH The first Masjid built for Allāh ʼs worship in the city of Makkah, nourished by the divinely-provided well of Zamzam. The worshipper at this blessed area finds their prayer to be multiplied in reward 100,000 times over.

Masjid al-Ḥarām is our Qiblah, the direction of our worship, and the destination for our pilgrimage. It is the greatest place on earth, and we should try to visit it as often as possible.

MASJID AN-NABAWĪ ﷺ, MADĪNAH MUNAWWARAH ﷺIn the blessed city of our Messenger , surrounded by the mountains of Uḥud, and housing the final resting place ﷺof our and Allāh ʼs beloved, is the Masjid of Rasūlullāh . The city is pleasantly temperate and peaceful; the ﷺMasjid gracefully welcoming, as though embodying the smile, warmth and reception our Messenger would offer to each visitor over 14 centuries ago. Madīnah is an oasis for the heart, healing and soothing for every believer, and creates a yearning within one and all to return. Ṣalāh here is multiplied in reward 1,000 times over.

Free-Mixing

what is will cover free-mixing, why ﷺThe Sharīʻah of Islām that Allāh sent down to His Messenger Muḥammad was sent it is forbidden in to promote healthy societies that are constantly aware of Allāh . To this end, Islām has Islāmsome , and legislated laws and practices that prevent societal degradation and public vice as much rules regarding ﷺas they promote individual good and moral virtues. Allāh and His Messenger have free-mixing. provided us with laws relating to many things, including trade, family, and interactions with others, so that our experiences with others will not only be free from sin and foster good, but also will not lead to any harmful and immoral practices.

Allāh is our Creator, and thus He recognises our inherent frailties and weaknesses better than even ourselves. It is therefore befitting that Allāh has made laws which govern our interactions. Through His wisdom, Allāh has determined that Ikhtilāṭ, free-mixing for unrelated men and women, is forbidden for the immorality  it could lead to. Allāh mentions in the Qurʼān, Legislate: to make or enact laws O Prophet! Tell the believing men to Nafs: capricious self lower their gaze and or ego of a person guard their chastity.

Maḥram That is purer for (pl. QURʼĀN 24:31

WHY IS FREE MIXING FORBIDDEN?

One of the wisdoms for the ruling of impermissibility for decreases the possibility and occurrences of Zinā (fornication/adultery). Allāh mentions in the Qurʼān, And do not even go close to fornication. It is indeed a shameful act, and an evil way to follow.

QURʼĀN 17:32

The emphasis on not even going close to it is important here, as certain actions are such that they are similar to a slippery slope: the smallest step in their direction leads to bigger mistakes and even greater damage to a person.

Another reason for Islāmʼs position is that if Zinā does become widespread, it usually leads to the destruction of family units within a society. These family units are integral to strong communities and nations, and their loss often precedes civil strife and disorder. Islām values the upbringing of children and the love of a family which is shared between those within the family. Islām also values that people are connected through families and communities, and that a personʼs lineage is pure from immorality. For this reason, Allāh  has created laws which govern us in such a way that they tackle the very roots of what causes such problems and remove any possibility from the very outset.

ﷺThus, it is not merely the act of Zinā which is sinful, but rather all that leads to it. The Messenger of Allāh said, The adultery of the eye is the (lustful) look, and the adultery of the tongue is (lustful) speech. The heart desires and yearns, which the private parts may or may not put into effect.

MUSLIM

Thus, by intermingling with those of the opposite gender, it is likely that sins will be committed. For this reason, Islām advises us to keep our interactions only to what is necessary.

In the topic of free-mixing, Taqwā (god-consciousness) is vitally important. Taqwā is being constantly aware of Allāh , and it is a fundamental characteristic of a believer, as it allows them to live in a manner pleasing to Allāh . Having Taqwā means that while there may be situations where we have to battle our desires and the inclinations of our Nafs, our awareness of Allāh will help us through those situations whilst adhering to the guidelines of Sharīʻah. It is vital we build our Taqwā, as ultimately it is only awareness of Allāh which will stop us from falling into sin.

DESIRES In the Qurʼān, Allāh likens the desires of some people to be like a god, whose orders are followed religiously.

Allāh says, Have you seen he who has taken his desires as his god?

QURʼĀN 45:23

Our impermissible inclinations are not to be followed, but rather to be overcome, and made to submit to the command of Allāh . On the Day of Judgement, it will be no justification to say one felt a certain way and so they committed an action. Allāh has endowed humanity with reason and revelation, and our intellect should lead us to being above base desires and instinctual inclinations.

Every person has been created with Shahwah (desire), and it is natural to feel an inclination to the opposite sex. Within some, the inclination may be towards the same sex, and they may wish to act upon it, which is impermissible in Islām. The test of this life is not on how we feel, but rather on how we react to our feelings and desires. Allāh will not take us to task over our thoughts and feelings so long as we do not entertain and act upon them. Thus, the test for everyone, regardless of their inclination, is in them following the guidelines set out by Allāh . The one who does so, is successful in the hereafter, and the one who follows only their desires, will be eternally unsuccessful.

WHAT IS NECESSARY, OR WHAT ARE THE EXCEPTIONS? In todayʼs world, it is very difficult if not wholly unrealistic to suggest that one might live life without interacting with the opposite gender. Fortunately, Allāh has provided us with guidelines by which we may live, and the ﷺexample of our Messenger Muḥammad to follow. Adhering to such guidelines, whilst they may be difficult at times, will hopefully enable us to live our lives according to how Allāh wants us to live, and keep us away from sinful acts.

GENERAL RULES We are not allowed to Islām forbids any bodily contact between be alone in an enclosed non-maḥram men and women. This includes place with someone of handshakes and embraces, as well as everything the opposite gender besides. Doing so in a confident but respectful manner often brings about respect and admiration, and most will happily respect your wishes.

SADD ADH-DHARĀʼIʻ Within Islamic law, there is a term known as 'Sadd adh-Dharāʼiʻ'. This term is a legal term which is based around a concept within Islamic law of preventing evil from occurring. It allows for laws to be made and explains earlier laws which labelled something as 'impermissible' or 'close to impermissible' due to it leading to something definitively Ḥarām. When something Ḥarām cannot be done except via or through certain means, then depending on the likelihood of those means being used for the (Ḥarām) objective in question, it may be considered impermissible as well. For example, wine cannot be made without grapes, therefore the growing of grapes is a means to the production of wine. However, due to the relatively insignificant likelihood of wine being produced from every grape produce, the growing of grapes is permissible. On the other hand, selling of grapes - which by default is permissible – to a wine producer would be impermissible, due to the high likelihood of those grapes being used in the production of wine, which is impermissible.

SHUʼAB AL-ĪMĀN Marriage in Islām is important for the role it plays in creating healthy families, Walī: Islamic legal guardian fulfilling the human need for intimacy, and expanding the Ummah. It is a means of safeguarding oneʼs faith, protecting oneʼs modesty and chastity, Istikhārah: a special prayer and promoting social stability. THE NEED FOR MARRIAGE ﷺRasūlullāh said, 0 youth! Those amongst you who can support a wife should marry, for it restrains eyes (from casting evil glances) and preserves one from immorality; but he who cannot afford it should fast, for it is a means of controlling the sexual desire.

MUSLIM

Marriage is a life-changing step, as it comes with responsibilities and a new role to play. It should not be taken lightly, and one should prepare themselves adequately. Living with someone else and being responsible for another requires a certain level of emotional stability and maturity, and whilst a part of this is developed after marriage, one should also prepare oneself beforehand. For men, being financially able to support a wife is part of marriage, and he should prepare to do so. A man should be adequately capable of supporting his wife, and this should be factored into plans for marriage. At the same time however, as Muslims, we believe in rizq (sustenance) being provided by Allāh , and so one should not forego marriage because they feel they need to meet a certain threshold of wealth such as purchasing a house or earning a particular wage. If one can get married, and is financially able to do so, then they should look to do so. THE DECISION If either of the potential bride or groom decide they do not wish to marry the other, the marriage should not go forward. The families of either should not pressure them to get married, as the issues which may occur later are far worse than any indignity in rejection now.
