PREPARATION AND EXPENDITURE ﷺRasūlullāh said, The marriage which produces most blessing is the least in expenditure.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

There is more Barakah (blessings) in a marriage which foregoes extravagant expenditure and innovative customs. In the lead up to the big day, one may prepare by purchasing clothes and gifts, and arranging for the day of the wedding.

ﷺHowever, we should remember the words of the Prophet , and that Allāh loves simplicity and sincerity. The wedding should not become a financial burden on the family or the couple-to-be. Our marriages should not be grand displays of wealth, and our joy should not make us forget the commandments of Allāh .

 ﷺAllāh and His Messenger have emphasised the importance of good company, and so we should make a point to invite the pious to our events and ceremonies. We should ensure that our events always comply with the guidelines of Sharīʻah, and do not contain any free mixing, music, dancing, and similar impermissible .

SETTING THE MAHR The Mahr is money given by the groom to his bride in lieu of her hand in marriage. The Mahr is the womanʼs divine right, and none can deny her of it. Allāh says, Give women their doweries graciously.

QURʼĀN 4:4

It is necessary for the groom to give the Mahr, regardless of whether it was demanded in the Nikāḥ ceremony or not. The amount given in Mahr must be above ten dirhams in value, and there is no maximum value. However, it is preferable that such a high Mahr is not fixed as it may deter suitable prospective grooms. The Mahr is decided between the bride and groom, and forms part of their marriage contract.

THE CEREMONY Nikāḥ is a blessed ceremony marking the beginning of a new journey. It is to be celebrated and enjoyed, and thus it is preferable for it to be conducted in the centre of every Muslimʼs life: the Masjid, and with the Muslims present. The Nikāḥ will be performed by the Imām in the Masjid, and the Imām will recite a Khuṭbah wherein he will mention verses of the Qurʼān and Aḥādīth on the merits of Nikāḥ, followed by the details of the marriage contract for all present to witness.

Nikāḥ is performed with an offer (Ījāb) and acceptance (Qabūl). It is a contract, though a blessed and unique one, and requires consent from both parties and their confirmation. Usually, the Ījāb comes from the bride, and her consent and offer will be represented by a Wakīl (representative). The groom will be asked if he accepts the offer, and he will reply with 'I have accepted her' or similar words in the past tense. For the Nikāḥ to be valid, there must be at least two witnesses (two males, or one male and two females) in the Nikāḥ ceremony to witness the offer of marriage and acceptance. As the bride will often be represented on her part in the Masjid, it is advisory for two witnesses to be present for her consent to her representative to avoid any potential future disagreements.

WALĪMAH The Walīmah is a meal given by the husband following the consummation of the marriage, or a private meeting between the bride and groom for the first time. It is a Sunnah to provide the Walīmah, and it is the only meal related to the marriage which one is encouraged to give. Any meal from the bride and her family is not required. The Walīmah meal should not be extravagant, but rather simple with the purpose of feeding others out of happiness and to increase Barakah.

MARRIED LIFE Married life is one of love and mercy, highs and lows, compromises and brokering. Marriage is a binding contract till Jannah, and one should make every effort on their part to keep their marriage stable and secure. This means stopping oneself from saying something negative even if one may be in the right. A personʼs marriage, and the happiness of their spouse is far more valuable than an insignificant argument won or having the last word.

Whilst both spouses have certain rights and responsibilities as given by Sharīʻah, one should not see their relationship with their spouse to be one in which they demand certain rights and responsibilities to be fulfilled. Rather, through consultation, an appreciation of context and circumstance, and through tender affection of each other, the husband and wife should negotiate their lives together whilst always maintaining the dictates of Sharīʻah in mind. Such a marriage will yield a beautiful relationship, pleasing to Allāh and pleasing to the spouses.

RIGHTS OF THE WIFE MAHR The wife has the full right to her Mahr and denying her the Mahr is a grave sin.

NAFAQAH The husband must provide for the wife, regardless of her ability to provide for herself. This includes food, clothing, lodging and necessary financial support according to his standard of living.

KIND TREATMENT Allāh  says in the Qurʼān, “” And live with them in a kind manner.

QURʼĀN 4:19

A man should not abuse his position within the household, or the strength Allāh has given him through unjust treatment of his wife. A person will be rewarded for the kindness they show and what they spend on their spouse.

PROTECTION OF HONOUR It is the husbandʼs responsibility to ensure the safety of his wife, and alongside that, he should never speak ill of her in front of others. He should keep matters between himself and his wife private and address them with her directly.

SPENDING TIME WITH HER It is a right of a wife that her husband spends time with her. Besides attending the Masjid for Ṣalāh, work and other necessary requirements, a man should spend his time at home with his wife and children, educating them and raising them spiritually.

OBEDIENCE Allāh has placed the responsibility of the household on the man, and with it leadership.

Whilst the wife deserves to be consulted and have her views heard, the final decision rests upon the husband, and he deserves that his decision is respected, and obeyed (so long as it does not break a law of Allāh ).

PROTECTION OF HONOUR The wife should protect the honour of her husband by defending and speaking good of him in his absence, and refraining from ever speaking ill of him to others. The matters of the home should remain within the home, and the issues between spouses should remain private.

PROTECTION OF THE HOME The wife should not allow anyone into the home of her husband whom he would not like in their home.

PROTECTION OF WEALTH The wife should not spend her husbandʼs wealth except with his permission, even if it may be for something commendable such as charity.

RIGHTS OF THE HUSBAND

INTIMACY WITHIN MARRIAGE One of the purposes of marriage is the fulfilment of desires inherent within every human being, by which we save ourselves, families, and communities from the harm of Zinā (fornication/adultery). Intimacy is a crucial aspect of marriage, and spouses having positive intimate experiences with each other increases their love and affection for one another. Problems within intimacy should also be addressed delicately but frankly between spouses, as it can often lead to unresolved feelings and tensions, which may extend to further harm. The Qurʼān and Ḥadīth give reference to intimacy in various places, and hint at encouragement of the passionate fulfilment of desires with oneʼs spouse.

Tenderness, beautification, kissing, and playfulness are referenced, and are important to intimacy. Foreplay in intimacy allows for better enjoyment and the greater likelihood of fulfilment of pleasure for both spouses.

Importantly, the Qurʼān and Ḥadīth make references without doing so Ḥayāʼexplicitly. We should follow in this example and display in matters of intimacy. Ḥayāʼ in intimacy means keeping the matters of intimacy private, being intimate with oneʼs spouse only in private, and refraining from immodest acts which others may practise. Where the need to discuss an issue may arise, it should similarly be conducted in a manner befitting of Ḥayāʼ.

BUKHĀRĪ Intimacy should be preceded by Duʻāʼ and succeeded by Ghusl (which is Farḍ), or if it is to be delayed, then Wuḍūʼ. However Ghusl still remains obligatory and must be done at the earliest opportunity. There are certain supplications one should memorise and recite, and similarly one should learn the various rules and prohibitions relating to intimacy before marriage. These can be found in books by scholars on the matter, courses, or approaching scholars directly. Similarly, advice relating to the matter of intimacy may be found there.

CONTRACEPTION There are two types of contraceptive methods: reversible and irreversible. Irreversible contraception is impermissible. On the other hand, certain reversible contraceptive methods may be permissible with a valid Sharʻī reason. For example, if a woman is weak and unable to sustain pregnancy at the moment. Before using any contraception, one should firstly determine if the contraceptive method is permissible, followed by checking whether it is suitable for the short-term and long-term health of both spouses. Finally, and importantly, the usage of contraceptives is dependent on the consent of husband and wife, and this should be explicitly sought prior.

CHILDREN Children are a blessing from Allāh , and they are a responsibility in the care of their parents. They require nurture and upbringing through a mixture of tender treatment and love, alongside firm, consistent rules, and discipline. The upbringing of children may determine their futures, and Islām encourages parents to be active in their childrenʼs emotional, spiritual, religious, and educational development.

BIRTH OF A CHILD The birth of a child is a momentous occasion of joy for the parents, the family, and the community. The child represents an increase in the Ummah and a blessing from Allāh . To begin the process of Tarbiyah, and in gratitude to Allāh , Islām has ordained certain practices to be performed.

Children are the backbone of the Muslim Ummah, ﷺand Rasūlullāh encouraged having more children and large families. More children allow for larger extended families and the Barakah that comes with them, as well as larger and better-connected communities. The Qurʼān instructs us to not 'kill' children out of fear of poverty, from which we understand that family planning, whilst important, should not be seen purely from the financial perspective.

ADHĀN The Adhān will be said in the right ear of the child, and the Iqāmah will be delivered in the left ear immediately after birth.

TAḤNĪK It is Sunnah to place part of a softened or chewed date in the mouth of a child upon birth, followed by making Duʻāʼ for the child.

NAMING The child should be given an honourable name with a good meaning. A child may be named after a prophet, Ṣahābī / Ṣahābiyyah, or a pious individual.

ʻAQĪQAH In gratitude to Allāh for the child, parents should offer an animal sacrifice called ʻAqīqah on the seventh day. Two animals acceptable for Uḍḥiyah will be sacrificed for a new-born boy, and one animal for a girl.

SHAVING THE HAIR The hair on the new-bornʼs head will be shaved on the seventh day, and its weight in silver or the equivalent in money will be given in charity.

CIRCUMCISION It is Sunnah to have a baby boy circumcised. This is good for hygienic reasons, and forms part of the natural practice (Fiṭrah).

TARBIYAH Tarbiyah is an Arabic word meaning to take something stage by stage to completion. In the Islamic sense, it refers to bringing up a child through their various stages in life to mature into productive and well-rounded individuals. Such ﷺchildren are sources of reward for their parents, and badges of pride for their families and communities. Rasūlullāh said: WHEN A PERSON DIES ALL THEIR GOOD DEEDS COME TO AN END EXCEPT THREE:

ONGOING CHARITY BENEFICIAL KNOWLEDGE AND A RIGHTEOUS CHILD WHO PRAYS FOR THEM.

NASĀʼĪ

ﷺTarbiyah then is a vital part of having a child. The Messenger said, Indeed, every one of you is a shepherd, and every one of you will be questioned about his flock.

BUKHĀRĪ

This metaphor relates to the responsibility of oneʼs family, and their spiritual and emotional nurturing. Children require tender care coupled with firm and consistent rules. They require a steady effort to build within them a trust in Allāh , and a habit of performing good deeds. Parenting is a full-time role in this regard, as children will learn from their parents through what they say, and most importantly, what they do themselves. Your cousin is going to have a child. They have messaged you to ask what they should do following the birth. steps in the form of a .

The belief in Allāh is the most important of all that a parent may impart to their child. Nurturing children to have a firm belief, and an understanding of their Dīn is the first and most important part of parenting.

Alongside that, parents are responsible for teaching children good character, by modelling it for them, correcting them when they go wrong, and praising them when they do good. Beyond that, being fair with them, spending time and money on them, and showing them affection are all important aspects of parenting. It is important to keep oneself informed as a parent on how to bring up oneʼs child, and the challenges they face as they get older. Attending courses on parenting from the Islamic perspective may be beneficial. Prior to marriage or having children, it is important to look for such courses and material so one may be adequately informed as they move into parenthood.

DIVORCE ﷺThe Messenger of Allāh said, The most hated of permissible things to Allāh is divorce.

IBN MĀJAH

Divorce in Islām is called Ṭalāq, and it is the last resort of a couple for whom there seems no hope of reconciliation or continuation in their marriage. It is not a decision to be rushed into, nor one to be made on a whim. Divorce proceedings in Islām should only be conducted once sincere and earnest efforts to resolve marital issues by the family and METHODS OF qualified Muslim practitioners have been exhausted.

RECONCILIATION BETWEEN THE COUPLE If an issue were to arise within a marriage, the spouses should firstly attempt to resolve the matter themselves through honest and respectful conversation. Marriage is sharing a life with another person, and rather than letting any issue fester, it should be addressed in a way that oneʼs spouse does not feel humiliated.

BETWEEN THE FAMILY If the couple cannot resolve an issue amongst themselves, they should approach experienced and respected members of the family for advice and arbitration. Family members will work in the interests of the couple out of love for them, and often, from experience, they may provide solutions to resolve the conflict.

MUSLIM PROFESSIONAL COUNSELLOR OR QUALIFIED SCHOLAR If matters cannot be resolved between the families of the spouses, then they should seek external support through a Muslim counsellor or scholar. This may be an Imām with experience in marriage mediation, or a Muslim professional who works with spouses.

Death & Bereavement

HOW DIVORCE IS ISSUED Khula’: the proposition of divorce from the If matters between the spouses cannot be resolved, and they wish to continue with wife in exchange of a divorce, then they may do so. In Islām, only the husband has the power to issue returning the Mahr or divorce, whilst the wife may resort to Khula’ (proposition of divorce) through mutual another sum. negotiation.

THERE ARE TWO TYPES OF ṬALĀQ IN SHARĪʻAH:

Ṭalāq Rajʻī is issued with explicit words, such as 'I give you Ṭalāq'. If the husband says it once, then one will occur. If he issues a second one later, or if he had issued two at once, then two will have occurred. The woman will begin her ʻIddah immediately following the divorce being issued.

ṬALĀQ RAJʻĪ REVOCABLE DIVORCEIf after issuing one or two divorces, the husband wishes to take her back in his marriage, he may do so without a new Nikāḥ if it is within the ʻIddah period. However, if the ʻIddah period has passed, then a new Nikāḥ will be required with her consent.

Ṭalāq Bā’in is issued with figurative words which have a meaning of Ṭalāq, such as 'It’s over'. The intention of Ṭalāq must also be present on uttering such words. If the husband intends one Ṭalāq, only one will occur. If he intends two, or ṬALĀQ BĀʼIN eventually issues it a second time (after remarriage), then two will have occurred. The woman will begin her ‘Iddah immediately following the IRREVOCABLE DIVORCE divorce being issued. If after issuing one or two irrevocable divorces, they wish to reconcile during or after the ʻIddah period, a new Nikāḥ will have to take place. If after two divorces from any of the two above categories, the husband issues a third divorce, explicitly or figuratively, then the third and final divorce will take place. After this divorce, they cannot reconcile and will be permanently separated. After the third and final divorce, the man and woman cannot remarry unless the woman marries another man, consummates the marriage, and is divorced by him. This is known as Ḥalālah. It is Ḥarām to pre-condition a Ḥalālah marriage to facilitate a remarriage between the spouses. If this is done however, the remarriage will be valid. It is extremely disliked and sinful to issue three divorces at once, whether using explicit or figurative words. If this is done however, three Ṭalāqs will have been given. This is known as Ṭalāq Mughallaẓah. The ideal method of issuing Ṭalāq is to issue it in a woman’s Ṭuhr period wherein one has not had intimate relations with their wife. Only one Ṭalāq should be issued, without anger and after having exhausted other means of reconciliation.

THE ‘IDDAH PERIOD ʻIddah: the waiting period a divorcee or widow must observe before remarrying.

ACCOMMODATION DURING ʻIDDAH During the period of ‘Iddah, a divorcee will remain in the house of her husband, and the widow will remain in the house of her late husband. During this period, the expenses of the divorced woman will be borne by the husband during the Memorise the Duʻāʼ in the ‘Iddah, whilst the widow may use the share she inherits to cover her expenses.

Qurʼān 25:74, learn its The woman in ‘Iddah will not leave the house except due to dire need (such as meaning and aim to make this a widow who needs to provide for herself).

Duʻāʼ after every Ṣalāh.

If, during the ‘Iddah period, the husband during their ‘Iddah. This is called Iḥdād. MUSLIM

LAST MOMENTS The last moments of a personʼs life are incredibly significant, both for the person and for their family. For a Muslim, these moments can secure a personʼs salvation by their utterance of a few words. For the family, it is the final goodbye to a loved one, and often a place of mutual compassion and care during a time of grief. During the personʼs final moments, be careful to adhere to the ﷺguidelines given to us by Rasūlullāh .

Refrain from saying or doing anything that might displease Allāh . We should rather engage ourselves in the recitation of Sūrah Yāsīn, and in Talqīn (reciting the Kalimah near the person close to death) to remind them to recite: We should not instruct the person directly, but rather simply read in their presence.

Immediately after death, Over 56 million deaths the eyes and mouth of occur annually. That is the deceased should be closed if it is still open. The approximately 150,000 limbs should be straightened, and the body may daily, 6,000 hourly, be covered with a clean sheet. The family of 106 every minute, and the deceased may now proceed with funeral nearly 2 deaths every arrangements, and where necessary, in second. compliance with the laws of the country, inform the relevant authorities.

Once a person has passed away, the process of preparing the body and burial takes place. In Islām, we GHUSL treat the body with respect, and for one last time, clean the body in preparation for the Janāzah Ṣalāh to be performed over it. The process of cleaning and preparing the body is as follows: Do not comb or cut the hair or nails of the deceased, but remove any jewellery, dentures, etc.

Remove all clothing and prepare the body for Ghusl by covering it with a cloth, blocking the nostrils, ears, and mouth with cotton wool, and performing Wuḍūʼ on the body. If the deceased passed away in the state of major ritual impurity (Ḥadath al-Akbar), then the mouth and nose will also be wetted using wet cotton wool.

Wearing gloves, wash the private area with a cloth. The head and beard should be washed.

Whilst ensuring privacy for the body using cloth, tilt the body to its left side and scrub it with 6 soap whilst pouring water, starting from the head and along the body, ensuring that water reaches the left underside of the body. The same process will be repeated with the body tilted on its right side.

Raise the top half of the body and gently massage the stomach. Wipe and wash away any waste.

Wuḍūʼ will not be repeated. The Ghusl (steps 6-8) should be repeated two more times, to complete the Sunnah.

Dry the body with a clean towel preparing it for enshrouding. During this process, the ʻAwrah of the body should never be exposed.

It is preferable to use a white Kafan for shrouding.

KAFAN The cloths used and the process is as follows:

The funeral prayer is performed with the body of the deceased placed in front of the Imām.

JANĀZAH ṢALĀH There is no Rukūʻ or Sajdah in Janāzah Ṣalāh. There will be four Takbīrāt in Ṣalāh.

FIRST TAKBĪR This is the Takbīr Taḥrīmah: Raise your hands and say 'Allāhū Akbar'.

Fold the hands as in Ṣalāh. Recite the Duʻāʼ al-Istiftāḥ of Janāzah Ṣalāh.

SECOND TAKBĪR Say Takbīr (Allāhū Akbar) again without raising the hands.

Recite Durūd Ibrāhīm.

THIRD TAKBĪR Say Takbīr again without raising the hands.

Recite the relevant Duʻāʼ for the deceased.

FOURTH TAKBĪR Say Takbīr for the last time without raising the hands. Thereafter, turn your head to the right and left, saying 'Assalāmu-ʻalaykum wa- raḥmatullāh' for each turn.

BURIAL In Islām, we are told to hasten in burying the body after death. The ﷺMessenger said, When a funeral is ready and the men carry the deceased on their shoulders, if it (the deceased) was a pious ūperson then they will say, 'Present me quickly'.

BUKHĀRĪ

A Muslim will wish to be received and welcomed by the heavens and its inhabitants, and we should hasten to fulfil that wish. From the moment of death, the processes of preparing, transporting, and burying the body should be completed as quickly as possible, though with due care and attention. In certain countries, it may be necessary to comply with certain regulations such as obtaining a death certificate, and such matters should be attended to quickly and properly.

Besides this, there are some other points to bear in mind: The body should not be moved to another country or city. The burial should take place in the nearest graveyard. The body should be carried on the shoulders to the grave.

It is desirable for the close relatives of the deceased to enter the grave to lower the body.

There are two types of graves:

LAḤAD: SHIQQ: A small recess is made on the side facing Qiblah at A shallow trench is dug in the bottom of the grave to allow for the body to be placed the centre of the grave. This grave inside it. This grave is used where the ground is firm.is used where the ground is soft.

AḤMAD

Following the burial, Duʻāʼ should be made for the deceased.

BEREAVEMENT Grief is a natural emotion that Allāh has created within a person. It is an expression of sadness that comes from ﷺa place of mercy and love, and it is something we should embrace. The Messenger of Allāh wept at the passing of his loved ones, and when asked about his tears, he replied, It is mercy which Allāh has lodged in the hearts of His slaves, and indeed Allāh is merciful only to those of His slaves who are merciful.

BUKHĀRĪ

When someone close to us passes away, it is completely natural to feel grief. The death of our loved ones is a test from Allāh , and we succeed by observing Ṣabr (patience).

Allāh says in the Qurʼān: We shall certainly test you by afflicting you with fear, hunger, loss of properties and lives and produce. Give glad tidings then, to those who remain patient; those who, when difficulty meets them, they say:�

�وَُعَحَارَ هُْيْلا اتُاوهِلل اتُاإإإ�ِِِ

Those are the ones upon whom there are blessings from their Lord, and mercy as well; and those are the ones who are on the right path.

QURʼĀN 2:155-157

Grief can sometimes bring a person to lose control over themselves, and because of this, we should be especially careful in such times of ﷺwhat we say and do. Rasūlullāh said:

Allāh does not punish for shedding tears, nor for the grief of the heart but He punishes or ﷺbestows His Mercy because of this: and he pointed to his tongue.

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺRasūlullāh forbade the practise of wailing loudly and excessively, and he advised Ṣabr. Ṣabr means to be steadfast in the face of difficulty and to continue to trust Allāh , and it should be present from the moment we are presented with ﷺdifficulties. The best example we might find of this is in the life of the Prophet himself, when his own son Ibrāhīm was breathing his last:

رضي الله عنهAnas ibn Mālik narrates,

We entered Abū Saifʼs house where Ibrāhīm was breathing his last breaths, ﷺand the eyes of Rasūlullāh began to shed tears.

رضي الله عنهʻʻAbdur Raḥmān bin Auf said,

“O Messenger of Allāh , even you are weeping?” ﷺʻRasūlullāh replied, “O Ibn Auf, this is mercy.” ﷺAfter weeping some more, the Messenger of Allāh said, “Certainly, the eyes weep, and the heart is saddened, but we say nothing except that which pleases our Lord, and — O Ibrāhīm — indeed, we are saddened at your separation.”

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺThe Prophet passed by a woman who was weeping beside a grave. He told her to fear Allāh and be patient. She replied, “Go away, for you have not been afflicted with a calamity like mine,” and she did not recognise him. Then she was informed that he was ﷺthe Prophet . So she went to the ﷺhouse of the Prophet and there she did not find any guard. She said to him, “I did not recognise you.” He said, “Verily, (true) patience is at the first stroke of a calamity.”

BUKHĀRĪ

TAʻZIYAH (CONSOLATION)

Taʻziyah is a practice in Islām of Muslims to visit the family of a deceased person and offer them comfort during their period of grief. As part of the Ummah, and in keeping close family and communal ties, we are expected to offer ourselves ﷺto others during such a period of immense difficulty. Rasūlullāh said, The Muslims are like one body: if the eye is sore, the entire body is troubled (in trying to find a cure); and ūlikewise if the head is wounded, the entire body is troubled (in trying to find comfort).

MUSLIM

Taʻziyah is a virtuous which brings No believer consoles his brother for a great reward. Furthermore, it strengthens ties calamity but that Allāh will dress him with of kinship and provides a sense of community. noble garments on the Day of Resurrection.

ﷺThe Prophet of Allāh mentioned that:

IBN MĀJAH

Ta’ziyah is a time for us to offer support to the family. This means that we should be considerate to the family and try to ease the pain and difficulty. We should ensure that we are not doing the opposite, where we are burdening the family further and wasting time engaging in unfruitful . Joking, laughing, speaking of worldly affairs, overstaying our welcome and not allowing the family rest are all unfortunately common in the houses of people who have passed, yet that should not be the case.

SOME TIPS ON HOW TO CONSOLE Encourage Ṣabr and patience, and gently remind the person that they will be rewarded for it.

Offer Duʻāʼ (supplication): for the deceased that they are forgiven and for the family that Allāh  eases their affliction and grants them Ṣabr.

Mention the good qualities and characteristics of the deceased. Along with this, if the person passed away in a good situation or time (e.g. in Ramaḍān, after performing ʻUmrah, etc), emphasise that to the family as words of comfort.

Remind them that everything is in Allāh ʼs hand, and we all belong to Allāh . Everyone has an appointed time, and we are all due to return to Allāh  one day.

Tell the family about any optional good deeds you plan on performing on behalf of the deceased (e.g. recitation of Qurʼān, Tasbīḥ, etc). It will warm their heart to hear of others sharing in their grief and empathising with them.

Make or organise the provision of food for the family if you can.

When Jaʻfar رضي الله عنه was martyred in battle, Allāhʼs Messenger ﷺ personally

delivered the news to his family, consoled them and then said, ʻPrepare food for the family of Jafar, for they have been afflicted with something that has engaged them.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

Taʻziyah can be made within three days after the death has Exceptions to this are for the wife of a occurred. As some family or friends may live afar, or might only deceased husband, or a pregnant woman. have the opportunity to visit later, there is an exception made for such people and they should make an effort to visit if they could Their ʻIddah (mourning period) will be four not do so earlier. However, the objective of the Sharīʻah is to allow months and ten days, or until delivery of the people to move on with their daily lives as soon as possible. For child or miscarriage respectively. this reason, Taʻziyah should not be extended beyond three days.

Make a practice of visiting the graveyard regularly and reflecting on life.

VISITING THE GRAVEYARD Visit the graves, for that makes you mindful of death.

MUSLIM

The grave is the first station after our death, and there is benefit for us as well as the deceased in our visiting of the graveyard. The benefit for us is that the graveyard serves as a reminder for every person that their death is ever approaching, and they need to make preparation for it. It sobers us from the intoxicant of daily life and makes us reflect. It is also beneficial to the dwellers of the graves through the reward we send forward to them. As many Companions and ﷺﷺthe Prophet did, we should frequently visit the graveyard. When Rasūlullāh would enter the graveyard, he would recite the Duʻāʼ:َ ََُُّْْْ��

نَيْمَلُسَّمَٰلاونَيْٰتَمِوَُمٰلا نِمِ رَاتُدِّلا لُٰهُامْكْيْلَعَ مُالَسَّلاِِِ� ،�وَُ�ْحَالمْكيَهِللا ءٍاشِ�ا اتُاوإإِ� ،ةُْيْقَاٰعٰلا مْكُلو اْيْلهِللا لُٰتَٰسَّبِِ

Peace be upon you, O Believers and Muslims of these abodes. Verily, if Allāh wills, we are to join you. We pray to Allāh for safety for us and for you.

MUSLIM

Visiting the graveyard should make us introspect, and bring about a state of seriousness, however temporary. The graveyard should be treated with utmost respect; by making sure we walk on footpaths rather than over graves; being mindful of other people; and observing a solemn silence or praying rather than talking. WHEN IN THE GRAVEYARD, WE MAY DO THE FOLLOWING:

Make Duʻāʼ of Recite the Duʻāʼ forgiveness for upon enteringthe deceased ReciteRecite any other Sūrah Ikhlāṣ Sūrahs (e.g. Sūrah three times and Takāthur, or the Sūrah Yāsīnlast few Sūrahs)

Reflect and contemplate on death We should make the intention that Allāh sends the reward forward to all the deceased.

ĪṢĀL ATH-THAWĀB Īṣāl ath-Thawāb refers to performing optional good deeds and sending them forward to those who have passed away to be recorded amongst their good deeds. It is through the mercy of Allāh , and a sign of His grandeur, that the deeds we pass on are not only recorded for those who we send them to, but also in our records without any decrease. Hence, we should utilise Allāh ʼs gift, and pray for every Muslim who has passed. From recitation of the Qurʼān, to performing Ḥajj on behalf of the deceased, to giving charity in their name; we can pass on good deeds in many ways. A person who has passed can no longer perform good deeds themselves, but can receive a constant stream of good deeds through means such as pious children, ongoing charity, and anything they did which is still producing good. As life flickers by as it does, we are all bound to inevitably lose people we love, and we may have lost many already. For us as Muslims, death is a permanent fixture of life which rather than fear, we find solace in. It reminds us of our Creator, and that we are indeed to return to Him. We are reminded to make preparation for it beforehand and help those who have passed away by sending reward to them, which hopefully those after us will do for us. Rather than the end of existence, Islām informs us that death is a gateway to eternal life from a temporary one, where we will be rewarded for the toils and struggles we endured. For this reason, it is imperative that we make the absolute most of our time in this world, so that we are successful in the place that matters most: the hereafter.

Ḥalāl Earnings

the will cover importance of a As Muslims, we have an obligation to earn wealth. Managing money refers to spending what one IsrāfTabdhīrhas responsibly without wasting (called or ), and effectively managing oneʼs finances to look after oneself.

Allāh says in the Qurʼān, And do not spend wastefully. Surely the wasteful are brothers to the devils.

QURʼĀN 17:26-27

As one gets older, it is very important to have an overview of oneʼs finances, knowing what is coming in, and where money is being spent. This may be done by writing down or using a spreadsheet to budget income and outgoing expenses.

Importantly, we should budget to limit wastefulness and extravagance, and so that we can allocate spending for good, whether that be on our family, or in charitable causes.

Rizq Our (sustenance) ultimately is determined by Allāh . It is He who decides who is to receive what, and we will  only get at any given moment what Allāh has already allotted for us. As Muslims, this knowledge should give us reassurance that Allāh has planned for us and should increase us in our trust in Allāh . At the same time, having faith  that our Rizq is fixed will control the greed inherent in us, as we will never receive what Allāh has not allocated for us. For this reason, if ever an opportunity to increase wealth misses us, we should content ourselves with the reality that Allāh had something better planned, and that He is the best of planners.

Zakāh & Ṣadaqah

In this you the will cover rulings of Zakāh, Ṣadaqah is the voluntary act of kindness or goodness by someone without expectation of the importance of anything in return. This may mean the giving of not only money, but also food and clothing, giving Zakāh and and extends as far as a kind word, a smile or even removing obstructions on a path. Ṣadaqah what is Ṣadaqah. is incredibly broad in what it can be, and so many good actions we do for others, if done with the intention of reward, will become Ṣadaqah. Moreover, Ṣadaqah is not only for those ﷺoutside our families, but it includes our own immediate families, such that the Prophet is reported to have said, When a Muslim spends something on his family intending to receive Allāhʼs reward, it is regarded as Ṣadaqah for him.

ZAKĀH & Ṣ We can give charity openly and discreetly. On one hand, we do it openly to encourage others, who by watching us may feel inclined to do the same. Again, this can be financially, but can also be through our time and effort. However, it is important to maintain pure intentions in this case, as doing so with the aim to impress others will bring us no benefit from such charity. On the other hand, the Ṣadaqah we give secretly should be greater in amount. This will work to safeguard our intentions.

Finally, being able to give Ṣadaqah is a blessing, and we should regard it as such. If we are in a position to give, we should consider ourselves fortunate, firstly for the wealth that Allāh has given us, and secondly for the opportunity to give.

One way that Allāh tests those whom he blesses with wealth is by seeing whether they utilise that wealth in His way. On the Day of Qiyāmah, one of the laments of people will be, My Lord, if only You would delay me for a brief term so I would give charity and be of the righteous.

QURʼĀN 63:10

We should make the most of our opportunity to give charity now, so we do not regret later.

ZAKĀH Zakāh is the obligatory charity upon every Muslim who meets certain thresholds (Niṣāb) to be given to specified recipients. Zakāh is the 'cleansing' of our wealth, where Allāh has specified an amount for us to give so that we receive Barakah (divine blessings) in our remaining wealth and enjoy it fully. Zakāh provides benefit not only to the giver and the receiver, but it functions to aid the entirety of society, where the rich and wealthy members of the community assume their roles and responsibilities to help others. Furthermore, Zakāh fosters a culture of giving and assistance for all, restricting the diseases of materialism and the hyperfocus on this life.

WHAT IS NIṢĀB?

Niṣāb is a threshold of wealth one must have for Zakāh to become compulsory. It is calculated by adding up the Zakātable assets you have in hand and deducting the debts you owe.

Niṣāb is equivalent to the value of:

87.48612.36 OR gramsgrams OF SILVEROF GOLD The Niṣāb will be the one with the lower of the two prices (gold or silver).

ZAKĀH & Ṣ THE FOLLOWING ARE THE CONDITIONS THAT MAKE ZAKĀH OBLIGATORY UPON A PERSON CONDITION The person must be a Muslim.

CONDITION The person must be Bāligh (mature) & sane.

CONDITION The person must have complete ownership of Zakātable assets of an amount equivalent to Niṣāb (These assets are to be of a productive nature and in excess of personal needs).

CONDITION The person must begin to own the Niṣāb 4 amount, and one full lunar year later be in possession of an amount equal to or above the Niṣāb. If the above conditions are met and a person has the Niṣāb The Zakāh anniversary will not change if one's amount or more on the annual Zakāh anniversary, after wealth decreases below the Nisāb between deducting liabilities, they will give an amount equivalent gaining the Niṣāb amount and the Zakāh to 2.5% (one-fortieth) of their total Zakātable assets to a anniversary. The Zakāh anniversary will only valid recipient of Zakāh or via a reputable Muslim charity. be reset if one's wealth decreases to zero. The ruling will change slightly for livestock and agricultural products.

Economics

will cover an introduction to The branch of economics relates to the production, consumption, and transfer of wealth. economics in In the real world, we are surrounded by the economic realities of our lives, especially in Islām, Islamic a globally connected world, where there is a continuous motion of wealth, goods and principles of currency. Furthermore, the study of economics has brought forth different, often competing economics, and theories and ideologies on how wealth should be produced, managed and distributed, important terms which all impact our lives today. related to Islamic Islām has its own perspective on the field of economics, economics. complete with overarching principles which inform a variety of laws. These laws affect production, consumption and transfer of wealth, as well as the Economics:interactions between them. Similarly, Islām seeks to maximise the welfare of all involved and reduce exploitation, whilst maintaining justice and allowing the branch of entrepreneurship to flourish. knowledge related to production, Before delving into the principles consumption and of Islamic economics, it is transfer of wealth important that we understand the nature of wealth. This contrast shows the attitude we should have to this world, that though we partake in in making our stay comfortable, our ultimate goal should not be this world, but rather the hereafter, and this worldly life should not distract us from that goal.

ISLAMIC PRINCIPLES TRUE OWNERSHIP IS FOR ALLĀH  All wealth is owned by Allāh  ultimately, and He gives it to whom He wills.

MAINTAINING THE OF SHARĪʻAH The core of Sharīʻah are incorporated within Islamic principles on economics. Thus production, consumption and transfer of wealth are guided by the of Sharīʻah first. Preference in production is given to necessities, followed by requirements, then comforts and luxuries. If any of the key which the Sharīʻah seeks to protect and maintain are compromised, such economic will be contrary to Sharīʻah.

PROFIT AND RISK-SHARING Profits and the risk of loss should be shared between the contributor of capital and the entrepreneur.

WIDE CIRCULATION OF WEALTH Wealth is for all of society, even those not directly involved in its production.

Islām does not believe in communism, but rather that wealth should be given voluntarily by the rich to the poor, as gratitude to Allāh and in hope of reward from Him. Ṣadaqah and Zakāh are examples of charity, and additionally, one may fund a Waqf fund for long-term giving.

ِ�WHAT IS A WAQF FUND? A waqf is a perpetual charitable endowment, usually in the form of an So that wealth may not merely circulate asset, which is 'donated to Allāh ' among your rich. for its proceeds or benefit to be for society. Waqf endowments have been

QURʼĀN 59:7

used widely throughout Islamic history This verse highlights how wealth should flow and not stagnate to develop and support communities. within the rich. Rather, wealth should be used for business, to An example of Waqf is a university or a employ or aid others, or be spent in charity. Wealth should flow hospital.throughout society to benefit all, not the few.

PROHIBITION OF EXPLOITATION Islām seeks to remove exploitation, and for this reason, Ribā (usury) is forbidden.

Allāh says, And Allāh has permitted trade and forbidden Ribā.

QURʼĀN 2:275

Any economic based on, or party to the practice of usury is against Islamic principles. Islām believes in organic growth where risk is shared between the contributor of capital and the one exercising entrepreneurship.

MONEY IS NOT A COMMODITY The nature of Money in Islām is that it is not a commodity, but rather a medium of exchange and provides value to products and services. Money therefore is a means rather than an end and should be invested (for material or spiritual gain) rather than left to depreciate through inflation, or worse, increase through interest.

INVESTMENT Investing oneʼs wealth is recommended in Islām, and if one cannot do so themselves, they may engage in partnerships to utilise it where they share risk. Investment is also beneficial in that it provides opportunities to others through employment and trade, and stimulates the economy helping all.

DEBT Islām views debt as something to be taken in times of need, but only when one is sure of their capacity to fulfil their debt without interest. The lender should also be accommodating to the debtor, and should take nothing more than what they are owed.

FREE MARKETS The market and its prices are regulated by Allāh , and so there will be no intervention on market prices to artificially inflate or decrease prices. Alongside this however, it is prohibited to hoard products, especially essential products, to raise prices and increase profit.

SANCTITY OF CONTRACTS The Qurʼān stresses the importance of documenting debts, dealings and financial matters. Muslims are also exhorted to honour their verbal and written contracts, and Allāh  describes Muslims as those who hold true to their word.

RIGHTFUL OWNERSHIP Islām emphasises that the rights of others should not be infringed, and that a personʼs wealth is theirs and cannot be taken from them without their consent.

Exploitation of the weak to manipulate them into relinquishing ownership is forbidden, and Islām advocates protection for those who may be exploited.

PROHIBITION OF INVESTMENT IN ḤARĀM Islām prohibits certain , such as the consumption of pork or alcohol, gambling, and adultery. No investment may be made into any Ḥarām , and any source of income through sales revenue, production, manufacture, distribution, marketing or anything related is forbidden.

PROHIBITION OF SPECULATION (MAYSIR)

Islām forbids any form of speculation or gambling. This is called Maysir. For this reason, any financial , sale, or contract where the ownership of goods is dependent on an uncertain event in the future will be void.

PROHIBITION OF UNCERTAINTY (GHARAR)

Islām forbids any contract or financial with excessive risk or uncertainty. The prohibition of gharar leads to greater openness in dealings, and protects the parties of the sale from deceit, fraudulent , and conflict.

GHARAR USUALLY EXISTS IN ONE OR MORE OF THE FOLLOWING SCENARIOS:

010203 THERE IS NO THERE IS THE ITEM OF GUARANTEE OF AMBIGUITY IN THE SALE OR SERVICE OWNERSHIPITEM OF SALE, THE CANNOT BE SERVICE BEING SUPPLIED OR GIVEN IN GAMBLING, ONE PROVIDED, OR THE PAYS FOR A CHANCE TIME MENTIONED SELLING AN ITEM ONE TO WIN SOMETHING, DOES NOT YET POSSESS BUT THERE IS NO RENTING OR LEASING GUARANTEE OF OWNING WITHOUT AN END DATE SOMETHING FROM THE FOR THE LEASE TRANSACTION Create an infographic Analyse Gharar, Maysir 'Moderation in expenditure is half of poster with 10 key and Ribā and discuss in livelihoodʼ

Cryptocurrency: a decentralised digital currency secured by cryptography which may be used for online transactions Stock market: a place where traders and investors can buy and sell shares of publicly traded companies ROI: return on investment; calculated by dividing the profit earned on an investment by the cost of that investment and shown as a percentage Bond: represents a loan to a company or government, and pays out interest Dividend: periodic distribution of profits to shareholders

RESPONSIBLE INVESTING Investing should be done responsibly. Wealth is a gift from Allāh which we should take good care of, and investing in a way that risks our livelihood or future is harmful to ourselves and families. When asked on how much one may bequeath for charity after ﷺdeath, Rasūlullāh said, (At most) a third, and a third is too great.

TIRMIDHĪ

If in the matter of the hereafter we have been told to give only a third, so that the dependents and family members have a livelihood after death, then naturally during life we should take care of our wealth and ensure we have enough to support our dependents.

One should only invest what they can afford to, and when investing, they should conduct thorough prior to ensure they are doing so correctly and not wasting their wealth. Using the internet for information, or speaking to experts are different ways one may educate themselves on how and where to invest.

Another aspect of responsible investing is checking for Sharīʻah compliance.

Sharīʻah requires that investments be ethical, free from exploitation, and free from dealing in anything Ḥarām. When looking into an investment opportunity, one may need to perform thorough checks on the of a company to verify their degree of Sharīʻah compliance. Whilst there are websites and applications, free and paid, which offer services in checking for Sharīʻah compliance, in certain cases, one may need to refer the case to an expert scholar in the field.

WHAT IS ISLAMIC FINANCE?

Islamic finance is a growing sector of the global financial market, and it refers to people and businesses raising and investing capital according to Sharʻī principles. It encompasses banking, leasing, investment funds, Sharīʻah compliant insurance, equity markets, micro finance and Sukūk.

MUSHĀRAKAH Different parties contribute capital for a venture, and divide profits according to a pre-determined ratio. Losses will be shared according to proportion of capital invested. Each party has control over how the investment is managed, and each party is liable for the actions of others.

MUḌĀRABAH One party contributes capital while the other offers expertise or labour. Profits will be divided according to a pre-determined ratio, whilst losses will be taken by the one investing capital.

ISLAMIC MURĀBAḤAH An asset is purchased on behalf of a client and resold to the client at a pre- determined price, usually with profit.

FINANCE Ownership of the asset will remain with the financier until full payment is completed.

INSTRUMENTS ISTIṢNĀʻ A long-term financing contract wherein a party agrees to construct or manufacture and deliver an asset for a customer at an agreed price. The exact specifications for the asset or the project will be agreed in the contract, and payment may be in َinstalments or upon delivery.

SALAM (لَشِ)مِ A forward financing contract where the financier will pay in advance for the delivery of a specific, measurable asset at a pre-determined date.

TAKĀFUL Islamic insurance where members contribute money to be pooled together and paid out as reimbursement in case of loss for any member. The pool of money may also be invested to increase its effectiveness as an insurance tool.

BAYʻ MUʻAJJAL A credit sale wherein delivery is taken immediately, but payment is deferred to an agreed period.

IJĀRAH (LEASING CONTRACT) A contract in which the owner of an asset transfers its right of use to another for an agreed price and time period. An asset is purchased on behalf of a client who uses the asset for a fixed- rental payment. The financier will retain ownership of the asset, though it may gradually transfer to the client through periodic payments. The rental payment may decrease in proportion to percentage of ownership.

ISLAMIC MORTGAGES An alternative to traditional interest- bearing mortgages: Islamic mortgages HOW AND WHERE TO INVEST? usually involve the banking institution buying out the property itself and then and advice is needed before any type of investment, but generally, one should look to place transferring the property to the potential the majority of their assets in low-risk investments, buyer through a profit-bearing agreement with a smaller portion of their wealth in high-risk that utilises Ijārah, Mushārakah, or investments. The high-risk investments offer a Murābaḥah. greater reward but also are more likely to fail, so one should only spare a percentage of their wealth for such investments. On the other hand, low-risk which offer near-guaranteed profits, so one should plan with such knowledge in mind.

COMMON INVESTMENTS COMMODITIES Raw materials, metals, or agricultural products to be invested in and sold. Certain commodities (such as gold) may be kept as they retain and increase in value.

Sharīʻah Compliance: Ḥalāl SHARES Shares are units of ownership in a company which may be bought and sold on the stock market. Shares may be a short-term investment where the investor buys a share at a lower price to sell at a higher price; or it may be a long-term investment to be sold at a much later date.

Sharīʻah Compliance: The company being invested in must be checked for Sharīʻah compliance.

CRYPTOCURRENCY A cryptocurrency is a decentralised digital currency secured by cryptography which may be used for online transactions. Due to fluctuations in prices of cryptocurrencies, they may be bought and sold for investment purposes.

Sharīʻah Compliance: The cryptocurrency being invested in must be checked for Sharīʻah compliance.

FOREX A global market for trading currencies.

Sharīʻah Compliance: Generally impermissible BONDS Bonds are debt instruments (loan repayment promises) issued to raise capital, upon which interest is paid. The holder of a bond will receive interest until the end of the bond term.

Sharīʻah Compliance: Generally impermissible ANY INTEREST RECEIVED BY A PERSON MUST BE GIVEN TO A CHARITY WITHOUT INTENTION OF REWARD.

SUKŪK Sukūk are Islamic financial certificates similar to bonds, however they are based on ownership of assets from which profit is shared rather than interest.

Sharīʻah Compliance: Ḥalāl PROPERTY Land or buildings which may be used for rent and leasing, manufacturing, or similar investment purposes.

Sharīʻah Compliance: Ḥalāl MUTUAL FUNDS Mutual funds pool money from multiple investors to purchase a diversified portfolio of assets. This diverse portfolio reduces risk and ensures slow yet steady growth for the investors.

Sharīʻah Compliance: The assets being invested in must be checked for Sharīʻah compliance.

ETFs ETFs (Exchange-Traded Funds) are very similar to mutual funds as they track multiple assets rather than one.

Sharīʻah Compliance: The assets being tracked by the ETF must be checked for Sharīʻah compliance.

SAVINGS ACCOUNT (401K, LIFETIME ISA) A savings account is (usually) a bank account specifically for saving money, often with tax advantages, but also restrictions on withdrawals for a period.

Sharīʻah Compliance: Any savings account which accrues interest is impermissible. Ḥalāl alternatives may be available.

PENSION PLANS Pension plans are provided by government and employers for employees to contribute a portion of their salary for future retirement income. Many pension plans will invest the money allocated into funds for growth over time.

Sharīʻah Compliance: The investments made by any pension fund must be Sharīʻah compliant.

Pension payments must also be included in Zakāh calculations.

GAMBLING Islām forbids gambling in every form. Wasting wealth for chance is Ḥarām because it devalues what Allāh has given a person, often leads to financial ruin, and it undermines hard work and effort. Gambling may be through betting, games, or lotteries, and it is a highly addictive and destructive behaviour which must be avoided at any cost. Any money gained through any form of gambling is impermissible to use, and anything bought through such wealth is also impermissible to use or consume. THE GREATEST INVESTMENT Who is the one who would give Allāh a good loan so that Allāh multiplies it for him many times? Allāh withholds and extends, and to Him you are to be returned.

QURʼĀN 2:245

dividendsThe greatest investment is the one which continues to give the longest, and the one which multiplies upon itself the most. If this is the aim of every investment, then there is no investment like the one for  the hereafter. Allāh has promised for every good deed that it will be multiplied ten-fold, and for wealth given in Allāh ʼs sake, Allāh has promised increase in this world, and reward in the hereafter. For as much as we invest in this life and prepare for a future which may or may not come, we should never forget that the real life is the one to come, and it requires preparation as it will undoubtedly arrive.

In the Qurʼān, Allāh mentions the cry and regret of the one in the hereafter, where He says, And spend out of what We have given to you before death overtakes one of you and he says, “My Lord, would you not give me respite for a short while, so that I should pay Ṣadaqah and become one of the righteous?”

QURʼĀN 63:10

This Āyah highlights the importance of investing for the Ākhirah. Of all the good deeds one will feel regretful over not performing whilst alive, not having spent wealth for Allāh ʼs sake will cause the greatest regret. We should ensure we do not become like the one mentioned in the verse, and secure our future through timely investments which we will see the fruits of one day, after we pass from this world.

you will cover the status of inheritance comes into effect. QURʼĀN 4:13

Bequest: the act of giving or leaving Inheritance something by Will, or and the laws the thing being leftpertaining to it are clearly defined so none may be cheated of their rights. For this reason, though the matter of inheritance is slightly complex, we should familiarise ourselves with the basic knowledge of how it works.

WHAT IS PAID FOR FIRST? The first cost that is incurred for a deceased person is that of their funeral. A person will require a shroud, digging of their grave and other such necessities, and so the funeral costs take precedence in oneʼs inheritance. If there remains wealth following the fulfilment of the funeral costs, the next step is to fulfil the debts of the deceased, if any. Only after the above two are fulfilled, Willthe of the deceased shall take effect, and his bequests, if Islāmically sound, will be honoured. The remainder of the wealth will be distributed between the inheritors in accordance to the shares mentioned in the Qurʼān.

It is important to Another matter related to inheritance is that of the Will. BUKHĀRĪ

their Will legally binding. Similarly, This shows the importance of a Will, and we should, if we have wealth, try and keep a Will. This one should also will allow us to set aside some of our wealth for that which may benefit us after death, and get Islamic advice also, safeguard our wealth with a binding document. from a scholar on a Will for Sharīʻah A will allows us to leave instructions behind about ourselves, our assets and our families and compliance. also to set aside some of our wealth for that which may benefit us after death. Furthermore, without a will, one’s wealth may be distributed contrary to the laws of Sharī’ah, and as the laws on inheritance are divine, we must abide by them. A person may bequeath wealth in their Will to anyone or any cause besides those who are legally bound to receive inheritance. Furthermore, a person cannot deny the right of an inheritor through their will by specifying that such a person should not receive anything, and any such stipulation will be disregarded. The bequest can only take effect in one-third of a persons inheritance, so any stipulations or bequests may only be taken from a third of the total amount remaining after the burial costs and debts. When writing a will, it is important to take into account the laws of the country in which one resides. The will may not be legally valid if certain conditions are not met, and so care must be taken in this regard. Furthermore, it is important to note all of oneʼs assets and debts in oneʼs will (including passwords!), so that the family knows what the deceased owned, what they owed and to who, and how to access the documents and assets.

One should look to get their will checked by someone trained in Islamic law and the law of the country. A COMMON MISCONCEPTION: WHY DO MEN RECEIVE A DOUBLE SHARE?

Allāh has determined His Sharīʻah with justice, and this is the overarching theme in all laws given by Him. It is our role to submit to Allāh ʼs decree, regardless of whether we understand the wisdom behind it or not. Nevertheless, there are reasons, when viewed with understanding of the system Allāh has placed, for a male to receive a double share. As you will read, a male does not always receive a double share, but only does so in certain circumstances where it has been determined to be the just and fair course due to other laws and responsibilities. For example, a son will receive double of a daughterʼs share as the daughter is or potentially may be a dependent of the son (her brother), requiring the son to provide for his sister or sisters. The sisters however receive their share with no responsibility to spend on any other person. Likewise, a husband will receive a greater amount of his wifeʼs inheritance upon her death than she would upon his death due to the responsibility of the children, where in the case of the wifeʼs death, the children will be dependents of their father, but in the case of the fatherʼs death, the responsibility will fall upon the childrenʼs fatherʼs side (their paternal uncles and grandparents) rather than the mother, who will not be financially responsible.

The division will be made by writing down the names and relation of the deceased in a HOW IS IT DIVIDED? line, with their share underneath. Following that, the lowest common denominator must be found, and the shares divided accordingly. An example is given below:

Addiction to a vice could turn a mistake into a continuous sin. Any person can fall into sin, for which they are expected to seek sincere forgiveness with the intent to not commit such a sin again. If one has fallen into addiction, that does not mean there is no hope! The first HOW TO GET OFF THE HOOK and most important step to recovery is recognising that one has a problem. This is the hardest step, and the steps to recovery after that are easier. One may consider the following to complete a full recovery:

IDENTIFY YOUR Identifying your triggers is very important, TRIGGERSas you can then plan alternative behaviours when those triggers arise.

PLAN Try not to be hard on yourself, and refrain from simply relying on ALTERNATIVE'willpower' to defeat addictive behaviour. Rather, use the power of dopamine by replacing the negative behaviour with something positive.BEHAVIOURS It is very important to speak to someone that you trust to recover SPEAK TO from addiction. In some cases, this may simply create accountability, but in other cases, you may need therapy which will greatly accelerate your SOMEONE recovery.

Example: If someone is addicted to pornography, identifying their triggers will mean identifying when and where they are likely to feel they want to watch pornography. This may be their bed at night, or when they feel stressed from school or work. After identifying their triggers, they can plan to counteract it, for example by ensuring they do not have their phone with them at night and having alternative stress-release options such as sport. The road to recovery is not easy, and as Muslims, we believe that for our every effort to do good and become better, we will undoubtedly be rewarded. A person may sincerely repent, and fall into the same sin, and repent, and sin, and do so endlessly, but will be forgiven for as many times they sincerely repent. Whilst an addiction may make a person feel helpless, that they are undeserving of Allāh ʼs mercy, and that their repentance is not accepted, we must always remember that such thoughts are the whispers of Shayṭān, and Allāh ʼs words tell us the complete and absolute opposite. Our Lord, the All-Forgiving, All-Merciful says:

TIRMIDHĪ

Drugs & Intoxicants

you will cover the status of ﷺWhen the Messenger of Allāh was taken from Makkah to Bayt al-Maqdis for the Night Journey intoxicants in and Ascension (al-Isrāʼ wa al-Miʻrāj), he was presented with a choice of drink. The Angel Jibrīl Islām, how they ﷺﷺoffered Rasūlullāh two vessels, one containing milk and the other wine. The Prophet were forbidden, looked at both and chose the vessel full of milk. Upon seeing this, Jibrīl said, and the various All praise is due to Allāh who has guided you to the Fiṭrah, harms of had you chosen wine your nation would have gone astray. intoxicants.

BUKHĀRĪ

This incident serves to highlight several important points, most notably that sound Fiṭrahhuman nature () is against intoxicants and their like. It also points to the destructive nature of those things which bring about a drunken state, so much so Fiṭrah: sound human that it could be the singular reason for the destruction and fall of an entire nation. nature: natural and ﷺThe Messenger of Allāh displayed in that moment what we as Muslims should seek innate disposition to emulate: that we strive to attain a sound natural state that is disgusted at the idea which Allāh has cognitiveof losing and physical function through the non-medicinal consumption of placed within every anything which may intoxicate. human Cognitive: mental, rational, intellectual Khamr: intoxicantWHAT IS FORBIDDEN?

Opportunity cost:

ﷺThe Messenger of Allāh said, the loss of other alternatives when Every intoxicant is Khamr and one alternative is every intoxicant is forbidden. chosen

MUSLIM

Khamr is defined as something which clouds or covers the mind. Therefore, the prohibition of those things which intoxicate is not limited to the various forms of drink or alcohol, but extends to all substances which may impair the cognitive or physical state of a person. For this reason, the consumption, and indeed, ﷺproducing, shipping, selling and buying of any drug, substance or alcohol is forbidden. The Messenger of Allāh was distinctly clear on the matter, and in a Ḥadīth which demonstrates the severity of the sin of intoxicants, he says, Allāh has cursed Khamr: its consumer, its server, its seller, its buyer, its presser (producer), the one for whom it is pressed, the courier, and the one to whom it is delivered.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

This shows how Islām views intoxicants, and we should make every effort to stay away from all kinds of drugs, regardless of how harmless their consumption may seem.

Reframing the matter of the prohibition of intoxicants in Islām in a better manner would be to say that Islām, rather than banning intoxicants, seeks more to promote healthy and respected individuals who are part of a harmonious greater society free from the disease of substance abuse. The objective of Sharīʻah is not to limit human freedom, but rather to provide the best circumstances in which humanity may live and recognise their Lord. A society addicted to intoxicants is far less likely to recognise and worship their Creator than one which is sober, dignified, and morally upright.

HOW INTOXICANTS WERE BANNED In the early days of Islām, the consumption of wine was still allowed as it had been the custom and habit of the people of Makkah. Allāh then revealed the first Āyah regarding alcohol: They ask you about wine and gambling. Say, "In both there is great evil, and some benefits for people.”

QURʼĀN 2:219

This provided some with enough motivation to quit, but as it was not clearly and fully prohibited, others would still drink occasionally or during social gatherings. This further changed with an incident of a Ṣaḥābī drunkenly leading Ṣalāh where he, due to his intoxicated state, made major errors in the recitation of the Qurʼān. Allāh  then revealed the Āyah:

O you who believe, do not go near Ṣalāh when you are intoxicated until you know what you say.

QURʼĀN 4:43

This Āyah was then later followed by the complete prohibition of intoxicants in the verse:

O you who believe; indeed wine, gambling, altar- stones and divining arrows are filth from the work of Shayṭān. Therefore, refrain from it…

QURʼĀN 5:90

With this Āyah, the Companions, regardless of their previous drinking habits, completely and fully gave up alcohol for the sake of Allāh .

PHYSICAL HARMCOGNITIVE IMPAIRMENT The physical harms of intoxicants are widely As in the name, intoxicants known, from addiction to the effects it can induce a state within a person have on the body. Even seemingly harmless where their cognitive function substances such as nitrous oxide (laughing gas) is severely reduced, and in can have life-changing or fatal consequences. some cases the damage may be This is without taking long term effects into permanent. The intellect of a account, which may be even worse.person is a gift from Allāh , and maintaining it is a responsibility upon every person.

THE THE LOSS OF PERSONAL DIGNITY A person under influence is a shadow of themselves, and through the actions HARMS OF they commit or the impression they exhibit of themselves, their dignity suffers. Islām seeks to protect the INTOXICANTSinherent nobility that Allāh  has

عليه السلامplaced within every child of Ādam ,

and the prohibition of intoxicants is aimed at achieving that.

FINANCIAL HARM Substance abuse is expensive, and the time spent using intoxicants is also time spent away from seeking SOCIETAL HARM a livelihood or learning new skills.

Intoxicants have immense societal impact, Therefore, the financial harm is whether it be disadvantaged children twofold: for the expenditure itself, because one of their parents are substance and the opportunity cost. abusers, to youth wasting their potential in intoxicants when they might contribute to society, or even the financial burden placed

رضي الله عنهʻUthmān , the third Khalīfah of Islām, once said,

upon wider society to remedy issues caused Avoid alcohol, for it is the by those under influence. The harms are mother of all wickedness. incomprehensibly endless.

NASĀʼĪ

Indeed, alcohol and intoxicants may bring a person to commit what in normal circumstances would be considered grossly immoral. An intoxicated or drugged person may be persuaded, often with little effort, to commit one or many immoral acts. It is often in a drunken state that many commit acts of unspeakable violence, or do that which has untold consequences. As a result, those consequences often produce a significant amount of further damage and suffering, which may have altogether been avoided had such substances not been consumed.

PREVENTS YOU FROM REMEMBERING ALLĀH  This truly is the greatest of the harms. Allāh  says, Shayṭānʼs plan is to ūwith intoxicants and gambling prevent you from remembering Allāh and praying.

QURʼĀN 5:91

Intoxicants take a person far from remembering Allāh , through the sin itself and the habit of coming back to it, which prevents a person seeking forgiveness. Likewise, Ṣalāh will easily be missed when under influence.

CREATING ENMITY AMONGST PEOPLE Allāh  says, Shayṭānʼs plan is to stir up hostility and hatred between you with intoxicants and gambling.

QURʼĀN 5:91

Thus, intoxicants create enmity and hatred between people, fracturing the bonds which exist to promote harmonious interaction between people.

LOSS OF POTENTIAL Allāh  has placed potential within every human being, and given them ability that they may utilise to achieve in this world and the hereafter. Intoxicants, and addiction to them, destroys the potential good within a person, as their only fixation is their next session of substance abuse.

DEATH How awful would it be that death come to a person whilst they are under influence? This is very possible however, as the abuse of substances increases the likelihood of such an occurrence. A person will be resurrected as they died, and such a death would indeed be amongst the most misfortunate.

HOW MUCH TIME SHOULD WE SPEND?

ﷺRasūlullāh said, A strong believer is better and dearer to Allāh than a weak one, and there is good in both of them.

MUSLIM

The best which nourish the mind and body of a person are those which are beneficial through making a person ﷺhealthier, stronger, and smarter. For this, the Ḥadīth of the Prophet applies to us in that we spend our free time doing things which give us such benefit. However, Allāh has also allowed us to relax, and we may use games to do so.

Gaming is acceptable and allowed so long as religious duties are not affected, or our physical and mental health are not neglected. If they are, then the time spent gaming must be reduced. IS A PASTIME, NOT A LIFESTYLE

As Muslims, we believe that Allāh has placed us in this world for a purpose, which is to worship him. Whilst we are allowed to relax and play, this should not become the sole  of our lives. Allāh refers to people who consider this life to be one only for pleasure in the Qurʼān and says, Those who took their religion for distraction, a mere game, and were deluded by worldly life. Today We shall ignore them, just as they have ignored their meeting with this Day.

QURʼĀN 7:51

We should not let gaming come in the way of our lives, and it should not become a fixation. As soon as we feel rejuvenated and rested, we should return to our tasks and responsibilities. We may see gamers online with luxurious lifestyles and huge followings, but rather than see them as inspiration, we should reflect on how those lifestyles are contrary to what Allāh wants from us. We should not allow gaming to affect our studies, lives, and achievements.

Games are a tool to unwind, not something to build our lives around. Our character and dignity suffer if we allow the fate of our life to be dictated by what should only be small pleasures to be enjoyed for a short time.

ﷺRasūlullāh said, The world is a prison for the believer.

MUSLIM

This is because a believer understands the temporary nature of the world, and limits their enjoyment whilst focusing on the hereafter.

EXPLICIT CONTENT One of the detestable aspects of the internet is that it has allowed easy access to pornography. representation of intimate parts of the body or intimate acts in images, video and writing for the gratification of a consumer. The amount of explicit content, pictures, and videos has increased, and viewing it, speaking about oneʼs viewing habits, and referencing it has become normal. The abundance and normalisation of explicit content should make us more vigilant of our internet browsing habits. Content blockers, curating our feed for better control of what we see, and disabling advertisements are ways we can retain some control over what we see. Similarly, we must avoid watching films and TV series as not only is the content impermissible for other reasons, but there has been an increase in explicit material, nudity, and indecency on those media formats as well.

AL-ADAB AL-MUFRAD

HARMS OF WATCHING PORNOGRAPHY DECREASED SPIRITUALITY Committing sins weakens the connection with Allāh , and makes it more difficult to reattach oneself to Him. The habit of sin can be difficult to break, and it can also affect the heart to push it away from good, and remain engrossed in evil. Remember however, no matter how bad the sin, Allāh is always ready to forgive.

Addiction to anything is often harmful, and addiction to something as physiologically, psychologically and spiritually damaging as pornography can have extreme consequences.

DESENSITISES THE VIEWER The consumer of pornography constantly needs something greater and more stimulating to receive a similar sensation. The consumer will eventually seek out more extreme forms of pornography for the same thrill, which may lead them to extremely filthy practices, or even illegal content.

DECREASED FOCUS AND ATTENTION Due to the overload and dependency on pleasure chemicals, the consumer of such tasks. Naturally, this affects their productivity and achievement.

DEPRESSION The constant 'high' and 'crash' of pleasure chemicals means that a person does not maintain a healthy balance. This imbalance could affect a personʼs mental health, and lead to or worsen a depressive state.

AND MASTURBATION PHYSIOLOGICAL PROBLEMS Watching pornography may cause physiological issues for a person, where they may find it difficult to enjoy the Ḥalāl intimacy allowed by Allāh between a husband and wife. This will affect the marriage and could lead to dissatisfaction for both partners.

LOW MOTIVATION Motivation is driven in part by certain chemicals such as dopamine, and the effect of pornography on those chemicals may result in a person losing motivation to do tasks they must do.

CHANGES IN ATTITUDES TO THE OTHER SEX Pornography, as opposed to Ḥalāl intimacy, ultimately objectifies the subject being viewed for gratification. Prolonged exposure could mean that a personʼs views on their opposite sex changes to see them only as objects for sexual gratification, rather than people.

INVASIVE THOUGHTS Prolonged exposure to pornography makes the mind 'dirty', where everything and everyone is sexualised, and oneʼs mind is constantly dominated by such immoral thoughts.

AIDING AN EXPLOITATIVE INDUSTRY Consumption of pornography aids in its continued production. This means aiding exploitation, immoral practices and people.
