STEPS TO RECOVERY ISTIGHFĀR Ask Allāh  for forgiveness, even if you feel you do not deserve it, or you feel insincere. Allāh  forgives sins, and He loves that His servant feels repentant over disobedience. Another benefit of Istighfār is that it prevents normalising the sin, and it prevents closing the door of Allāh ʼs mercy.

PERFORM GOOD DEEDS ﷺRasūlullāh said, Follow every bad deed with a good deed that erases it. TIRMIDHĪ Sin can make it more difficult to commit good deeds but persevere with doing so. Not only will it erase the bad deeds, but the habit of good deeds can eventually overcome the habit of bad.

IDENTIFY YOUR WEAK POINTS Are you more likely to view explicit content when you are stressed? Or whilst in bed? Do you view it more on a particular social media site? If so, you may need to take active steps to identify, and then put a plan in place to tackle those weak points. This may include leaving your phone in a different room at night, only going to bed when you are tired, or having blockers on your phone.

FIND A ḤALĀL ALTERNATIVE If you are of marriageable age, try to get married. While marriage does not mean a person will completely stop the sin of viewing Ḥarām, it does provide an alternative for the urges. If one cannot marry, then one should fast regularly, eat healthy and nutritious foods, and commit to a demanding exercise regime.

SET A GOOD PENALTY Make a promise to Allāh that each time you slip up, you will perform a good action such as a number of Nafl Rakʻāt in prayer, or by giving a small amount in charity.

Write a letter to a teenager, who has fallen prey to the evil habits of pornography and masturbation, explaining the harms and steps to recovery.

Social Media

the will cover importance of In the beautiful chapter of Sūrah ar-Raḥmān, Allāh safeguarding enumerates the favours He has bestowed upon humanity oneʼs speech, and Jinn. From mentioning the bounty of our existence, the fruits we eat and the conveyance we board, to the and its relation Ghībah: backbitinggreatest reward of Jannah, Allāh describes in vivid to speech, and detail the many things He has gifted us. Of the things Allāh Namīmah: tale- recounts, He begins with the blessing of the Qurʼān, etiquette to bearingour existence and then the power of speech. Allāh maintain on social says, media.And He has taught him Ghaflah:

(mankind) articulate speech.heedlessness

QURʼĀN 55:4

ʻAwrah: the intimate Allāh highlights the gift that is our ability to communicate and express ourselves, and to parts of a human use our tongue and speech for the correct reasons. body, which for men refers to the area ﷺRasūlullāh is reported to have said, from the navel to the Whoever guarantees for me ūthat they will safeguard that bottom of the knees, and for women the which is between the jaws and that which is between the entire body besides thighs, I will guarantee for that person Jannah. the face, hands and BUKHĀRĪ feet Safeguarding our tongue and speech, online or in-person, is critically important in Islām, Ḥasad: envy as some of the worst of sins are committed through them. Ghībah (backbiting), lies, insults, swears and false promises are sins of speech. Conversely, there is no limit to the good we Echo Chamber: a can do with our power of speech: enjoining good, remembering Allāh , speaking good, place where one spreading Salām, and so many other beneficial acts may be committed by using our ability only comes across to communicate. things they already agree with and think, usually ignoring other ideas

COUNT YOUR WORDS ﷺThe Messenger of Allāh said, ʻI have been sent with Jawāmi al-Kalim (comprehensive expressions), and I was made victorious with awe (cast in the hearts of others).

BUKHĀRĪ

ﷺRasūlullāh ʼs Sunnah was to speak less, but to ensure that the words used are weighty. Speaking less and choosing when and what to say also ensures we maintain integrity for ourselves, and a sense of 'awe' in the eyes of others. Following the Sunnah and giving value to oneʼs words by reducing the supply is a good way to be heard and listened to. Another Ḥadīth illustrates this ﷺperfectly, where Rasūlullāh says, Whoever believes in Allāh and the Last Day, let him speak good, or remain silent.

MUSLIM

ONLINE The internet and social media are undoubtedly some of the most impactful inventions of humanity. It has allowed for connections between people who might have never met, and for friends and family to communicate though they may be many miles apart. The internet is inseparably embedded in our lives today, and it is difficult to live without it. For this reason, approaching our use of the internet and social media with an Islamic perspective is critical if we are to continue using it, to stay away from what is impermissible and harmful, and to make our usage of the internet beneficial and rewarding for ourselves and others. The average person spends 143 minutes per day on social media.

That’s 870 hours or 36 days in a year, totalling an entire year spent on social media every decade!

The Sharʻī laws which apply to speech are the same which apply to our speech online. Before we post and comment, it is vitally important that we think through what we are to post. Consider the following questions before doing so: Is what you are posting Islamically valid?

1 d · It goes without saying that one may be sinful for posting what is Ḥarām such as pictures showing the ʻAwrah, women, or videos with music. Likewise, backbiting, exposing othersʼ sins, and anything unlawful in normal interactions is impermissible, whether it is in private chats or on open posts and status updates.

LikeComment Is it beneficial?

2 d · Just because something is permissible, or even true, it does not mean it is beneficial. Our social media feeds and online presence should be a net benefit to others, and Ghaflahvetting all that we post and say to filter out what is unnecessary or leading to is essential.

LikeComment Does it harm anyone?

3 d · Sharing, posting, or commenting anything which may harm someone is Ḥarām. Beyond the Islamic perspective as well, there are often real-life consequences for offences committed online, and we should not be led to believe that we are protected from consequences when we are online.

LikeComment Is it necessary?

4 d · A Muslim speaks when it is necessary to do so, because they are aware that their every word is to be examined on the Day of Qiyāmah. This principle applies to the online sphere as well. Posting and commenting only when it is necessary saves us time, effort, as well as reduces the possibility of us doing something wrong.

LikeComment

Is it true?

5 d · The internet and social media have allowed for information to spread fast, and in wanting to keep up, or to fulfil the urge to forward the latest developments of something of interest, we often forget to critically analyse the accuracy and truthfulness of what we are sending. Quite simply, it is Ḥarām for a believer to spread what they hear without verification.

LikeComment Why are you posting?

6 d · Intention is the keystone of every action, as the famous Ḥadīth states, Actions are judged by intentions.

BUKHĀRĪ

When we are posting or commenting good – and this applies especially online as our intention may easily be corrupted by a desire for recognition, praise or fame, we should always check our intention. If ever our intention is not solely for the pleasure of Allāh  and the good of others, we should restrain ourselves from posting.

LikeComment Ḥadīth 1 w · ﷺSo he ūthe Prophet ] grabbed his tongue and said “Restrain this.” I said:

“O Prophet of Allāh! Will we be taken to account for what we say?” ﷺHe said:

ʻ“May your mother grieve your loss, O Muadh! The reaping of the tongues will toss people into the fire on their faces!”

TIRMIDHĪ

LikeComment

ETIQUETTE Be very careful about keeping your eyes and heart pure. The internet is an easy place to view Ḥarām, and we should remember that Ḥarām is not just explicit content, but according to Islām it entails the uncovering of the ʻAwrah, or the viewing of others with Shahwah (desire). Never view Ḥarām, and if it pops up on your feed, use every tool to block it from returning. As much as we are not allowed to view the ʻAwrah, we cannot post it either. Remember to check pictures before posting, and ensure that nothing on such pictures, videos or similar media contain anything which we are not allowed to show others.

Posting personal pictures for all to see may lead to envy within the hearts of others and the evil eye. It is not advisable to post food, places one visits, or every occasion for everyone to see. This is a common habit, but inappropriate for a believer.

Remember that just as you only post the best pictures and the best moments of your life, so do others. The social media feed or profile of another is unlikely to be a realistic snapshot of their life, and it shows nothing of their struggles.

Expressing gratitude to Allāh for what you have, and being happy for others and praying Allāh blesses them further brings contentment in your life, and saves you from Ḥasadthe disease of .

ﷺRasūlullāh said, Two of three people should not speak privately, excluding the third.

BUKHĀRĪ

This Ḥadīth, in the social media context, can be applied such that in the presence of another, we should not browse our phones, but rather engage in conversation with the person sitting alongside. It is against social etiquette, and deeply frowned upon the world over, that a person may ignore others in their company by using their phone. Our online presence should not be our only presence. As Muslims, we have an obligation to disconnect from the world to spend time talking to our Lord. This should be a time of welcomed peace and serenity. Similarly, we are encouraged to spend time with our families, communities, friends and in the Masjid. This will undoubtedly affect our spiritual, physical, and mental health positively.

Correcting people online or in group chats, 'trolling' others, or pointing out their mistakes or possible hypocrisy is unlikely to have a positive impact or result in change. Rather, our religion teaches us to offer Naṣīḥah (sincere advice) with wisdom and kindness, and doing so will allow the person to see oneʼs sincerity, and will offer a far greater chance of success in rectifying the possible error.

ETIQUETTE impression of moral superiority. Islām values intention, and the only intention that is rewarded is that which is for the sake of Allāh . Posting, sharing, commenting and supporting a cause because others are doing so, or to portray oneself as compassionate does not bring reward.

Assume nothing ever gets deleted from the internet, so be very careful about what you say and share. A sin posted online may be a sin forever. Personal information, addresses, personal pictures and similar data should never be shared. A personʼs life prospects may be affected negatively by what they posted years before.

Social media algorithms promote content based on a personʼs likes and dislikes to keep them engaged. This not only creates a harmful addiction, but also echo chambers where we only view that which we agree with. It is crucial we seek out diverse perspectives from reliable online and in-person sources. Who do you follow? Your social media following paints a picture of who you are, and what you value. Remember to curate your feed so it reflects your Muslim identity, and keep Ḥarām and unwanted influences away. Make sure to weed out anything impermissible as soon as possible, and clean your social media so it increases rather than diminishes you spiritually.

If everyone and everything on your feed is very similar or offer similar echo chamberopinions, you are probably in an .

ﷺRasūlullāh said, If you have no shame, then do as you wish.

IBN MĀJAH

As Muslims we value Ḥayāʼ (modesty), and this extends to online interactions. Modesty then would be to ensure we do not comment, message, post or share anything immoral, vulgar, or explicit.

Remember to follow the law. The internet is not out of the jurisdiction of the law, and it is easy to fall prey to the idea that the internet offers anonymity. What you say, comment, post, promise, threaten or abuse may one day be used as evidence against you. quick message of encouragement, ask how someone is with a few taps, and brighten someoneʼs day with a few words. As with most things, our intention and how we use the internet determines whether we are to be rewarded or punished for it. Undoubtedly, we will all be asked on the Day of Qiyāmah about our use of modern technology, and we should bear that fact in mind whenever we pick up our devices.

COMMON PITFALLS GOSSIP ﷺNobody likes someone who gossips or spreads tales without verification. Rasūlullāh said, It is sufficient to render a person a liar ūon the basis that they spread all that they hear.

MUSLIM

Similarly, even if something is true, if spreading it is likely to cause harm and strife, such ﷺNamīmahgossip may be considered (tale-bearing), and it is impermissible. Rasūlullāh said, The tale-bearer will not enter Jannah.

MUSLIM

BACKBITING Ghībah or backbiting is to say something true about your fellow Muslim to another which they would not like. Highlighting the abhorrent nature of Ghībah, Allāh likens it to the eating of the dead flesh of oneʼs fellow Muslim. Backbiting is a deadly disease and can become a habit, and we should be wary of it taking control of our tongues.

SWEARING Swearing, vulgarity and foul language often have more to say about the one giving, than the one receiving. A person disgraces themselves with the frequent usage of foul language, and it highlights their inability to use better speech. In the long term, there is no temporary social reputation to be gained through swearing that is worth oneʼs honour and dignity. We should refrain from swearing as it is a sinful act.

LYING ﷺRasūlullāh said, Lying leads to immorality, and immorality leads to the Fire. And a man may keep on telling lies till he is written before Allāh as a liar.

BUKHĀRĪ

Lying is frowned upon by all people and time, and it is seen as a wicked deed. Honesty on the other hand is considered an admirable trait, even when that honesty may be detrimental to oneself. To develop this, building a habit of honesty is essential. Lying should make us feel bad inside, and we should feel a sense of dignity and gratitude to Allāh when we speak the truth, even if doing so may have been bitter.

EXAGGERATION We are prone to exaggerate our accomplishments, actions or the events which may have occurred in our presence to a certain degree. Doing so regularly however will lead to others seeing us with a habit to exaggerate and will make them disinterested in what we have to say. Exaggeration is a form of lying and decreases our respect in the eyes of others, and devalues our contributions, and so we should be mindful of how we express ourselves.

EXCESSIVE SPEECH Every word of every person shall be weighed on the day of Qiyāmah, and all shall be taken to account for what they said. Allāh alludes to this in the Qurʼān saying, Not a single word is uttered by one, but there is a watcher near him, ready (to record).

QURʼĀN 50:18

The best way to ensure we are less likely to be taken to account and punished for something said is to simply speak less. Doing so will safeguard our tongues and ourselves in this world, and more importantly, in the hereafter.

COMMON PITFALLS ARGUING ﷺRasūlullāh said, I guarantee a house in the suburbs of Jannah for the one who avoids quarrelling even if they were in the right.

ABŪ DĀWŪD

This great reward is awaiting us every time we are in a potential argument, and we only need to walk away to receive it! Few arguments are worth the effort and time to argue them, and often, the disputes are left unresolved even after.

BREAKING PROMISES A Muslim is one who keeps their word, and who can be trusted to fulfil their promise. Allāh mentions about the believers in the Qurʼān that: They are those who are true to their trusts and promises.

QURʼĀN 23:8

Losing the trust of people due to the non-fulfilment of promises or false promises is damaging not only to our reputation and career opportunities in this world, but more importantly to our chances in gaining the highest stages of Jannah.

EXCESSIVE JOKING Having fun and occasionally sharing a joke or something funny is permissible, and even the ﷺMessenger engaged in light-hearted fun. However, having a disposition of constantly joking, or making light every situation is unbefitting for a believer, and we should try to maintain a mature personality which understands each circumstance and the behaviour appropriate for it. One should avoid lying in all jokes.

UNREALISTIC EXPECTATIONS One of the major issues with social media is how it portrays only the good of people’s lives, and so it sets unrealistic standards for others to live up to. Moreover, since only those people become popular who can display the most wealth, beauty, possessions and fascinating experiences, this creates a false sense of what is normal.

Due to this, one may fall into the trap of comparing themselves to such people, and upon falling short of their apparently amazing lives, feel unaccomplished and inferior. This can lead to negative emotions, pain, and potential issues with mental health. For this reason, we should avoid such media, thank Allāh for what we have, and remind ourselves that social media in no way a representation of reality or normal life.

BODY IMAGE ISSUES One of the worst aspects of social media is how it makes many users conscious of their body image. Due to a certain standard being shown across media, users may be led to feel that they should look a certain way, and that not being in such a shape, colour or form is unnatural or undesirable. This leads to dissatisfaction in the way Allāh has created us, and a person can fall down a spiral of trying to achieve a certain look at great expense, and whilst harming themselves emotionally and physically.

ﷺIt is very important that we remember the words of our Messenger here:

Verily Allāh does not look to your faces and your wealth, but He looks to your heart and to your deeds.

MUSLIM

Look to one who is lower (has less) than you, and do not look at one who is above (has more than) you. For indeed that is more worthy ūthat you do not belittle Allāh's favours upon you."

TIRMIDHĪ

Follow REPLACE THE BAD WITH GOOD! A KIND WORD Our religion values the smallest of actions, and even a small compliment, a word of encouragement or the most seemingly insignificant utterance of kindness is great ﷺin the court of Allāh . Our Messenger said, And the compassionate word is charity.

BUKHĀRĪ

Sometimes it takes the tiniest of effort on our part to merely say something nice to another, yet our words can have a huge positive impact on their day, or even their life. A GOOD LIE Lying is impermissible, but in certain conditions, it may be good and even rewardable to speak something untrue. Lying to mend relations between two Muslims, or to not hurt someoneʼs feelings where a lie would not be harmful to them are two such occasions. Similarly, covering the faults of others is an act of great reward that promises our faults being kept hidden on the day of Qiyāmah.

ĀDĀB IN SPEECH Speaking in a manner which reflects good character and comportment is an essential part of being Muslim. Every word of ours should be weighed for our audience accordingly, and should be intentional. The tone we use should likewise reflect the subject and audience, as often it is the tone rather than what is said that determines the reaction of the one with whom we are speaking.

WORSHIP Our tongues should be moist with the remembrance of Allāh .

ﷺRasūlullāh said, The son of Ādamʼs speech is against him, not in his favour, except for commanding good, or forbidding evil, or the remembrance of Allāh.

TIRMIDHĪ

We will not be questioned on the good deeds we do sincerely, so our every utterance should be in using our tongue for its intended purpose.

REMEMBER THAT SPEECH SHOULD BE APT Make a poster comparing the Do’s and Don’ts of social media etiquette.

APPROPRIATE IT SHOULD TAKE INTO CONSIDERATION THE:+ AUDIENCEPURPOSETONE The ability to speak which we as humans have been gifted with can be the source of a personʼs greatest successes or their deepest failures. Words can express ideas, inspire action, and encourage change. They can also disgrace completely, insult, and stir into action the most terrible deeds. The ability to express oneself confidently and clearly, and to be fully aware of every word that is uttered is then one of the greatest talents and gifts that Allāh may bestow upon someone.

Similarly, it is an effort which deserves our full attention and devotion: that we ensure that no evil comes into this world as a result of something we have said, and that an innumerable amount of good is left behind us due to our speech. IF THERE IS NOTHING GOOD TO SAY, ITʼS GOOD TO SAY NOTHING.

Discrimination

the will cover prohibition of Discrimination is the unjust treatment of another due to a perceived superiority of one over another. While our religion allows treatment of certain categories of people to be in Islām, the differentiated accordingly for their benefit, for one to consider themselves better than link between another on the basis of colour, gender, race, nationality or ability is a grave sin, and deeply discrimination frowned upon in Islām. and pride, and The Qurʼān and Sunnah contain many verses and different types of Aḥādīth condemning any pride or arrogance over a discrimination. personʼs race, sex, ability, wealth or status. As Muslims, we value Taqwā as the deciding factor in a personʼs ultimate value, and Allāh says Himself, Discrimination: the unjust treatment Indeed, the noblest amongst you is the one who is of another from a most God-fearing. perceived superiority

QURʼĀN 49:13

Pride: feeling of satisfaction and pleasure over oneʼs qualities, characteristics, or achievements Tafsīr: explanation of the Qurʼān ﷺOur past, from the time of the Prophet to the prophets of old has shown that it rarely is societal status or wealth, nor ethnicity, colour or gender which determines ultimate success, but rather the humility to submit before Allāh . Such humility is rarely found in one declaring their superiority over another.

ﷺIn his address at his parting Ḥajj, Rasūlullāh famously said, O people, your Lord is one and your father (Ādam) is one. There is no superiority of an Arab over a foreigner, nor a foreigner over an Arab, and neither white skin over black skin, nor black skin over white skin, except by righteousness. People are from Ādam, and Ādam was from dust.

ṬAḤĀWĪ

ﷺعليه السلامHere, the Prophet begins by stating how we all come from one creation of Allāh ; Ādam . This we believe to be

undoubtedly true, and related to that belief is the idea that we are all one and the same. The differences Allāh has placed within us of colour, nationality and ethnicity is one of His signs, as He says, Among His wonders is the creation of the Heavens and the Earth, and the diversity of your tongues and colours.

QURʼĀN 30:22

Elsewhere, Allāh mentions, We have made you into nations and tribes, so that you might come to know one another.

QURʼĀN 49:13

The differences between us, as Allāh says, should lead to greater understanding of each other and an appreciation of Allāh as al-Khāliq (the Creator)

and al-Muṣawwir (the Designer). Allāh created us differently to overcome those barriers of differences and work together in good. We see examples of this in our history, where Muslims despite differences in language and culture, and at times with histories of conflict, have bonded over their submission to one Creator. AND PRIDE Pride has no place in Islām, and thus should have no ﷺplace in a Muslimʼs heart. Rasūlullāh said, None shall enter Paradise who has in his heart the weight of a mustard seed of pride.

MUSLIM

dangerous. Pride is not only sinful itself, but it can blind a person from the wrongs they commit and injustices they inflict upon others. Someone who thinks they are better than others are unlikely to ask them for forgiveness also, as they will consider that demeaning.

In the Qurʼān, Allāh mentions the stories of many prophets, and the reasons why their people chose to disbelieve. A common theme across the stories of many prophets was the pride and arrogance of the disbelievers, where they saw themselves above either the Messenger sent to them, or the people who believed in him. The disbelievers would often discriminate on the basis of wealth, lineage, and intelligence, and would consider it beneath themselves to associate with such people. Thus, they condemned themselves to eternal punishment.

TYPES OF DISCRIMINATION Discrimination can be of many types, and every facet is wrong. Allāh will not judge us on our outwardly appearances, ﷺour gender, or where we hail from. Rasūlullāh himself said, Verily Allāh does not look at your faces and your wealth; rather He looks to your heart and to your deeds.

MUSLIM

Since we cannot see intentions and the meaningful actions of others, we have no reason to think we are superior to another.

Materialism

materialism and its consequences, the Islamic perspective on materialism, and the concept of Qanāʻah. The world around us today is consumerismone filled with and a focus on the material aspect of life and existence. We are surrounded by materialism, and materialistic lives are glorified, celebrated, and shared. We are taught that happiness lies in the accumulation of things, and the pursuit of more Materialism: a things. Materialism is a stain upon the heart which blinds a person from their ultimate belief that material objective, and leaves a person chasing to satisfy what will ultimately never be satisfied. possessions are more important than spirituality Materialism in a person is seen as an obsession in things. A fixation on certain products and possessions, pride in owning them, and a desire to display that ownership to Materialistic: others are all signs of materialism. Materialism leads to the creation of a fake self- excessively image, where one portrays themselves in a manner not reflecting their true reality. concerned with material posessions For one who believes this life is the entirety of existence, then maximising pleasure, Consumerism:accumulating wealth and possessions, and devoting attention only to this life may the be a suitable objective. However, for us as Muslims who know of a hereafter, and of a idea that increasing greater and far lengthier existence to come, it is wrong for us to focus so much on a consumption of temporary residence like this world. We are encouraged to seek balance in our lives, material goods between sustaining ourselves in this world, and preparing well is economically for the Ākhirah.desirable ﷺThe Prophet of Allāh said, Qanāʻah: contentment of the Richness does not lie heart in the abundance of (worldly) goods but richness is the richness of the soul.

MUSLIM

Countless examples, present today and recorded from days past have shown the reality that riches and materialistic obsession does not bring happiness, nor offer refuge from the tribulations of our unpredictable lives. Attempting to satisfy the desire for the riches of this world and making them oneʼs primary focus not only excludes one from the riches of the hereafter, but grants nothing but a lack of contentment and a troubled heart.

ﷺRasūlullāh said, If the son of Ādam were to possess two valleys of riches, he would wish for the third one. And the stomach of the son of Ādam is not filled but with dust.

MUSLIM

It is human nature to desire more than one has, and one may feel that they will truly be happy after attaining a certain amount of possessions or wealth. However, this Ḥadīth shows, and Islām seeks to teach us that such hopes are deceptive, and the yearning for more within us will never be fulfilled. WHERE MIGHT A PERSON BE MATERIALISTIC?

Surely, the wasteful are brothers Materialism often makes people spend extravagant sums of money which is wasteful. We have been warned against of Shayṭān, and Shayṭān is very extravagance and waste, and Allāh says, ungrateful to his Lord.

QUR’ĀN 17:27 The following are some examples in which many people are materialistic.

TRAVEL & CLOTHESFOODTECHNOLOGYHOMESCARSWEDDINGS HOLIDAYS ENVIRONMENTAL AWARENESS Another aspect of wastefulness which comes from materialism is how it affects the world around us. Allāh has placed humans on Earth as stewards, which means we are responsible for it. This includes the animals which Allāh has created, and the natural world Allāh has provided for us. We have a responsibility to look after the Earth and protect it from human greed and overconsumption.

Throughout the Qur’ān, Allāh has made reference to how human action has a damaging impact to the natural world.

Primarily, this comes through sin, and the more humanity sins, the more the world around us suffers. Allāh says, Calamities have appeared on land and sea because of what the hands of the people have earned (man’s deeds).

QUR’ĀN 30:41 However, the world is also affected by our actions directly, whether that be pollution that poisons the earth and oceans, plastic that litters and ruins the beauty of the Earth, or trash which causes immense suffering, pain and ultimately death to millions of innocent animals. Our actions, when viewed collectively as millions and billions of people, can have enormous consequences. For this reason, we should not think of our actions as little or insignificant, but rather act responsibly trying to preserve the beauty of Allāh ’s creation.

There is no Muslim who plants Even if the Day of Resurrection a tree or sows seeds, and then were established upon one of a bird, or a person or an animal you while they have in their eats from it, but it is regarded as hand a sapling, they should an act of charity for them.plant it.

AḤMADBUKHĀRĪ

STRENGTHEN YOUR CONNECTION WITH ALLĀH  The foundation of protecting oneself from materialism in Islām is to strengthen oneʼs faith and maintain a deep connection with Allāh . When oneʼs objective is the pleasure of Allāh , nothing else matters, and material possessions become mere tools to achieving the primary objective.

PRACTISE GRATITUDE of not having enough, and to counteract this belief, one should practise gratitude to Allāh as much as possible. By actively reminding oneself of Allāh ʼs countless favours, and reciting HOW TO 'Alḥamdulillāh' regularly, one PROTECT can protect themselves from materialistic thoughts and ONESELF impulses.

FROM GIVE CHARITY Giving charity regularly removes the love of the world and wealth from oneʼs heart. Allāh  says about righteousness, ūIt is to give wealth despite love for it.

QURʼĀN 2:177

Mankind naturally has a tendency for wealth and material possessions, and giving charity effectively forces out the natural love we have for such things.

REMEMBER DEATH Rasūlullāh ﷺ said, Remember often the destroyer of desires (death).

NASĀʼĪ

Death will come to one and all, and with it, all material wealth ceases to benefit. Constantly reflecting on death and the mortality of life reminds a person of their ultimate goal: the hereafter.

Islām values Qanāʻah, meaning contentment of the heart. This path teaches that being grateful with whatever one has, regardless of how little, may lead to far greater happiness and fulfilment than being wealthy but constantly being in the pursuit of more. Additionally, gratitude and contentment with what Allāh has given a person may lead to receiving further, as Allāh has promised an increase for the person who is truly grateful.

Qanāʻah should be a part of every believer. Allāh says, And those who are saved from the greed of their hearts are the successful.

QURʼĀN 64:16

In a world and in environments where we are constantly shown adverts of materialism and pushed towards lifestyles reflecting it, it is our responsibility to take forward the far healthier and beneficial position of Islām which promotes contentment and living simple, non-superficial lives. Our lives should reflect our belief in the life to come, and our every action should be one to ultimately please Allāh , our beloved Lord, to whom one day we will most certainly return.

“The upper hand is better than the lower hand. One should begin his charity by spending on his dependents. And the best charity is that which is given by (and from the surplus of) a wealthy person. And whoever abstains (from asking others for financial help), Allāh will make them so (independent), and whoever seeks (financial) independence, Allāh will make him self- sufficient.”

BUKHĀRĪ
